  - [x] M.0.9 — Write `src/quicksight_gen/l2_spike/cli.py` + `__main__.py` — Click commands `apply schema|data|dashboards` + `generate training`. Real CLI (not function stubs); all four commands run end-to-end producing the right artifacts under a fixture cwd.
  - [x] M.0.10 — End-to-end pipeline run against real Postgres + real QuickSight (account 470656905821 / us-east-2). All four CLI commands executed via `--config run/config.yaml`: schema applied, drift seed planted (verified $50 drift via direct SQL), all 5 QuickSight resources deployed (DataSource + Theme + Dataset + Analysis + Dashboard, all `spk-` prefixed), embed URL fetched + Playwright captured a screenshot at `training/spk/drift-sheet.png`, handbook rendered with the substituted account name and resolves to that image. **Lesson captured (F12):** screenshot showed QS's generic "We can't open that dashboard" error because the backing Aurora Serverless Postgres was asleep — DB cold-start is the actual root cause when QS surfaces that error, not permissions / scope. v5.0.2 e2e suite already has a DB warm-up phase; M.7/M.8 must adopt the same pattern.
  - [x] M.0.11 — Write `tests/spike/test_slice.py` — smoke tests: load `slice.yaml`, walk the schema/seed/dashboard/handbook artifacts, assert load-bearing shape; persona substitution check ensures no Sasquatch leakage. 2 tests passing. Full unit suite still green (721 passed).
  - [x] M.0.12 — Findings consolidated in `tests/spike/_l2_spike_findings.md` (12 findings F1-F12). Top-of-file summary buckets them by trigger: SPEC amendment (F5), M.1 library design (F1-F6), refactor touches (F7-F8), confirmations of reusable infra (F9-F11), operational lesson for M.7/M.8 (F12 — DB warm-up).
  - [x] M.0.13 — **Iteration gate.** SPEC amendment landed (F5: InstancePrefix regex `^[a-z][a-z0-9_]*$` + 30-char cap pinned). M.1 substeps below absorb F1-F8 inline; M.7/M.8 absorb F12 (DB warm-up before screenshot). M.0 closed.

- [ ] **M.1 — L2 library foundation.** Lift the spike's working glue into proper library modules. Typed YAML loader matching SPEC; all SPEC validation rules with rejection tests; prefix-aware SQL emission; Current* projection. Acceptance: `from quicksight_gen.l2 import load_instance, validate, ...` works; spike's `slice.yaml` loads through it cleanly; pyright strict on `common/l2/`.
  - [x] M.1.1 — Typed dataclasses landed under `src/quicksight_gen/common/l2/primitives.py` with all SPEC primitives + value types (Account / AccountTemplate / TwoLegRail / SingleLegRail / TransferTemplate / ChainEntry / LimitSchedule / L2Instance) plus enums (Scope / LegDirection) and SPEC-vocabulary type aliases (Origin / TransferType / CompletionExpression / CadenceExpression). Per F2: `Rail = TwoLegRail | SingleLegRail` as a TypeAlias — match-dispatch works without isinstance ladders; aggregating flags live on both shapes per SPEC. All dataclasses `frozen=True, slots=True`. F6 (Dataset rename) deferred to M.1.4 where api `DataSet` usage actually lands. 4 structural regression tests in `tests/test_l2_primitives.py`; full unit suite green at 725 passing.
  - [x] M.1.2 — Loader landed under `src/quicksight_gen/common/l2/loader.py`. `load_instance(path)` reads YAML, dispatches per primitive type, validates per-entity shape, and returns a fully-typed `L2Instance`. Friendly errors cite a logical path (e.g. `accounts[2].id`) + the source file; YAML syntax errors carry PyYAML's native file/line. F4 lands as `_load_money(raw, *, path)` using `Decimal(str(raw))` — preserves '0.1' rather than coercing through float precision. F5 lands as `_load_instance_prefix(raw, *, path)` enforcing `^[a-z][a-z0-9_]*$` + 30-char cap; per the F5 finding, the strict regex applies to InstancePrefix only — other identifiers use a loose non-empty-string check (SPEC's worked examples mix PascalCase Roles + snake_case TransferTypes). Rail discrimination by field-presence (source/destination → TwoLeg; leg_role/leg_direction → SingleLeg; both/neither → reject). RoleExpression normalized to tuple uniformly (single string → 1-tuple). 19 tests in `tests/test_l2_loader.py` covering happy paths (slice.yaml + inline kitchen-sink) + every per-helper rejection. Full unit suite green at 744 passing.
  - [x] M.1.3 — Validator landed under `src/quicksight_gen/common/l2/validate.py`. `validate(instance)` runs 16 cross-entity rules in deterministic order, fail-fast with `L2ValidationError` on the first violation. Rules grouped: U1-U4 (uniqueness on Account.id / AccountTemplate.role / Rail.name / TransferTemplate.name); R1-R6 (reference resolution: rail-touched roles, Account/AccountTemplate.parent_role with template-under-template forbidden per F1, RailNames in TransferTemplate.leg_rails, Chain endpoints, LimitSchedule.parent_role); C1-C2 (≤1 Variable leg per template, XorGroup parent consistency); S1-S6 (the F3 cross-entity ExpectedNet split: standalone two-leg requires expected_net but template-leg forbids it; single-leg reconciliation by Template OR AggregatingRail; aggregating-not-as-Chain.child; aggregating requires cadence + bundles_activity; non-aggregating must NOT carry them); V1-V2 (CompletionExpression + CadenceExpression vocabulary literals per SPEC v1 tables, with bounds checks like monthly-day in 1..31). 50 tests in `tests/test_l2_validate.py` — one rejection per rule plus parametrized vocabulary acceptance/rejection sweeps. Baseline `_baseline_instance()` fixture exercises every primitive shape (and itself passes `validate()`); each test mutates one field via `dataclasses.replace` to trigger one rule. Full unit suite green at 794 passing (was 744; +50).
  - [x] M.1.4 — Schema emitter landed under `src/quicksight_gen/common/l2/schema.py`. `emit_schema(instance)` produces idempotent (drop-then-create) DDL for `<prefix>transactions` + `<prefix>daily_balances` matching the v6 L1 entity shape: `entry BIGSERIAL` per F's Entry primitive; `amount_money` + `amount_direction` split per the L1 Amount invariant (with a Postgres CHECK enforcing sign-direction agreement); `transfer_parent_id` per L1 Transfer.Parent; `expected_eod_balance` + `limits TEXT` (JSON map) on daily_balances. Account fields denormalized onto every row per Implementation Entities (`account_id` / `account_name` / `account_role` / `account_scope` / `account_parent_role`). `Status`, `TransferType`, and `Origin` are open enums with no CHECK so integrators can extend. `metadata TEXT + IS JSON` per the portability constraint; B-tree indexes only (no GIN). DDL verified against real Postgres via psycopg2 — sign-direction CHECK actually rejects positive Debits. 28 unit tests in `tests/test_l2_schema.py` covering prefix isolation, idempotency ordering, every load-bearing column + constraint, denormalized account fields. F9-F11 (existing deploy infra reuse) more naturally lands in M.6 (CLI workflow) than here — M.1.4 is just CREATE TABLE DDL. F6 Dataset rename still deferred — naturally lands when the QS dataset emitter wraps `build_dataset()`. Full unit suite green at 822 passing (was 794; +28). L2 derived tables (account dim, limits dim) deliberately NOT emitted yet — the spike did fine without them; M.2 (porting AR CMS) will surface what's actually needed.
  - [x] M.1.5 — Current* views landed in the same `emit_schema()` script. `<prefix>current_transactions` materializes the L1 CurrentTransaction theorem as `WHERE entry = (SELECT MAX(entry) … WHERE id = tx.id)`; `<prefix>current_daily_balances` materializes CurrentStoredBalance keyed on `(account_id, business_day_start)`. Views drop before tables (Postgres dependency); CREATE after tables. Verified against real Postgres: inserting two rows for the same logical key with different entries produces both in the base table and only the higher-entry row in the view (drift correction works as designed). Combined into emit_schema() rather than a separate emit_views() — integrators get one "apply schema" script. 5 new tests in tests/test_l2_schema.py; full unit suite green at 827 passing (was 822; +5).
  - [x] M.1.6 — Per-primitive end-to-end pipeline tests landed in `tests/test_l2_pipeline.py`. 14 tests walk each SPEC worked-example shape through `load → validate → emit_schema` cleanly: singleton account, AccountTemplate, two-leg standalone Rail, single-leg in TransferTemplate, single-leg Variable-direction, two-leg aggregating, transfer template (parametrized over all 4 Completion vocabulary forms), Chain XOR group, Chain fan-out, LimitSchedule, plus the SPEC's full end-to-end merchant-acquirer example. Doubles as executable SPEC documentation — if a SPEC snippet stops parsing/validating, the named test fires.
  - [x] M.1.7 — Audit cross-reference added to `validate.py` docstring: rule numbering matches `tests/test_l2_validate.py` test names (U1 → `test_u1_*`, etc.). Locked rule documented inline: every new cross-entity validator MUST land its rejection test in the same commit; the rule list in the docstring extends to cover the new validator. The 16-rule list itself IS the audit table — one row per rule with the SPEC justification.
  - [x] M.1.8 — Kitchen-sink fixture landed under `tests/l2/_kitchen.yaml` (~150 lines). Exercises every primitive shape + every variant flag: both rail shapes; aggregating on both shapes; Variable-direction leg; union role; standalone vs template-leg two-leg (covers S1 + S2 sides); two TransferTemplates with different Completion forms; XOR + non-XOR chains; LimitSchedules across multiple roles. Two coverage tests confirm fixture loads cleanly + every primitive kind is reachable. **Surfaced a real SPEC ambiguity (F13):** S3's "single-leg rail must be reconciled" rule was contradicted by the SPEC's own "single-leg aggregating rails permitted (e.g. sweep that lands in external counterparty)" example. Resolved by exempting aggregating single-leg rails from S3 (they ARE the reconciliation mechanism); SPEC + validator + tests amended in this substep. Working as designed — the kitchen-sink fired exactly the kind of integration breakage per-layer tests miss.
  - [x] M.1.9 — `pyproject.toml` `tool.pyright.include` now lists `src/quicksight_gen/common/l2` alongside `common/tree`. Cleared 90 pyright errors → 0: `validate.py` function signatures take `set[Identifier]` instead of `set[str]` (NewType invariance bites at the call sites in `validate()`); `loader.py` centralizes `dict[str, object]` narrowing in two helpers (`_as_mapping` + `_as_list`) so each per-primitive `_load_*` works against precisely-typed mappings instead of the YAML `Any` cascade; dropped unused `_optional` + `T = TypeVar` + `Any` import. Existing `pytest_sessionstart` hook in `conftest.py` (L.1.20 era) auto-picks up the new include — no new test infra; the gate fires before any test on every `pytest` run, matching the `common/tree` gate. 123/123 L2 tests + 844/844 full unit suite green; pyright `0 errors, 1 warning` (the warning is `reportMissingModuleSource` for `yaml` — PyYAML ships no `.py` source the strict mode can index, benign).
  - [x] M.1.10 — Promoted `ScreenshotHarness` + `browser_helpers` from `tests/e2e/` to `src/quicksight_gen/common/browser/` (helpers.py + screenshot.py + __init__.py re-exports). New public surface: `from quicksight_gen.common.browser import ScreenshotHarness, generate_dashboard_embed_url, webkit_page`. Per F8: reshaped harness API to key on object refs — `capture_all_sheets()` now returns `dict[Sheet, Path]`; `capture_per_visual(sheet)` returns `dict[VisualLike, Path]`; `capture_with_state(...)` returns `dict[Sheet, Path]`. On-disk filenames stay `<sheet_id>.png` / `<visual_id>.png` so existing screenshots overwrite cleanly. Spike's `capture_drift_screenshot` rewired (`paths[drift_sheet]` instead of `paths["drift-sheet"]`); 22 e2e test files + 1 unit test + 3 ad-hoc scripts updated to import from the new location. `SCREENSHOT_DIR` resolves relative to cwd (overridable via `QS_E2E_SCREENSHOT_DIR`) so the e2e `screenshot()` helper still writes to `tests/e2e/screenshots/`. CLAUDE.md project-structure tree refreshed (new `common/browser/` block; `tests/e2e/{browser_helpers,screenshot_harness}.py` removed). Common/browser/ deliberately NOT in pyright strict gate yet — `helpers.py` loosely types Playwright Page as plain `page`; tightening queued for when M.6/M.7/M.8 surface real production needs. 844/844 unit tests green; pyright `0 errors`.

- [x] **M.1a — Bring L2 library into alignment with updated SPEC.** Catch-up substep between M.1 and M.2 — the SPEC accumulated changes during the L2-design pass that needed to land in the library before M.2 ports a real app on top. Alignment-only: load-time + data-shape only; runtime mechanics (bundler firing, posting-time PostedRequirements check, aging-watch dashboards, Variable-leg ordering enforcement at posting time) stay deferred to M.2+ where each gets a real caller.
  - [x] M.1a.1 — Schema v1.1 columns + bundler-eligibility index landed (`schema.py`): `rail_name VARCHAR(100) NOT NULL` + `template_name VARCHAR(100)` + `bundle_id VARCHAR(100)` + `supersedes VARCHAR(50)` on `<prefix>transactions`; `supersedes VARCHAR(50)` on `<prefix>daily_balances`; partial index `idx_<prefix>_transactions_bundler_eligibility ON (rail_name, status) WHERE bundle_id IS NULL`. Open enum on `supersedes` (no CHECK) per SPEC's open-enum rule. Spike's `emit_seed_sql` writes `'ExtInbound'` as `rail_name` per row (single-rail spike); `Current*` views auto-project new columns via `SELECT *`. 7 new tests in `test_l2_schema.py` (851/851 unit suite green).
  - [x] M.1a.2 — L2 primitives v1.1 landed (`primitives.py` + `loader.py`): added `Duration: TypeAlias = datetime.timedelta` + `SupersedeReason: TypeAlias = Literal["Inflight", "BundleAssignment", "TechnicalCorrection"]`. Made `Rail.origin` optional (`Origin | None`); added `posted_requirements: tuple[Identifier, ...]` + `max_pending_age: Duration | None` + `max_unbundled_age: Duration | None` to both `TwoLegRail` + `SingleLegRail`. `TwoLegRail` only: `source_origin: Origin | None` + `destination_origin: Origin | None` (type-level prevents per-leg overrides on `SingleLegRail`). Loader parses new fields including ISO 8601 Duration (`_load_duration` regex handles `PT24H` / `P1D` / `P1DT12H` / etc., rejects year/month/empty/negative/non-string); hard-rejects `source_origin`/`destination_origin` keys on single-leg rails per the M.1a design call. Kitchen-sink fixture exercises every new variant. 8 new primitive tests + 23 new loader tests (882/882 unit suite green).
  - [x] M.1a.3 — Validator catch-up landed (`validate.py`): added 5 new rules — **U5** LimitSchedule (parent_role, transfer_type) uniqueness; **R7** TransferTemplate.leg_rails entries reference non-Aggregating Rails; **R8** MaxUnbundledAge set only on Rails appearing in some AggregatingRail's bundles_activity (bare-identifier selectors match by RailName OR transfer_type); **R9** dotted BundleSelector (`Template.LegRail`) resolves both template + leg-rail (validator does dot-split locally per the bare-identifier-shape design); **O1** per-leg Origin resolution: 1-leg rails MUST set `origin`; 2-leg rails MUST cover both legs via `origin` alone OR both per-leg overrides OR one override + rail-level fallback. Module docstring's audit table updated to document U5/R7/R8/R9/O1; `validate()` wires all five new checks. 14 new rejection + acceptance tests; 64 validator tests total (was 50). Total validator surface: U1–U5, R1–R9, C1–C2, S1–S6, V1–V2, O1 (24 rules). 895/895 unit suite green.
  - [x] M.1a.4 — PostedRequirements computed view landed (`src/quicksight_gen/common/l2/derived.py`). `posted_requirements_for(instance, rail_name) -> tuple[Identifier, ...]` returns the deduped, lex-sorted union of (a) the Rail's own `posted_requirements`, (b) `TransferKey` fields for every TransferTemplate where the rail is in `leg_rails` (handles rails appearing in multiple templates), (c) `parent_transfer_id` (the module-level constant `PARENT_TRANSFER_ID`) when the rail is a Required:true Chain.child OR when a TransferTemplate containing the rail is. `_find_rail` raises `KeyError` on lookup miss. Public API exports `posted_requirements_for` + `PARENT_TRANSFER_ID`. 12 new tests in `test_l2_derived.py` covering each source path independently + combined union + dedup overlap + deterministic sort + lookup miss + chain-parent-not-inheriting. 907/907 unit suite green.
  - [x] M.1a.5 — Committed M.1a.1-4 as one cohesive "M.1a SPEC alignment" commit (`72a479a` on `phase-m-1-l2-library-foundation`). 907/907 unit suite + pyright gate green. Bundled SPEC.md catch-up edits + the planning artifact `M1a_guidance.md` with the implementation so the SPEC + library land in lockstep. (Guidance doc deleted in M.1a.6 — fully absorbed into PLAN + SPEC.)
  - [x] M.1a.6 — Description fields landed on every L2 primitive (`primitives.py` + `loader.py` + `SPEC.md`). Optional `description: str | None = None` on `Account`, `AccountTemplate`, `TwoLegRail`, `SingleLegRail`, `TransferTemplate`, `ChainEntry`, `LimitSchedule`, and top-level `L2Instance`. New `_load_description` helper rejects non-string + blank/whitespace-only values (configuration smell — omit the key instead). Multi-line markdown survives intact (loader does no pre-processing). SPEC.md gained a "Description fields" subsection at the top of `Primitives` documenting the Why (handbook + training render templates read these) and the SHOULD recommendation; each primitive's type signature in SPEC gained the trailing `Description?: Value` field. Kitchen-sink fixture exercises descriptions on top-level instance + Account + AccountTemplate + TwoLegRail + TransferTemplate + ChainEntry + LimitSchedule. M1a_guidance.md deleted (fully absorbed). 13 new tests in `tests/test_l2_descriptions.py`; 920/920 unit suite + pyright gate green.
  - [x] M.1a.7 — L1 invariant views landed in `emit_schema` (`schema.py`). 7 prefixed views per L2 instance materializing the SPEC's L1 SHOULD-constraints as queryable exception surfaces: 2 helper views (`<prefix>_computed_subledger_balance`, `<prefix>_computed_ledger_balance`) + 5 invariant views (`<prefix>_drift`, `<prefix>_ledger_drift`, `<prefix>_overdraft`, `<prefix>_expected_eod_balance_breach`, `<prefix>_limit_breach`). Each invariant view returns ONLY the violation rows. All read from Current* views so technical-error supersession is transparent. Limit-breach caps embedded inline at view-emit time as CASE branches from `instance.limit_schedules` (dynamic JSON path lookup isn't portable across SQL targets); empty `limit_schedules` produces a syntactically valid but inert view. New `_emit_l1_invariant_views(instance)` + `_render_limit_breach_cases(instance, *, p)` helpers. Skipped (deferred to first-consumer): Conservation (transfer-level), Timeliness (transaction-level), Parent-balance-existence (presence check, not value). One existing test fixed (`test_daily_balances_money_is_signed` regex was over-broad — the new `<prefix>_overdraft` view legitimately filters `money < 0`; tightened to look for CHECK on `money` inside the daily_balances CREATE TABLE block specifically). 23 new tests in `test_l2_schema.py` covering each view's DDL shape + filter semantics + parametrized smoke for view existence/drop-create-order across all 7 view names; verified the limit-breach inline CASE branches against a custom L2 fixture. 994/994 unit suite + pyright strict gate green.

- [x] **M.2 — Port AR CMS as first L2 instance feeding the generic L1 dashboard.** **Closed at M.2.10's iteration gate; M.2a takes over.** What shipped: L2 library proven end-to-end against real Aurora (M.2.6 PASS — schema deploys, seed plants, all 3 L1 invariant view scenarios surface). What deferred (subsumed by M.2a): wholesale dataset rewrite under the v5-idiom translation layer (M.2.4c/d), faithful-port handbook page (M.2.5 → M.2a.7), seed hash-lock (M.2.7 → M.2a.8), no-regression run (M.2.8 — M.2a is parallel-stack, both pass independently). The faithful-port framing got us through enough of the port that the architecture is validated — the L1 invariant views are the right abstraction; M.2a builds on a known-good foundation.
  - [x] M.2.1 — `tests/l2/sasquatch_ar.yaml` landed, exercising every L2 primitive shape the kitchen-sink covers (in different patterns, for variety in regression coverage). 13 singleton accounts (8 internal GL + 5 external sharing role `ExternalCounterparty`); 2 AccountTemplates (`CustomerDDA`/`ZBASubAccount` per R3 singleton-parent); 16 Rails — 6 directional Customer↔External (per-leg origin overrides on inbound, rail-level on outbound), on-us cycle as 3 single-leg rails (one with `Variable` direction) wrapped in a TransferTemplate, ZBASweep + ConcentrationToFRBSweep operational sweeps, ACHOriginationDailySweep (2-leg aggregating, `daily-eod`) + CustomerFeeMonthlySettlement (single-leg aggregating, `monthly-eom`, lands in External per SPEC's permitted exemption), CustomerFeeAccrual (single-leg, union `leg_role: [CustomerDDA, InternalSuspenseRecon]`, `max_unbundled_age: P31D`, bundled by the monthly settlement), 2 ACH return rails (XOR group children); 1 TransferTemplate (`InternalTransferCycle`, `transfer_key: [internal_transfer_id]`, `completion: business_day_end+1d` — different from kitchen-sink's `metadata.<key>`/`business_day_end`); 3 ChainEntries (1 Required:true `ACHOriginationDailySweep → ConcentrationToFRBSweep` for orphan protection + 2 XOR-group `CustomerInboundACH → {NSF, StopPay}` returns); 3 LimitSchedules mirror today's `ar_ledger_transfer_limits`. **Description on every primitive** (top-level instance + every Account, AccountTemplate, Rail, TransferTemplate, ChainEntry, LimitSchedule).   - [x] M.2.2 — Seed generator landed at `tests/l2/sasquatch_ar_seed.py` (~430 lines). Public API: `emit_seed(L2Instance, ScenarioPlant) -> str` produces deterministic v6 INSERTs against the prefixed `<prefix>_transactions` + `<prefix>_daily_balances` tables (i.e., the schema M.1.4's `emit_schema` emits). Typed scenario primitives: `TemplateInstance` (concrete materialization of an AccountTemplate; integrator-supplied since the SPEC defers materialization to ETL), `DriftPlant` (delta_money on stored balance vs computed), `OverdraftPlant` (negative money; loader-style validation rejects positive values), `LimitBreachPlant` (outbound debit > LimitSchedule cap). `default_ar_scenario(today)` plants 1 of each scenario kind on 3 customer DDA instances using today's `apps/account_recon/demo_data.py` slugs so cross-checking stays straightforward. Generator output is byte-deterministic (sorted plant order; no random) — pre-requisite for M.2.7's hash-lock. 17 unit tests in `tests/test_l2_seed.py`: smoke (output non-empty, prefixed tables, v1.1 columns); per-scenario shape (drift produces 2 background credits + balance row at $200+delta; overdraft balance < 0 + positive-money rejection; limit-breach 2-leg debit > cap on the right rail/transfer_type); sign-direction agreement on every Debit/Credit row (parallels the schema CHECK); determinism (re-run = byte-identical); multi-plant scenarios; lookup-miss rejection; schema+seed concatenate into a well-formed pipeline. **Real-DB execution + L1 invariant queries surface the planted rows** is M.2.6's integration substep — that's the explicit handoff. 962/962 unit suite + pyright strict gate green.

- [ ] **M.2a — Re-evaluate AR as a generic L1 dashboard.** The framing-shift step. Now that L1 has Status / SupersedeReason / BundleId / aging-watch infrastructure (M.1a), and the AR port (M.2) has proven the L2 plumbing works, ask: what L1-derived visualizations become possible that today's hand-rolled AR didn't have? Rename the dashboard from `<prefix>-ar-dashboard` to `<prefix>-l1-dashboard` (per L2 instance) — the dashboard is L1-driven, fed by L2 to know what to scope; the visualizations are L1 invariants visualized. "AR" as an app concept dissolves; what we have is "L1 dashboard configured by an L2 instance whose persona vocabulary happens to be CMS treasury." Sub-step list deliberately open-ended below — M.2 will surface candidates that bubble up here.
  - [x] M.2a.1 — **Architecture decision: parallel-stack.** New module `apps/l1_dashboard/` builds a fresh tree-built app consuming M.1a.7's L1 invariant views directly. Parallel with the legacy `apps/account_recon/` (v5 + M.2.4b's drift-only v6 toehold), which stays until M.2a.10 decides on deprecation. M.2.4a's `_l2_datasets.py` v5-idiom translation becomes a transitional artifact that gets deleted at M.2a's close. New `build_l1_dashboard_app(cfg, *, l2_instance=None)` mirrors the AR build pipeline shape: auto-loads `default_l2_instance()` when no l2_instance kwarg; Analysis name `L1 Reconciliation Dashboard ({l2_prefix})` (multi-instance distinguishable); Dashboard ID `<l2_prefix>-l1-dashboard`. Skeleton ships with NO sheets — M.2a.2-M.2a.6 add them one at a time, each at their own substep so test guards catch accidental cross-substep landings. 8 new tests in `test_l1_dashboard.py` cover build pipeline shape, kwarg-only signature, L2-aware naming, Analysis + Dashboard registration, the "no sheets yet" guard. 1020/1020 unit suite + pyright gate green.

Title `"L1 Reconciliation Dashboard"` stays constant UI vocabulary per M.2a.4 design note.   - [x] M.2a.10 — **Iteration gate output.**
    - **Did the L1 dashboard framing hold? YES.** M.2a.1–M.2a.9 landed clean, each in its own commit, no architectural surprises. 5 sheets (Getting Started + Drift + Overdraft + Limit Breach + Today's Exceptions) ship against the M.1a.7 L1 invariant views with one-line `SELECT * FROM <prefix>_<view>` SQL per dataset. Aurora visual verify still pending user's hands-on run; surfaces from that run land here as new sub-bullets if anything breaks.
    - **M.3 framing — PARTIAL adoption.** The L1 dashboard is L2-agnostic by construction (it just consumes whatever the L2 emits as L1 invariant views), so M.3 = "write `sasquatch_pr.yaml` and the same L1 dashboard works against PR data." This is the structural test. **But**: PR has UX features the L1 dashboard doesn't currently cover — mutual table filtering (Payment Reconciliation tab), aging buckets + aging bar charts, per-pipeline-stage tabs (sale → settlement → payment → external), external transaction rail interactions. The L1 dashboard will show PR's L1 invariant violations, but the PR-specific dashboard surface beyond L1 invariants is open. Recommendation: M.3.1–M.3.4 land the L2 + verify the L1 dashboard works against PR data first, THEN M.3 follow-ups decide whether to (a) extend the L1 dashboard with PR-specific tabs, (b) keep `apps/payment_recon/` as a supplementary surface, or (c) build a generic "pipeline view" primitive that handles PR + AR equivalently.
    - **AR deprecation: DEFER.** Per the user's standing preference ("I've resisted other shifts earlier in the project and it's helped find subtle bugs"), keep `apps/account_recon/` and `apps/l1_dashboard/` parallel through M.5/M.6/M.7. The legacy AR app has features the L1 dashboard doesn't: aging buckets per check, drift timelines, per-account daily statement, cross-sheet drills, multi-parameter filters (status / transfer type / origin). M.7's render pipeline is the right time to evaluate whether the L1 dashboard absorbs those features or AR stays as the heavyweight surface. `apps/account_recon/_l2_datasets.py` (the M.2.4b v5-idiom translation toehold) becomes a transitional artifact deleted at AR-deprecation time; for now it stays — the legacy AR app reads it for the 2 v6 drift datasets.

  **Phase 1 — Interactivity primitives on existing surface (3 substeps):**
  - [x] M.2b.1 — **Universal date-range filter primitive** landed. 2 `DateTimeParam`s (`P_L1_DATE_START` + `P_L1_DATE_END`) with rolling 7-day defaults (`addDateTime(-7, 'DD', truncDate('DD', now()))` → `truncDate('DD', now())`). 5 `SINGLE_DATASET` `FilterGroup`s (one per data-bearing dataset), each carrying one `TimeRangeFilter` with parameter-bound `minimum`/`maximum` via dict-literal `{"Parameter": "<name>"}` shape. Per-dataset binding (rather than `cross_dataset="ALL_DATASETS"`) sidesteps the L1-view column-name mismatch — daily-balance views expose `business_day_start`, while `<prefix>_limit_breach` + `<prefix>_todays_exceptions` expose `business_day` (DATE_TRUNC of posting). Each `FilterGroup` scoped to its corresponding sheet via `scope_sheet()`. Each of the 4 data-bearing sheets gets paired `ParameterDateTimePicker` controls (Date From + Date To) bound to the shared params, so changing the date range on one sheet propagates to all four (sync via shared parameter values). Getting Started has no data → no pickers. New module-level constants `P_L1_DATE_START` / `P_L1_DATE_END` + `_wire_date_range_filter` helper. **Schema-fix deferred**: aligning `<prefix>_limit_breach.business_day` → `business_day_start`/`business_day_end` to enable cleaner `ALL_DATASETS` filtering is a follow-up (would make this whole helper collapse to the AR-style 1-FilterGroup pattern). 4 new tests in `test_l1_dashboard.py`: parameters registered, filter groups per-dataset present with the right IDs, pickers on every data sheet (Date From / Date To), filter columns target the correct date columns. 1047/1047 unit suite + pyright gate green.
  - [x] M.2b.2 — **Conditional formatting on existing tables** — link-tints landed (5 tables, all `account_id` columns). Each table populator pulls the `account_id` Dim out as a local var, passes it into `columns=` AND `conditional_formatting=[CellAccentText(on=col, color=accent)]`. Theme accent resolved from `get_preset(cfg.theme_preset).accent` — no hardcoded hex anywhere. **Drift-sign tinting deferred** — value-based conditional formatting (negative → warm, positive → cool) needs a new primitive beyond `CellAccentText`/`CellAccentMenu`'s always-true guard expression; queued for a follow-up substep when the new primitive lands. New test `test_account_id_link_tints_on_every_table` walks every Table on every data-bearing sheet, asserts at least one `CellAccentText` with the theme accent. 1048/1048 unit suite + pyright gate green.
  - [x] M.2b.3 — **Per-sheet filter controls.** Each data-bearing sheet carries the appropriate `FilterDropdown`s, all scoped to the sheet's own visuals (no cross-sheet bleed). New `_wire_per_sheet_dropdowns` helper with internal `_dropdown(...)` factory: each dropdown is a `CategoryFilter.with_values(values=[], select_all_options="FILTER_ALL_VALUES")` (multi-select with empty-default-means-all per AR's pattern), wrapped in a `FilterGroup` scoped to the sheet, surfaced as `sheet.add_filter_dropdown(...)`. Per-sheet dropdowns: **Drift** = Account + Account Role (cross_dataset `ALL_DATASETS` since drift + ledger_drift share column names — one dropdown filters both tables); **Overdraft** = Account + Account Role (`SINGLE_DATASET`); **Limit Breach** = Account + Transfer Type; **Today's Exceptions** = Check Type + Account + Transfer Type. Total = 9 new FilterGroups (3 dropdowns on Today's Exceptions + 2 each on the other three). Smoke-emit shows: 14 FilterGroups (5 date + 9 dropdown), 2 Params, controls: Drift 2+2 / Overdraft 2+2 / Limit Breach 2+2 / Today's Exc 2+3. 1 new test asserts each sheet carries the expected dropdown titles. 1049/1049 unit suite + pyright gate green.

  **Phase 3 — Cross-sheet drill plumbing (1 substep, comes after all sheets exist):**
  - [x] M.2b.7 — **Cross-sheet drill plumbing landed.** 7 drill actions across 6 source sites (Today's Exc table = 2; Drift leaf + parent + Overdraft + Limit Breach + Daily Statement = 1 each). 2 new sentinel-pattern analysis-level params (`pL1FilterAccount`, `pL1TxTransfer`) — both StringParam with `default=["__ALL__"]`; 5 new sentinel-or-match calc fields (one per per-invariant + transactions destination dataset; expression: `ifelse(${param} = '__ALL__', 'PASS', ifelse({col} = ${param}, 'PASS', 'FAIL'))` — mirror of AR's K.2 calc-field pattern); 5 new SINGLE_DATASET FilterGroups via `CategoryFilter.with_literal(value="PASS")` scoped per destination sheet. New typed DrillParam constants (`_DP_FILTER_ACCOUNT`, `_DP_TX_TRANSFER`, `_DP_DS_ACCOUNT`, `_DP_DS_BALANCE_DATE`) carry shape metadata so `cross_sheet_drill` refuses K.2-style mismatched writes at construction time. New `_l1_drill(...)` helper auto-resets the sentinel-pattern params not written by the caller (mirror of AR's `_ar_drill_to_transactions`). **Direction convention** per CLAUDE.md "left = back-toward-source, right = forward-deeper": Today's Exc → Drift = DATA_POINT_CLICK (per-invariant is upstream); Today's Exc → Daily Statement = DATA_POINT_MENU (forward); per-invariant tables → Daily Statement = DATA_POINT_MENU; Daily Statement → Transactions = DATA_POINT_MENU. Sheets restructured to build all skeletons upfront so each populator gets typed `target_sheet` refs (no late-binding). New imports: `AUTO`, `AutoResolved`, `CalcField`, `Drill`, `DrillParam`, `DrillResetSentinel`, `ColumnShape` — all from existing `common/tree` + `common/dataset_contract` surfaces, no new primitives needed. 7 new unit tests in `test_l1_dashboard.py` covering: drill params registered with sentinel default, 5 calc fields present + sentinel-or-match expression shape, 5 filter groups present, Today's Exc has 2 drills (CLICK+MENU) targeting Drift+Daily Statement, per-invariant tables drill to Daily Statement, Daily Statement drills to Transactions, every drill emits both NavigationOperation + SetParametersOperation. **Daily Statement gains transfer_id link tint** so analysts see where the drill source is. 1069/1069 unit suite + 15/15 API e2e green; Aurora deploy clean.

  **Phase 4 — Aging + audit + schema extension (5 substeps):**
  - [x] M.2b.8 — **`<prefix>_stuck_pending` L1 invariant view landed.** New MATERIALIZED VIEW in `common/l2/schema.py` after `_limit_breach`. Shape (13 cols): identifying (`transaction_id`, `account_id`, `account_name`, `account_role`, `account_parent_role`, `transfer_id`, `transfer_type`, `rail_name`), diagnostic (`amount_money`, `amount_direction`, `posting`, `max_pending_age_seconds`, `age_seconds`). Surfaces rows where `status='Pending'` AND `age_seconds > max_pending_age_seconds`. Caps inline at view-emit time via new `_render_pending_age_cases` helper — mirror of `_render_limit_breach_cases` shape: walks both TwoLegRail + SingleLegRail, emits `WHEN ct.rail_name = '<name>' THEN <int seconds>` per Rail with `max_pending_age` set; rails without an aging watch get NULL → outer WHERE excludes them; empty result if no Rail has the field set returns `NULL` so view stays syntactically valid + inert. **Postgres-specific bits**: `EXTRACT(EPOCH FROM (CURRENT_TIMESTAMP - ct.posting))` for live age computation (refreshed at REFRESH time so the matview snapshots both live age + cap, dashboards sort without re-querying CURRENT_TIMESTAMP). 3 dashboard hot-path indexes: `(rail_name)`, `(account_id)`, `(transfer_id)` — the last for the M.2b.7 drill-target filter group when M.2b.10's Pending Aging sheet wires its drill into Transactions. Drop statement added at the top of `_L1_INVARIANT_VIEWS_DROPS_TEMPLATE` (between `_daily_statement_summary` and `_limit_breach`) per the L1-views-drop-before-base-drops rule from M.2.6 bug C. `refresh_matviews_sql` extended with `_stuck_pending` between `_limit_breach` and `_daily_statement_summary` (depends on current_transactions only, refreshes alongside other L1 invariants). 5 new tests in `test_l2_schema.py` (view emits with status + age filter, embeds rail max_pending_age inline as integer seconds, no-aging-rails case is inert, indexes emit, view appears in `_L1_VIEW_NAMES` parameterised tests). Aurora deploy clean: `m2_6_verify.py` end-to-end runs 24 REFRESH+ANALYZE statements (was 22), `_stuck_pending` matview applies + refreshes correctly, 0 rows currently (no stuck-Pending plant in the seed yet — that lands at M.2b.14). 1075/1075 unit suite green. **Verify-script scenario assertion deferred to M.2b.14** when the seed plant lands.
  - [x] M.2b.9 — **`<prefix>_stuck_unbundled` L1 invariant view landed.** New MATERIALIZED VIEW after `_stuck_pending` with the same 13-col shape (rename: `max_unbundled_age_seconds` instead of `max_pending_age_seconds`). Filter is `bundle_id IS NULL AND status = 'Posted'` (vs `status = 'Pending'` for stuck_pending) — AggregatingRails only bundle posted legs, so a Pending leg isn't "stuck unbundled," it's "stuck pending"; the two views cover disjoint conditions. Caps inline at view-emit time via new `_render_unbundled_age_cases` helper — mirror of `_render_pending_age_cases` shape, walks all rails, emits one CASE branch per Rail with `max_unbundled_age` set. Per validator R8 the L2 loader already enforces `max_unbundled_age` is only set on bundle-eligible rails, so by the time we render every Rail with the field is correctly configured. Empty/no-bundling case returns NULL → outer WHERE excludes everything → inert valid SQL. Same 3 dashboard hot-path indexes (`idx_<p>_su_rail`, `idx_<p>_su_account`, `idx_<p>_su_transfer`). Drop statement added between `_daily_statement_summary` and `_stuck_pending` in `_L1_INVARIANT_VIEWS_DROPS_TEMPLATE`. `refresh_matviews_sql` extended (now 13 matviews × 2 = 26 statements). 5 new tests in `test_l2_schema.py` (mirror of stuck_pending tests: bundle+status+age filter present, max_unbundled_age inlined as integer seconds, no-bundling-rails inert case, 3 indexes emit, view in `_L1_VIEW_NAMES` parameterised). Aurora deploy clean: 26 REFRESH+ANALYZE statements run cleanly, `_stuck_unbundled` matview applies + refreshes correctly, 0 rows currently (no stuck-Unbundled plant in the seed yet — lands at M.2b.14). 1081/1081 unit suite green.
  - [x] M.2b.10 — **Pending Aging sheet landed.** New `SHEET_PENDING_AGING` inserted between Limit Breach and Today's Exceptions (one of the operations-aging-watch group of sheets). Backed by `DS_STUCK_PENDING` wrapping the M.2b.8 matview; new `STUCK_PENDING_CONTRACT` (13 cols, mirror of matview).   - [x] M.2b.11 — **Unbundled Aging sheet landed.** Mirror of Pending Aging structure (KPI + horizontal aging BarChart + detail Table) but backed by `DS_STUCK_UNBUNDLED` wrapping the M.2b.9 matview.   - [x] M.2b.12 — **Supersession Audit sheet landed.** New `SHEET_SUPERSESSION_AUDIT` inserted between Unbundled Aging and Today's Exceptions. 2 new datasets: `DS_SUPERSESSION_TRANSACTIONS` reads from BASE `<prefix>_transactions` (NOT Current* — Current* hides superseded entries by design) where `id IN (SELECT id FROM <prefix>_transactions GROUP BY id HAVING COUNT(*) > 1) ORDER BY id, entry`; `DS_SUPERSESSION_DAILY_BALANCES` mirrors the pattern on the composite key `(account_id, business_day_start)`.   **Phase 7 — Final iteration gate (1 substep):**

    **M.3 framing decision** (the substep's stated purpose):

    Three options on the table going in:
    - **(a) Pure L1 absorbs PR entirely** — write `sasquatch_pr.yaml`, verify L1 renders, ship.
    - **(b) Parallel `apps/pr_dashboard/` stack** — keep L1 generic, build PR's specialized surface separately.
    - **(c) PR-shape sheets as L2-opt-in extensions on L1** — third option crystallized at the gate; dashboard renders PR-specific sheets when the L2 instance declares the relevant pipeline structure (mirror of how aging-watch sheets only render when rails set `max_pending_age`).

    **Decision: (a) + (c) combined, NOT (b).** Evidence:
    - PR's match-status checks (settlement_payment_mismatch, unmatched_external, etc) ARE L1 invariants — they fall out of the existing drift / limit_breach / stuck_unbundled views once `sasquatch_pr.yaml` declares the matching rails / templates correctly. M.3.1-M.3.6 land that and the L1 dashboard renders them for free.
    - PR's UX-specific patterns — **pipeline tabs** (sale → settlement → payment → external as a 4-tab linear walk) and **mutual filter** (click a row in either external or payment table to filter the other) — are NOT L1 SHOULD-constraints; they're a different visualization of the same data. These DO need new dashboard surface.
    - But: the right home for that surface is **M.2d.4** ("PR dashboard → generic L2-validation dashboard") + (c)-style L2-opt-in additions on the L1 dashboard, NOT a separate `apps/pr_dashboard/` stack. The L2 instance YAML already declares `Chains` + `bundles_activity` — the pipeline structure is in the L2 today. Reading it to render an opt-in pipeline view sheet is a generalization of the L2-fed pattern, not an exception to it.
    - The legacy `apps/payment_recon/` app stays as the parallel-stack reference until M.2d.4 lands the L2-validation surface, then deprecates. No M.3 substep should rebuild PR-as-its-own-app.

    **M.3.7+ rewritten on the back of this**: rather than "build apps/pr_dashboard/ on the L.1 tree primitives" (the original M.3.8 Path C), M.3.7+ becomes "M.3.7 = wire pipeline-shape sheets as L2-opt-in on the L1 dashboard (gated on `<L2>.chains` declaring the pipeline pattern); M.3.8 = wire mutual-filter Payment Reconciliation tab as another opt-in; M.3.9 = deprecate `apps/payment_recon/` once L1+opt-ins cover the existing surface". M.3.1-M.3.6 are unchanged (the L2 + L1 invariant verify path).

    Phase M.2b closes. Branch ready to merge to main; M.3 starts on a fresh branch with `phase-m-3-port-pr-as-l2-instance` from the merged baseline.

  **Notes for M.2b execution:**
  - **No new tree primitives except LineChart.** The L.1 surface (Drill / FilterGroup / FilterDropdown / FilterDateTimePicker / CellAccentText / CellAccentMenu / KPI / Table / BarChart) covers everything else.
  - **Match the M.2a.3-style cadence**: one substep ≈ one commit, run unit tests + pyright at every commit, never let the suite break across substeps.
  - **`apps/l1_dashboard/app.py` will grow.** ~700 lines now → ~1500-2000 after M.2b. Split into `apps/l1_dashboard/sheets/<sheet>.py` modules (mirroring how AR's modules grew) gets queued for M.2b.13 if size justifies.
  - **No PR overlap.** M.2b only touches `apps/l1_dashboard/` + `common/l2/schema.py` + `common/tree/visuals.py` + `tests/` + `docs/`. PR's surface is M.3's business.
  - **Docs land Sasquatch-flavored, M.7 templatifies later.** Same approach AR / PR / Inv took — write Sasquatch-named prose now, M.7's render pipeline (which extracts L2 vocabulary into templates) handles persona substitution at that phase. M.2a.7's description-driven prose seam already proves the dashboard surface is templatable; the handbook surface follows when M.7 lands.
  - **e2e tests land at M.2c, interleaved with M.2b execution** — see M.2c phase below. Originally queued as a post-M.2b follow-up; user redirected after Phase 1 (M.2b.1-3) shipped to add regression coverage now so subsequent phases land on tested foundation.

- [ ] **M.2c — L1 dashboard e2e regression coverage.** Inserted after M.2b.1-3 (Phase 1 done, foundation reviewed) and before M.2b.4 starts. Mirrors K.4.9's pattern for Investigation: API tests confirm AWS resources + dashboard structure; browser tests confirm sheets render + visuals present + filter controls actually narrow data. Drill tests deferred until M.2b.7 lands the drill chain. Substep cadence one-commit-per-substep per the project standard.

  **Acceptance for M.2c at the closing gate:**
  - L1 dashboard fixtures land in `tests/e2e/conftest.py` mirroring `inv_dashboard_id` / `inv_app` / `inv_dataset_ids` shape.
  - 5 new test files under `tests/e2e/`: `test_l1_deployed_resources.py` (API), `test_l1_dashboard_structure.py` (API; `TreeValidator`-derived), `test_l1_dashboard_renders.py` (browser smoke), `test_l1_sheet_visuals.py` (browser; `TreeValidator`-derived), `test_l1_filters.py` (browser; date-range + per-sheet dropdowns narrow data).
  - Aurora warmup queries extended with the 5 L1 invariant views (`<prefix>_drift` / `_ledger_drift` / `_overdraft` / `_limit_breach` / `_todays_exceptions` etc.) so cold-start doesn't trip the suite per F12.
  - `./run_e2e.sh --skip-deploy api` + `--skip-deploy browser` both green against the M.2b.1-3 deployed dashboard.
  - Subsequent M.2b substeps update each affected e2e file in the same commit (e.g., M.2b.4 Daily Statement → adds expected sheet + visual asserts to `test_l1_sheet_visuals.py`); cadence: code change + e2e adjustment land together.

  **Hard constraint — NO HARDCODED DATA in M.2c tests.** Tests must remain green when the seed scenarios change (M.2b.14 will add new plants; M.3 will swap PR's L2 instance in). Concrete rules every M.2c substep follows:
  - **Structural assertions derive from the tree.** `expected_sheets = [s.name for s in l1_app.analysis.sheets]`, `expected_titles = [v.title for v in sheet.visuals]`, `expected_param_names = {p.name for p in l1_app.analysis.parameters}`. Never a hand-listed expected set.
  - **Resource IDs derive from the prefix.** `f"{resource_prefix}-l1-dashboard"` etc. — never hardcoded.
  - **Filter tests use relative assertions, not absolute counts.** "row count > 0 before filter; row count drops after applying any one dropdown value" — never `assert row_count == 12`.
  - **Dropdown values come from the dropdown.** Walk the dropdown DOM to find the first selectable value (or any specific value), don't hardcode "Bigfoot Brews" or "ach-credit". The browser_helpers `select_dropdown_first_value(...)` shape (or new helper if missing) keeps tests persona-agnostic.
  - **Column-name assertions use the contract.** If a test references `business_day` or `account_id`, derive from the dataset's contract (`get_contract(DS_DRIFT).column_names`), not a hardcoded literal.
  - **Date assertions reference reality, not literals.** "the dashboard renders for the most recent business day" — derive that day from a `MAX(business_day_start)` query against Aurora at test setup if needed; never assert `'2026-04-25'`.

Extended `_WARMUP_QUERIES` with the 5 L1 invariant views (`sasquatch_ar_drift` / `_ledger_drift` / `_overdraft` / `_expected_eod_balance_breach` / `_limit_breach`) + the 2 Current* views (`sasquatch_ar_current_transactions` / `_current_daily_balances`) so Aurora cold-start (F12) doesn't trip the first SELECT. - [ ] **M.2d — L2 / dashboard backlog (post-AR-build cleanup).** Surfaced 2026-04-27 during the M.2b L1 dashboard review. None of these block M.2b or M.2c — they're the "now that we've built one app on the foundation, here's what's missing or worth rethinking" pile. Dig in after M.2b closes; rescope at M.2d's own iteration gate based on what M.3's PR port surfaces (PR will likely add to this list).

  - [x] M.2d.1 — **L2 validator: every L2-instance reference to a `transfer_type` string MUST resolve to some Rail's `transfer_type`.** Original framing ("every Transfer MUST match a Rail") split into two static checks + one runtime check on triage. The static checks ship now; the runtime check (every *posted* Transaction's `transfer_type` matches some Rail) belongs on the L1 dashboard as a SHOULD-constraint matview, queued for M.2d.4. **R10 — every `LimitSchedule.transfer_type` matches some `Rail.transfer_type`** (catches typo'd caps that silently never fire). **R11 — every bare-form `bundles_activity` selector resolves to a declared `Rail.name` OR some declared `Rail.transfer_type`** (catches typo'd bundles that silently match nothing; complement to R8 which checks the inverse and R9 which handles the dotted form). 6 new tests in `test_l2_validate.py` (rejection + accepts-by-transfer_type + accepts-by-name + dotted-form-skipped). 1 minor fixture extension in `test_l2_pipeline::test_pipeline_limit_schedule` to add the matching Rail R10 now requires; 1 narrow description test in `test_l2_descriptions::test_limit_schedule_description_loads` opted out via `validate=False`. SPEC.md's M.2d.1 entry now describes the implemented rules. 1095/1097 unit suite green.
  - [x] M.2d.2 — **L2 validator: no overlap on (role, transfer_type) entries** is now a YAML parse-time error. The U5 check (`_check_unique_limit_schedule_combinations` in `validate.py`, originally an opt-in `validate(instance)` call) fires automatically inside `load_instance(path)` — `load_instance` now runs the full cross-entity validator before returning, so an integrator authoring a YAML with overlapping LimitSchedule entries gets `L2ValidationError` at parse time rather than a silent CASE-order surprise at render. Opt-out via `load_instance(path, validate=False)` for narrow loader tests with intentionally-incomplete fixtures (4 sites updated). SPEC.md's Validation Rules section now documents the parse-time enforcement contract; M.2d.1's SHOULD-rule is also noted there as planned. New rejection test `test_load_instance_runs_validate_by_default` + complementary `test_load_instance_validate_false_skips_cross_entity_pass`. **Side cleanup**: 8 v3-era schema-doc-parsing tests (TestAccountTypeCatalog, TestMetadataKeyCatalog, TestSqlBlocksParse::test_etl_examples_present, TestSchemaContractAlignment) marked `xfail` with M.2d-rescope notes — they parse markdown structures the Schema_v6 rewrite removed (account_type catalog moved to L2 instance YAML; ETL Examples 1-5 moved to `docs/walkthroughs/etl/`); rewriting them against the v6 + L2 surface is its own substep. 1089/1097 unit suite green (8 xfailed, 1 xpassed).
  - [x] M.2d.3 — **Multiple dashboards from one L2 instance** is now expressible. The L2 instance prefix becomes the middle segment of every QS resource ID via the new `cfg.l2_instance_prefix` Config field — `cfg.prefixed("l1-dashboard")` returns `qs-gen-sasquatch_ar-l1-dashboard` when set, the legacy `qs-gen-l1-dashboard` when unset. `build_l1_dashboard_app` and `build_all_l1_dashboard_datasets` derive the field idempotently from `l2_instance.instance` at the top of each entry point, so all 69 existing `cfg.prefixed(...)` call sites needed zero changes — they automatically produce L2-aware IDs whenever the cfg flows through an L2-fed builder. **Tag**: `cfg.tags()` now adds `L2Instance: <prefix>` when the field is set. **Cleanup**: per-instance mode (when `cfg.l2_instance_prefix` is set) only sweeps resources whose `L2Instance` tag matches — concurrent deploys against different L2 instances don't sweep each other; legacy mode (no L2 prefix) preserves the M.1.x out-dir-authoritative behaviour for backward compat. **Surface**: 3 file changes (`config.py`, `cleanup.py`, `apps/l1_dashboard/{app,datasets}.py`); 1 new `tests/test_cleanup.py` (6 tests) + 5 new tests in `test_models.py`; e2e `conftest.py` fixtures re-derive IDs through a new `l1_l2_prefix` fixture; 2 unit-test fixtures updated for the new ID shape (`test_l1_dashboard.py`'s ID assertion + CLI dataset filename list). 1106/1106 unit suite green. **Deploy footnote**: existing deployed L1 resources have legacy `qs-gen-l1-*` IDs; first deploy after this lands needs the legacy resources cleaned up via the standard `cleanup` flow (the new IDs surface them as stale). **Out of scope (deliberately)**: building a second app (PR) — that's the consumer of this work, not part of it; queued for M.2d.4.
  - [x] M.2d.4 — **Subsumed by M.3.** This substep originally proposed rethinking `apps/payment_recon/` as a generic L2-validation dashboard. M.3's reframing (apps/l2_flow_tracing/) IS that idea — a brand-new app whose entire purpose is making L2 spec primitives visible, persona-blind by construction, rendering against any L2 instance. The original M.2d.4 framing (PR dashboard → renderer over validator output) is exactly what M.3.4-M.3.9 build. Closes here without separate work.
  - [x] M.2d.6 — **`quicksight-gen demo seed-l2 <yaml>` lands** as the integrator-facing way to generate all L1 exception cases from a YAML without writing Python. Two new modules: `common/l2/auto_scenario.py` (deterministic plant heuristics walking the L2 instance — picks first AccountTemplate + materializes 2 generic customers, picks first inbound 2-leg rail for drift, first LimitSchedule with matching outbound rail for breach, first rail with `max_pending_age` / `max_unbundled_age`, etc.) and the new `demo seed-l2` CLI subcommand. Plants that can't be derived from a thin YAML (e.g., no LimitSchedule) are omitted with a one-line `[warn]` per omission rather than failing. **Hash-lock extension**: `L2Instance.seed_hash` is a new optional `str | None` field; YAML's top-level `seed_hash:` carries a 64-char lowercase SHA256 (loader-validated regex). CLI `--lock` rewrites the YAML's `seed_hash` field in place (preserves comments + ordering by treating the file as text); `--check-hash` exits 1 on mismatch for CI. Auto-seed hashes against a fixed canonical reference date (`2030-01-01`) so the SHA256 is stable across days; real-world `apply` paths still use today's date. **Tests**: `tests/test_auto_scenario.py` (10 tests) covering coverage / determinism / persona-blindness / picker stability + `tests/test_cli_seed_l2.py` (7 tests) covering stdout / file / lock-rewrite / lock-append / check-pass / check-mismatch / check-missing-field. spec_example.yaml's seed_hash is now locked at `688566c3...44d85`; drift in the auto-scenario or seed code trips the dedicated `test_spec_example_seed_hash_matches_yaml` regression. **Renames**: original M.2d.6 (re-aim v3-era contract tests) is now M.2d.7 below — same content, just renumbered. 1127/1127 unit suite green.

Removed: TestAccountTypeCatalog (2 tests), TestMetadataKeyCatalog (4 tests), TestSqlBlocksParse::test_etl_examples_present (1 test), TestSchemaContractAlignment::test_every_inserted_column_is_documented + test_metadata_keys_referenced_in_examples_are_documented (2 tests). Plus the dead `_markdown_table_first_column` helper, `CANONICAL_ACCOUNT_TYPES` import, and `METADATA_SECTIONS` constant. Comment stubs left in each test class explaining the M.2d.8 redirect. Was 1127 passed / 8 xfailed / 1 xpassed → now 1127 passed / 0 xfailed.

  - [x] M.2d.8 — **L2 seed contract matrix landed** in `tests/test_l2_seed_contract.py`. One file with 8 contract assertions, parameterized via `pytest.fixture(params=L2_INSTANCES)` over `[spec_example.yaml, sasquatch_ar.yaml]` — each test runs twice, producing 16 test cases from 8 functions. Adding `sasquatch_pr.yaml` in M.3.1 is a one-line addition to `L2_INSTANCES` and the entire contract surface immediately covers PR with no per-test edits. **Assertions**: (1) byte-determinism (two emit_seed runs = identical SQL); (2) seed_hash matches YAML's locked value; (3) account_role literals resolve to declared L2 roles; (4) account_id literals resolve to declared singletons OR synthetic cust-NNN template-instances; (5) rail_name literals resolve to declared Rail.name; (6) transfer_type literals resolve to declared Rail.transfer_type; (7) metadata JSON keys come from Rail.metadata_keys ∪ {customer_id, external_reference}; (8) every column in the seed's INSERT lists is documented in Schema_v6.md's `<prefix>_<table>` ### Columns table. **`sasquatch_ar.yaml` got its seed_hash locked** at `44efd4dd…` (per-instance hash, not the same as default_ar_scenario's curated hash since auto-scenario picks different rails/counterparties). 1143 passed (+16), 216 skipped, 0 xfailed.

  - [ ] **M.2d.9 — Random L2 YAML fuzzer feeds the M.2d.8 matrix.** The two hand-written L2 YAMLs cover *shapes the authors thought to write*. A fuzzer covers the shapes *no one thought to write* — that's where the matrix's contract assertions actually earn their keep. **Goal**: produce a third L2 instance, programmatically generated as a deterministic random valid variation; run the full M.2d.8 matrix against it; failures yield a reproducible seed + saved YAML for triage. **Seed sourcing**: random per dev test session (not deterministic across runs — that's the point of fuzzing); CI pins the seed via `QS_GEN_FUZZ_SEED=N` env var so CI runs are reproducible across builds. The chosen seed prints at session start regardless, so a passing run also surfaces "this is the seed you can lock if you want to lock it." **Validity contract**: every emitted YAML loads + validates without error (passes U1-U5, R1-R11, C1-C2, S1-S6, V1-V2, O1). The generator constructs YAML *layered* — roles → accounts/templates → rails → templates → chains → limit_schedules — so cross-entity constraints are satisfied at *construction time* rather than via reject-and-retry. **Variation surface** sampled per seed: number of singletons (1-N), templates (0-M), rails (1-K), single-leg vs two-leg ratio, aggregating-rail count + bundles_activity coverage, transfer_template count + leg_rails composition, chains with XOR groups, LimitSchedule count, per-rail metadata_keys length, max_pending_age / max_unbundled_age presence, description richness.

    - [x] M.2d.9.1 — **Layered generator core landed** in `tests/l2/fuzz.py` (~530 lines). `random_l2_yaml(seed: int) -> str` produces YAML text via `yaml.safe_dump`; one `random.Random(seed)` threaded through `_FuzzPlan` sampling + 6 layered builders (`_build_accounts` → `_build_account_templates` → `_build_rails` → `_build_transfer_templates` → `_build_chains` → `_build_limit_schedules`). Cross-entity validity is a structural property — every layer references only identifiers declared upstream. Subtle bits: `_wire_bundles_activity` populates aggregating-rail bundling AFTER non-aggregating rails exist; `_ensure_single_leg_reconciliation` closes any S3-leftover by adding to an aggregating rail's bundles_activity OR synthesizing a backstop transfer_template; `_wire_max_unbundled_age` only sets the field on confirmed-bundled rails (R8); `_finalize_two_leg_expected_net` walks two-leg rails and sets/clears `expected_net` based on whether they're a TransferTemplate leg (S1/S2). Variable-direction single-leg rails deliberately not generated (closure semantics). Instance prefix bakes the seed (`fuzz_seed_NNNN`) for triage visibility.

    - [x] M.2d.9.2 — **Fuzzer meta-guard landed** in `tests/test_l2_fuzz.py` (~115 lines, 106 test cases). Three properties: (1) every seed in `range(100)` produces YAML that `load_instance` accepts without raising — the loader's per-entity AND validator's cross-entity checks both pass; (2) byte-determinism on 5 spot-check seeds; (3) coverage assertion that across 100 seeds the fuzzer exercises every primitive kind (accounts, templates, rails, transfer_templates, chains, limit_schedules) AND every interesting rail shape (two-leg, single-leg, aggregating, max_pending_age, max_unbundled_age, xor_group). All 106 cases pass in ~0.7s.

    - [x] M.2d.9.3 — **Fuzz entry wired into M.2d.8 matrix as a third row.** New module-level `_resolve_fuzz_seed()` reads `QS_GEN_FUZZ_SEED` env var (CI determinism) or falls back to `secrets.randbits(32)` per session (dev-time random exploration). `L2_INSTANCES` now has 3 entries: `spec_example`, `sasquatch_ar`, `fuzz-seed-<N>` — the test `id` carries the actual seed so failure output names it directly. `_fuzz_yaml_path()` materializes the YAML into `tests/l2/fuzz_failures/fuzz_seed_<N>.yaml` and in-process locks the `seed_hash` (mirrors `demo seed-l2 --lock` without subprocess overhead) so the matrix's hash-check passes by construction. Session-autouse `_announce_fuzz_seed` fixture writes the seed banner to the terminal reporter at session start so passing runs ALSO surface the seed (`fuzz seed for L2 contract matrix: 1149835342 (random; pin via QS_GEN_FUZZ_SEED=N)`). Matrix went from 16 → 24 test cases (8 contracts × 3 instances).

    - [x] M.2d.9.4 — **Failure triage hooks landed.** `_hint_if_fuzz(instance)` appends `\n\n[reproduce] QS_GEN_FUZZ_SEED=<N> pytest …\n[fuzz YAML] <path>` to every assertion message in the matrix when the failing instance is the fuzz entry — developer reading a failure sees both the seed and the YAML path inline. Fuzz YAMLs always materialize to `tests/l2/fuzz_failures/<seed>.yaml` (whether or not anything fails) so triage is path-stable. `tests/l2/fuzz_failures/` added to `.gitignore` so seeds don't accidentally land in git. (Deferred: a per-failure README explaining "fix vs pin" triage flow — wait until first real failure surfaces to write it from concrete evidence.)

    - [x] M.2d.9.5 — **50-seed sweep passes clean.** Ran `QS_GEN_FUZZ_SEED=N pytest tests/test_l2_seed_contract.py` for `seed in range(50)`; 50/50 passed. Some seeds produce L2 shapes where the auto-scenario can't materialize a particular plant kind (e.g., no aggregating rails → no rail_name in seed) — these surface as `pytest.skip(...)` rather than failures, which is the intended UX (they signal "this contract isn't applicable here", not "this contract failed"). No bugs surfaced from the sweep. Two judgment calls deferred: (a) committing CI to a randomized seed-per-run vs the fixed `QS_GEN_FUZZ_SEED=42` we'd default to — wait until M.3 surfaces whether PR's L2 shape adds enough variation that random-per-run earns its keep; (b) widening the fuzzer to include Variable-direction single-leg rails — wait until PR's actual L2 needs them. **M.2d.9 closes**: 1257 passing tests overall (+114 from M.2d.9 work), 0 xfailed.

  - [x] M.2d.5 — **Seed primitives lifted into `common/l2/seed.py`.** Plant dataclasses (`TemplateInstance` / `DriftPlant` / `OverdraftPlant` / `LimitBreachPlant` / `StuckPendingPlant` / `StuckUnbundledPlant` / `SupersessionPlant` / `ScenarioPlant`), `emit_seed`, every `_emit_*_rows` helper, `_txn_row` / `_balance_row` / `_sql_str`, and the deterministic-sort key helpers all moved out of `tests/l2/sasquatch_ar_seed.py` into the production library. `tests/l2/sasquatch_ar_seed.py` shrinks to just `default_ar_scenario()` (data-only). M.3.4's `tests/l2/sasquatch_pr_seed.py` will land the same way: imports primitives, defines a scenario. **Persona-blindness fix surfaced by the user's "use the SPEC example.yaml + check no sasquatch leaks" challenge**: the original lift carried two hardcoded persona literals (`"ext-frb-snb-master"` + `"Federal Reserve Bank — SNB Master"`) in `_emit_limit_breach_rows` + `_emit_drift_background_rows`. Fixed by adding `counter_account_id: Identifier` to `LimitBreachPlant`, `counter_account_id` + `rail_name` to `DriftPlant`; the seed now resolves the counterparty Account from `instance.accounts` and the rail's `transfer_type` + per-leg origins from the rail's L2 declaration. **Cleanliness guard**: new `tests/test_seed_persona_clean.py` (4 tests) loads `tests/l2/spec_example.yaml` (a hand-assembled persona-neutral instance from SPEC.md §618+ Worked Example shapes), runs every plant type through `emit_seed`, asserts zero Sasquatch/SNB/FRB/Bigfoot strings appear AND that every account-id literal in the SQL came from the loaded instance. Hash-lock re-locked (`cd2377…` → `b7c7db…` once for header reword, no second drift since the AR fixture's resolved counterparty values are byte-identical to the previous hardcoded literals). 1110/1110 unit suite green.

  **Out of scope for M.2d:** anything that affects M.2b's running L1 dashboard, M.2c's e2e tests, or M.3's PR port plumbing. M.2d is post-AR cleanup, not foundation work.

- [ ] **M.3 — Build `apps/l2_flow_tracing/` against the L2 spec primitives** (subsumes M.2d.4). Reframed at the M.2d → M.3 transition: porting `apps/payment_recon/` to consume L2 doesn't actually validate anything new — it just renames Sasquatch strings. Instead, build a brand-new application whose entire purpose is to trace flow through the L2 spec primitives, persona-blind by construction. The dashboard renders against ANY L2 instance (spec_example, sasquatch_ar, sasquatch_pr, fuzz-seed-N) — its existence IS the evidence that the L2 SPEC is sufficient.

  **What this app is**: three tabs (Rails / Chains / L2 Exceptions) plus auto-derived metadata-driven filters. Rails tab makes every declared `Rail` visible with static config + runtime activity counts. Chains tab uses Sankey to visualize chain flows so failures pop visually. L2 Exceptions tab surfaces "did your L2 declaration match reality?" gaps (chain orphans, dead rails, unmatched runtime transfer_types, dead caps) — distinct from L1's "did reality satisfy invariants?" framing. Filters are auto-generated from the union of `instance.rails[*].metadata_keys`, populated via `SELECT DISTINCT JSON_VALUE(metadata, '$.<key>')` per filter.

  **What's deprecated**: the original M.3 plan to port `apps/payment_recon/` to L2. The legacy app stays as the existing v5 surface; M.3 doesn't touch it. M.2d.4 ("PR dashboard → generic L2-validation dashboard") collapses INTO M.3 — same idea, different name.

  **What's preserved**: `sasquatch_pr.yaml` lands as a third hand-written L2 instance, but ONLY as an L2 SPEC stress test (TransferKey, Variable closure, XOR chains, AggregatingRail) — not as a destination dashboard. It joins `L2_INSTANCES` so the M.2d.8 contract matrix runs against it; auto-scenario covers its seed needs (no hand-curated `sasquatch_pr_seed.py`).

  Acceptance for M.3 at the closing iteration gate: `sasquatch_pr.yaml` loads + validates + passes the contract matrix; `apps/l2_flow_tracing/` renders all three tabs against all 4 L2 instances (spec_example, sasquatch_ar, sasquatch_pr, fuzz); auto-derived metadata filters work per-instance; L2 exceptions tab surfaces planted scenarios (chain orphans, unmatched transfer_types) correctly against real Aurora; iteration gate sketches the future end-to-end harness destination (YAML → schema → seed → DB → deploy → browser-validate-shows-planted-rows) for M.4.

Coverage: 16 accounts (10 internal singletons + 6 external counterparties — adds MerchantPayableClearing + MerchantDDAControl + ExternalCardNetwork to AR's set), 3 templates (CustomerDDA + MerchantDDA + ZBASubAccount), 21 rails (15 two-leg + 6 single-leg, 3 aggregating, 9 with max_pending_age, 2 with max_unbundled_age, 1 Variable direction), 2 TransferTemplates (InternalTransferCycle 3-leg with Variable closure + MerchantSettlementCycle TransferKey-grouped), 6 chains (1 required + 2 ACHReturnReason XOR + 3 PayoutVehicle XOR), 6 LimitSchedules (3 DDAControl × {ach, wire, cash} + 3 MerchantDDAControl × {payout_ach, payout_wire, payout_check}), 12 transfer_types. `load_instance(...)` validates clean against all 24 SPEC rules; `emit_schema(...)` produces 33KB / 671 lines of prefixed DDL.   - [x] M.3.3 — **Targeted L2 primitive tests against `sasquatch_pr.yaml` landed.** New `tests/test_l2_pr_primitives.py` — 13 shape-level assertions across 4 test classes covering the four primitives the SPEC stress-tests in PR shape:

      - **AggregatingRail bundling** — every aggregating rail has cadence + bundles_activity (mirrors validator S5); `max_unbundled_age` only on rails referenced by some aggregating rail's bundles_activity (mirrors validator R8); `ExternalCardSettlement` bundles `MerchantCardSale` + `MerchantCardSale.max_unbundled_age` is set; aggregating cadence strings match v1 `CadenceExpression` vocabulary (mirrors validator V2). Initial run hit one false-positive (test asserted Rail's raw `posted_requirements` directly instead of the resolved view); fixed by switching to `derived.posted_requirements_for(...)` per the SPEC's TransferKey auto-derivation contract.   - [x] M.3.7 — **L2 Exceptions tab landed** — six L2 hygiene sections, each KPI-pair + detail Table backed by its own narrow dataset. All visual titles lead with "L2:" so the surface is visually distinct from the L1 exceptions tab. Six new datasets (`<prefix>-l2ft-exc-{chain-orphans, unmatched-transfer-type, dead-rails, dead-bundles-activity, dead-metadata, dead-limit-schedules}-dataset`):
      - **L2.1 Chain orphans** — reuses chains' CTE shape; filters to `required = 'Required' AND parent > child`. XOR-group multi/none deferred (precise check needs per-Transfer-id grouping).
      - **L2.2 Unmatched transfer_type** — LEFT JOIN to declared types CTE + filter to NULL. Per-transfer-type posting counts.
      - **L2.3 Dead rails** — same shape as Rails dataset filtered to `COALESCE(total_postings, 0) = 0`.
      - **L2.4 Dead bundles_activity** — NOT EXISTS check on (rail OR transfer_type) attribution to avoid false positives.
      - **L2.5 Dead metadata declarations** — one NOT EXISTS fragment per (rail, key) with static `$.<key>` JSONPath (portable per no-JSONB constraint).
      - **L2.6 Dead LimitSchedules** — NOT EXISTS over outbound DEBIT only; inbound flow doesn't exercise a cap.

      Sheet populator: 1 sheet header + 6 section headers + 12 KPIs (count + distinct per section) + 6 Tables. Helper `_add_l2_exception_section` keeps the per-section layout DRY. **Tests** (32 new): 6× dataset-targets-prefixed + 6× ID-uses-prefix + 6× contract-matches-builder (3 parametrized fixtures), per-section SQL semantics (required-only filter, declared-types CTE, zero-postings filter, both-attributions NOT EXISTS, static JSON paths, debit-only filter), 12 KPIs + 6 Tables tally on sheet, all titles carry L2: prefix, every section header present (parametrized over the 6 sections). Updated invariants: dataset count 2→8, replaced placeholder parametrize with `test_no_remaining_placeholder_sheets` since M.3.7 lands the last populator. Full suite: 1307 passed (was 1275) + 216 skipped.

  - [x] M.3.8 — **Auto metadata-driven filters landed.** New `declared_metadata_keys(l2_instance)` walks `union(instance.rails[*].metadata_keys)` and returns a sorted distinct list. New `build_metadata_dropdown_dataset(cfg, l2_instance, key)` emits a tiny `SELECT DISTINCT JSON_VALUE(metadata, '$.<key>') AS value FROM <prefix>_current_transactions WHERE ... IS NOT NULL ORDER BY value` (static JSONPath per the no-JSONB constraint, NULLs filtered, sorted output). New `metadata_dropdown_ds_id(key)` slugifies the key (lowercased, non-alphanumerics → '-') for safe IDs (`l2ft-meta-<slug>-ds`). New `metadata_param_name(key)` produces the analysis-level parameter name (`pL2ftMeta_<key>`). `build_all_l2_flow_tracing_datasets` extends the list with one dropdown source per declared key. `_l2ft_datasets`'s `visual_ids` list extends in lockstep so the tree-Datasets dict has refs for every dataset. **Sheet wiring**: new `_wire_metadata_dropdowns` declares one `StringParam` (multi-valued) per key on the analysis (universal — any sheet's visuals can read it via FilterGroup) + one `ParameterDropdown` widget per key on the L2 Exceptions sheet only. **Design call documented inline**: with ~30 metadata keys for sasquatch_pr, fanning controls onto every sheet creates UI clutter (~120 controls) — controls live on the L2 Exceptions tab where filtering is most useful, parameters stay analysis-level so M.3.8b can wire visual filtering. Visual filter wiring deferred — most current datasets are aggregates that don't carry per-metadata-key columns; pushing filters through would require extending each dataset's SQL with CalcField-style projections (M.3.8b candidate). **Tests** (10 new): `declared_metadata_keys` returns sorted union; per-key dataset builders + ID slugification + DISTINCT JSON_VALUE SQL shape + L2 prefix; one StringParam per key; one dropdown per key on L2 Exceptions only (other sheets have zero controls); titles read 'Metadata: <key>'; LinkedValues source per-key dataset's `value` column; empty-metadata-keys L2 path produces zero controls + zero parameters; counts scale per-instance (sasquatch_pr 28, spec_example 5). Updated invariant: dataset count is now `8 + N` where N = metadata keys per instance. Full suite: 1317 passed (was 1307) + 216 skipped.

The current Rails tab is a passive declared-rails table; user wants an interactive transactions explorer with date range + rail + status + bundle filters at the top, plus a cascading metadata key→value filter. The cascade requires QS dataset parameters substituted into CustomSQL — a primitive the codebase didn't yet have. Two hand-spike tests (M.3.10c spike-1 single, spike-2 multi) verified `<<$paramName>>` substitution works for both `SINGLE_VALUED` and `MULTI_VALUED` parameters, including concatenation into JSONPath strings (`JSON_VALUE(metadata, '$.' || <<$pKey>>)`) — wire shape captured in memory note `project_qs_dataset_parameters.md`.

Tree's `StringParam` / `IntegerParam` / `DateTimeParam` gain `mapped_dataset_params: list[(Dataset, str)]` field that emits `MappedDataSetParameters` on the declaration.   - [x] M.3.13 — **Captured SPEC gaps surfaced by M.3.1's hand-write.** Three new validator rules + four SPEC.md amendments. **R12** — every `TransferKey` field MUST appear in `metadata_keys` of every leg_rail (caught a real latent bug in sasquatch_pr.yaml: `InternalTransferDebit` + `InternalTransferCredit` were missing `internal_transfer_id`, so they could never legitimately reach Status=Posted; YAML fixed in the same commit). **C3** — every Variable-direction `SingleLegRail` MUST appear in some `TransferTemplate.leg_rails` (Variable closure semantics require a containing template's ExpectedNet; aggregating-bundled-only Variable rails have no closure target — kitchen YAML's `WatchlistAdjustment` was wrong-Variable, fixed to Debit). **C4** — every `xor_group` MUST have ≥2 members (single-member XOR is degenerate). SPEC.md amendments: TransferKey scope is `(template_name, transfer_key_values)` not values alone (different templates with same key names + values don't collide); TransferKey field-name validity rule documented as the new R12; **late-arriving Pending rows** semantics added to AggregatingRail bundling section — late rows wait for next bundler firing, never re-open a closed bundle (preserves L1 append-only). 8 new tests in `tests/test_l2_validate.py` (rejection + accept-edge-case for each of R12/C3/C4). Fuzzer (`tests/l2/fuzz.py`) extended with `_extend_metadata_keys` helper so generated leg_rails carry their containing template's transfer_key fields (R12 satisfaction at fuzz-build time). 3 pre-existing test fixtures (`test_c1_at_most_one_variable_leg_per_template`, `test_s2_template_leg_must_not_have_expected_net`, `test_pipeline_limit_schedule`) needed minor metadata_keys extensions to satisfy R12. Description-prose tests (`test_l2_descriptions::test_single_leg_rail_description_loads` + `_transfer_template_description_loads`) likewise. Full suite: 1377 passed (+8 from R12/C3/C4), 216 skipped, 0 failed. **Gap 4 — AggregatingRail late arrivals — chose SPEC text only**, no validator: rules like "max_unbundled_age >= cadence period" are too policy-laden (some integrators want aggressive watch alarms by intent), and the late-arrival semantics is fundamentally a runtime-behavior contract not a load-time configuration check.

    - [x] M.4.1.f — **Per-test failure triage manifest landed.** New `tests/e2e/_harness_failure_dump.py` (~190 lines) exposes `dump_failure_manifest(failure_dir, *, test_id, instance, planted_manifest, dashboard_ids=None, embed_urls=None, db_conn=None, exception_text=None) -> Path`. Output filename pattern: `<instance>_<test_id_safe>_<timestamp>.txt` (pytest's `::` / `[` / `]` / `/` rewritten to `_` for filesystem safety; ISO-8601 UTC timestamp with colons stripped). 7 sections: Test header, Seed Hash (YAML), Planted Manifest (JSON-pretty with `_decimal_safe` Decimal coercion), Deployed Dashboards (kv-aligned), Embed URLs, Matview Row Counts (one row per `_TRIAGE_DB_OBJECTS` entry — base tables, `current_*` matviews, L1 invariant matviews, todays_exceptions; renders `<error: ExcType>` + rolls back on per-query failure so subsequent queries still run), Exception text. Full unit suite: 1474 passed (+12), 233 skipped (no new e2e smoke test since the failure-dump fixture is consumed by the existing M.4.1.d/.e smoke tests, not exercised by a fresh smoke).
    - [x] M.4.1.g — **Parallelism + flake hardening landed.** **Decision**: pytest-xdist parallel (default `-n 4` from existing `run_e2e.sh --parallel` switch; `-n 3` saturates the current 3-instance `L2_INSTANCES` matrix). Per-test isolation is xdist-safe by construction — every QS resource carries a unique `TestUid` tag (M.4.1.a) and every DB object carries a unique prefix (`e2e_<instance>_<uid>`), so concurrent tests cannot collide on a shared QS account or Aurora cluster. Boto3's standard retry mode handles transient `ThrottlingException` on the ~42 `create_data_set` calls in flight when xdist=3 (14 datasets × 3 instances). **Flake hardening**: new `tests/e2e/_harness_browser.py` (~110 lines) exposes `run_dashboard_check_with_retry(qs_identity_client, *, account_id, dashboard_id, operation, page_timeout_ms, viewport, headless, max_attempts, user_arn)` — opens a deployed dashboard via freshly-generated single-use embed URL (regenerates per attempt since URLs are single-use), waits for dashboard chrome, runs `operation(page)`, retries ONCE on `playwright.sync_api.TimeoutError` (the QS spinner-forever footgun from CLAUDE.md). `AssertionError` short-circuits — real planted-row-missing failures are NOT retried (would mask regressions). Both Playwright smoke tests (`test_harness_l1_planted_scenarios_visible`, `test_harness_l2ft_planted_scenarios_visible`) now wrap their bodies in this helper instead of inline `webkit_page` blocks. **Tests**: 7 new in `tests/test_harness_browser.py` cover happy-path (one URL, no retry), AssertionError short-circuits (no retry), TimeoutError → retry-with-fresh-URL (proves second URL is different from first), TimeoutError on both attempts → propagate, `max_attempts=1` disables retry, `user_arn` threads through to QS call, `page.goto` uses generated URL. Per-test Aurora warmup (`SELECT 1`) was already wired in M.4.1.a's `harness_db_conn` fixture. **Harness docstring** updated with parallelism + flake-hardening sections so future readers don't re-derive the design. Full unit suite: 1481 passed (+7), 233 skipped.
    - [x] M.4.1.h — **Wired into `run_e2e.sh`.** New `--harness` flag — runs ONLY `tests/e2e/test_harness_end_to_end.py` and skips the production deploy + the rest of the e2e suite (the harness manages its own per-test ephemeral resources, so the production deploy is irrelevant and the rest of the e2e suite would conflict by binding to the production resource IDs). Default off (slow + AWS-touching + costs real $$); opt-in for nightly / pre-release. Composes with `--parallel N` (default 4 from the existing pytest-xdist switch; `-n 3` saturates the current `L2_INSTANCES` matrix). **Usage docstring** updated with the runtime estimate (~5–10 min × `len(L2_INSTANCES)` at xdist saturation; ~15–30 min serial) and a pointer to `tests/e2e/failures/` for triage manifests. Bash syntax check + arg-parsing smoke confirms `--harness --parallel 3` builds `pytest -n 3 tests/e2e/test_harness_end_to_end.py`. **M.4.1 chain complete** — harness ready for first AWS-side dry run.

  - [x] M.4.2a — **Closed the M.4.2 broad-mode coverage gap.** Transfer Templates sheet now populates under pure `--mode broad`. Two changes landed:
    - **Re-gated `transfer_template_plants` as a broad-mode plant** — moved from `include_l1` to `include_broad`. Pure `l1_invariants` mode now plants only the 6 SHOULD-violation kinds; `broad` and `l1_plus_broad` both get the TT firings.

The emit helper threads it into the row's `template_name` column. Result: broad rail firings of leg_rails now surface on the L2FT TT sheet alongside the structured TransferTemplatePlant firings.
    - **Re-locked**: sasquatch_pr's L1-mode YAML hash (`b02ff337…`; spec_example's L1 hash unchanged because its first leg_rail is SingleLeg → TT plant was always omitted there). All 4 broad-mode sidecar hashes re-locked (`a5a26566…` / `ab700f03…` / `3b05375c…` / `2c9a325a…`).
