Existing `test_auto_scenario_against_sasquatch_pr_covers_all_six_plant_kinds` switched to `mode='l1_plus_broad'` to pick up both layers (TT plants are now broad-layer). Full suite: 1421 passed, 223 skipped.

  - [x] M.4.2b — **YAML-driven synthetic naming polish landed.** Two opt-in YAML extensions close the synthetic-value leaks identified post-M.4.2a:
    - **`account_templates[].instance_id_template` + `instance_name_template`** — optional Python `str.format()` templates with `{role}` + `{n}` placeholders. Loader validates placeholder set (rejects unknown ones like `{customer_id}` to catch typos). Seed `_materialize_instances` renders persona-aware ids + names when set; falls back to legacy `cust-{n:03d}` + `Customer {n}` when `None` so existing fixtures don't drift.
    - **`rails[].metadata_value_examples`** — optional `dict[str, list[str]]` per-key example value lists on TwoLegRail + SingleLegRail. Loader normalizes to tuple-of-tuples for frozen-dataclass storage. Broad-mode seed picker cycles examples by firing seq when set; falls back to `<rail>-firing-<seq>` per key when absent. Mixing opt-in keys with non-opt-in works naturally (per-key fallback).
    - **Validator R13** — every key in `metadata_value_examples` MUST appear in the same rail's `metadata_keys` (typo'd example keys would silently never fire; caught at load).
    - **No hash drift** — spec_example + sasquatch_pr don't opt in to either field, so all locked hashes (YAML seed_hash + sidecar dict) preserved as-is. An integrator's persona YAML opts in for richer dashboard labels.
    - **Tests**: 13 new in `tests/test_l2_yaml_naming.py` covering loader (parses cleanly, defaults to None / empty when absent, rejects unknown placeholder, rejects non-string + empty list + non-string value), validator R13 (rejects mismatched key), and seed integration (renders both id + name templates correctly, falls back when unset, cycles metadata examples, mixes opt-in + fallback keys per-key). Full suite: 1436 passed, 221 skipped, pyright strict clean.

  - [x] M.4.4 — **`apps/payment_recon/` deleted.** Same shape as M.4.3 — bundled M.4.6's PR-test deletes + M.4.7's CLI surface scrub into the same commit (`dcb565c`) since splitting would have left a broken intermediate state. **Deleted** the entire `src/quicksight_gen/apps/payment_recon/` directory (10 files: __init__.py, _l2.py, _l2_datasets.py, app.py, constants.py, datasets.py, demo_data.py, etl_examples.py, filters.py, recon_filters.py, recon_visuals.py, visuals.py). **Deleted tests**: `tests/test_recon.py`, all 9 `tests/e2e/test_pr_*.py` files. **Trimmed** PR fixtures from `tests/e2e/conftest.py`, `tests/test_dataset_contract.py`, `tests/test_demo_data.py`, `tests/test_demo_sql.py`, `tests/test_executives.py`, `tests/test_investigation.py`. **CLI scrubbed**: `payment-recon` removed from APPS / APP_CHOICE / DEMO_APP_CHOICE; per-app subcommands + helpers + branches gone; `sasquatch-bank` preset reference dropped from `demo apply` mapping. The original M.4.4 acceptance was met by the delete; the substeps below capture follow-on work that surfaced *during* the post-delete e2e harness debug session (M.4.4.5–M.4.4.13). Several were planned (App Info canary, KPI shape match) and several were emergent from real harness runs (epochMilliseconds bug, fuzz schema NULL-cast, JS console capture, persistent L1 render xfails).
    - [x] M.4.4.5 — **App Info ("i") sheet on every dashboard.** New `common/sheets/app_info.py` helper builds a 3-visual sheet (liveness KPI via `SELECT COUNT(*) FROM information_schema.tables`, per-matview row-count table, deploy stamp text box with git short SHA + ISO timestamp) wired in as the final `analysis.add_sheet(...)` call in every shipped app. Lets the operator glance at one tab to distinguish "QS healthy, dashboard data is the issue" from "QS itself is broken" (the spinner-forever footgun). Tab originally named `i` (single char) — QS hides single-char tab names, renamed to `Info`. Tree-walker test enforces presence + structure across all apps. CLAUDE.md "Conventions" section captures the contract.
    - [x] M.4.4.6 — **Fuzz schema cast bugs.** Three matview CASE expressions (`limit_breach`, `stuck_pending`, `stuck_unbundled` in `common/l2/schema.py`) emitted bare `"NULL"` literals where the surrounding column was numeric/bigint. The `numeric > text` comparison parsed fine for the production fixtures (whose CASE branches always landed in a typed column) but the fuzz L2 hit a permutation that exercised the NULL branch. Fixed by typing every NULL: `NULL::numeric` / `NULL::bigint`. Re-locked fuzz hashes.
    - [x] M.4.4.7 — **Per-app segment in App Info DataSetIds.** Both `build_liveness_dataset` and `build_matview_status_dataset` now require an `app_segment` keyword argument that gets baked into the AWS DataSetId — `qs-gen-<l2_prefix>-<app_segment>-app-info-{liveness,matviews}-dataset` — so `deploy <single-app>` can't delete-then-create another app's App Info dataset. The tree-internal `visual_identifier` stays shared because it's analysis-internal (each app's analysis has its own `DataSetIdentifierDeclaration` mapping the shared logical name to its own ARN). Updated all 5 caller sites to pass `app_segment="l1"` / `"exec"` / `"inv"` / `"l2ft"`. New regression test (`test_no_two_apps_share_an_app_info_data_set_id`) builds all 4 app segments and asserts pairwise-disjoint AWS DataSetId sets.
    - [x] M.4.4.8 — **KPI emit shape match.** Matched `KPIOptions` to the hand-built reference: full `Comparison` + `PrimaryValueDisplayType` + `SecondaryValueFontConfiguration` + `Sparkline` + `VisualLayoutOptions` block, plus explicit empty `TargetValues=[]` + `TrendGroups=[]` fields. Without those, partial KPIOptions emission triggers QS UI rejection ("Only PrimaryValueFontSize display property can be defined when TargetValue and TrendGroup fields are empty"). KPIs now render cleanly; `KPIOptions` dataclass extended with the 4 new optional `dict[str, Any]` slots in `common/models.py`.
    - [ ] M.4.4.9 — **QS-UI kitchen-sink reference tool — DEFERRED.** Standalone tool that consumes the QS console's "view JSON" output for every visual type once and dumps it as a reference fixture, so future shape-drift between our generator and the QS UI is one diff away from being noticed. Originally born from the M.4.4.10ab debug session ("the QS docs are a pack of lies; almost every field claimed optional turns out to be required for editor compat") — but now that M.4.4.10ab/c/d landed the concrete fixes that crashed the editor, the standalone reference tool is no longer urgent. Re-prioritize when the next QS-UI shape mismatch surfaces (M.5+ as a defensive measure, or sooner if a new editor crash class shows up). Capture intentionally tooled-out so the framing isn't lost.
    - [x] M.4.4.10 — **AnalysisDefinition shape match for QS UI editor.** Stack of fixes that, together, made our generated analyses survive editor open + re-edit + new-visual-add without crashing. Diagnosed by comparing a hand-built control analysis (created via the QS console) byte-by-byte against our emit:
      - [x] M.4.4.10ab — **Top-level + sheet-level missing fields.** Added `Options` (`WeekStart`, `QBusinessInsightsStatus`, `ExcludedDataSetArns`, `CustomActionDefaults`), `AnalysisDefaults` (`DefaultNewSheetConfiguration` with `InteractiveLayoutConfiguration.Grid.CanvasSizeOptions`), and per-sheet `GridLayoutConfiguration.CanvasSizeOptions` (FIXED, 1600px). `QueryExecutionOptions` dataclass added but NOT emitted — boto3's serializer crashes mid-call on the field even though the model accepts it; QS auto-fills server-side... CORRECTION: QS does NOT auto-fill, the deployed analysis carries `null` vs `{QueryExecutionMode: AUTO}` on hand-built. Field stays in the dataclass for future use; no impact on current rendering.
      - [x] M.4.4.10c — **Auto-VisualIds use UUIDs not positional slugs.** `_helpers.auto_id(slug)` wraps every internal ID (visual_id, action_id, control_id, filter_id, filter_group_id, field_id) through `uuid5(NAMESPACE, slug)` so the QS editor sees UUID-shape IDs (which it requires) instead of human-readable slugs (which it rejects on certain edits). CalcField names stay bare-slug because they're analyst-facing.
      - [x] M.4.4.10d — **Make `DateTimeParam.default` required.** Type-encoded the epochMilliseconds bug. Without a default, QS's date picker initializes with no value and the editor crashes with `Error: epochMilliseconds must be a number, you gave: null` on open. Made `default` a required (no-default-value) field on the `DateTimeParam` dataclass so the bug class is unrepresentable at the wiring site. L1's `pL1DsBalanceDate` got a `RollingDate({"Expression": "truncDate('DD', now())"})` default; kitchen-sink + 2 tree tests updated. Per project pref "encode invariants in the type system, not validation tests".
    - [x] M.4.4.11 — **Capture JS console output in e2e canary failure manifest.** Per-attempt `page.on("console")` + `page.on("pageerror")` listeners in `_harness_browser.py` accumulate into a list; on failure (timeout OR assertion), the list is written next to the screenshot as `<dashboard_id>_attempt<n>_console.txt`. Drove the M.4.4.10d epochMilliseconds bug discovery — that error never surfaced in the QS UI but printed to the JS console. Empty-output case writes a `<no console output captured>` sentinel so the human knows capture ran (vs missing file = capture broken). 6 new unit tests in `test_harness_browser.py` cover assertion failure / timeout / sentinel / pageerror / no-screenshot-dir / clean-run-no-artifact paths.
    - [x] M.4.4.12 — **L1 render xfails root-caused; all 3 L1 tests now pass.** The persistent xfails turned out to be three stacking real bugs the wrapper was hiding:
      1. **KPI title mismatch.** Harness asserted on "Open Exceptions Today"; the L1 dashboard's KPI is titled "Open Exceptions" (the sheet name "Today's Exceptions" already carries the temporal context). Harness expectation aligned to the analyst-facing label.
      2. **`todays_exceptions` matview missing UNION branches.** Matview only UNION'd drift / ledger_drift / overdraft / limit_breach / expected_eod_balance_breach — `stuck_pending` and `stuck_unbundled` were absent even though they're L1 SHOULD-violations. Added both as UNION ALL branches with no per-day filter (currently-stuck-by-construction).
      3. **KPI assertion semantics reframe.** Switched from manifest-derived "expected = sum of SHOULD plants" to "expected = SELECT COUNT(*) FROM <prefix>_todays_exceptions". The manifest model can't account for broad-mode rail_firing plants whose legs naturally age past their rails' caps and surface in stuck_pending / stuck_unbundled. Layer 1 (matview row presence) is the integrity check; Layer 2 KPI is now strictly a render-passthrough verification.
      4. **Dynamic date-filter widening.** Hardcoded `days_back=30` was tight enough that the M.4.4.13 cap-aware plant changes pushed sasquatch_pr's stuck_unbundled plant outside it (P31D cap + 7 buffer = 38 days). Compute `days_back = max(plant["days_ago"]) + 7` across the manifest.
      Diagnostic plumbing added during the investigation (a `print(traceback)` before each `pytest.xfail()` so the underlying exception text reaches stderr) stays in place — useful for future-similar diagnoses with near-zero overhead. L1 xfail wrapper REMOVED — assertion failures now propagate as real FAILED. L2FT wrapper still in place pending its own diagnostic pass. **Verified**: harness `--parallel 3` across all 3 L2 instances → 13 passed, 2 xfailed in 6:30.
    - [x] M.4.4.15 — **L2FT KPI assertion reframe.** The previous `assert_l2_exceptions_check_types_present` required ≥1 of 6 hardcoded `check_type` category labels to surface — wrong for clean SPEC-skeleton fixtures (spec_example) where the broad-mode scenario produces ZERO L2 violations and the dataset correctly returns empty. Reframed to `assert_l2_exceptions_kpi_renders` which verifies the KPI renders any non-negative integer (proves the dataset SQL ran cleanly). Outer L2FT xfail wrapper REMOVED; inline xfail kept ONLY around `assert_l2ft_plants_visible` pending M.4.4.16 (deferred to phase N — same date-filter widening pattern as M.4.4.12 but for the L2FT dashboard). Verified: spec_example L2FT PASSES standalone; full harness at parallel=3 → 14 passed + 1 xfailed (sasquatch_pr plants-visible).
    - [ ] M.4.4.16 — **L2FT plants-visible date-filter widening — DEFERRED to phase N.** Same root-cause family as M.4.4.12's L1 dynamic widening fix. After M.4.4.15 lifted the L2 Exceptions KPI assertion, `assert_l2ft_plants_visible` hard-fails on sasquatch_pr because some planted rail firings (e.g., `MerchantPayoutCheck`) have `days_ago` > the L2FT dashboard's default date filter window. Fix shape: compute `max_days_ago` from `planted_manifest["rail_firing_plants"]`, call the L2FT-side date filter widen helper, wire into `_check_l2ft` before the assertion. Workaround in place: inline xfail just around that assertion. Acceptance: drop the inline xfail wrapper; assertion passes for all 3 L2 instances. Re-prioritize when phase N picks up the deferred M.4.5/.5/.6/.7/.8 work.
    - [x] M.4.4.14 — **Per-role business_day offsets for the fuzz matrix.** Added optional `role_business_day_offsets: dict[str, int]` to `L2Instance` (loader + validator + emit threading). When set, each role's emitted `daily_balances.business_day_start` / `_end` shifts by the role's hour offset (e.g., GL closes 5pm → 17:00→17:00 next day). Roles absent default to midnight-aligned, so production fixtures' bytes-identical seed_hash holds (zero production drift). The fuzzer (`tests/l2/fuzz.py::_build_role_business_day_offsets`) populates the map with deterministic hour samples from `{0, 5, 9, 14, 17, 23}` per role, so every fuzz instance now exercises per-role business-day variation. Two new fuzz regression tests assert every seed emits the map covering every declared role + at least one seed in 100 produces distinct offsets. Verified: 1137 unit tests pass, no production hash drift.
    - [x] M.4.4.13 — **Cap-aware days_ago for stuck_pending plant.** Root cause: `_build_stuck_pending_plants` hardcoded `days_ago=2` in `common/l2/auto_scenario.py`. Production fixtures happened to pick rails with caps under 2 days (PT4H, PT24H) so plants landed; fuzz seed `227844959` picked a Rail_00 with `max_pending_age=P7D` and the plant silently failed (matview predicate is `age_seconds > cap_seconds`). Fix: applied the same cap-aware pattern stuck_unbundled already uses — `cap_days = max(1, int(rail.max_pending_age.total_seconds() / 86400) + 7)`. Plants land comfortably past the cap regardless of the picked rail's setting. Added 2 regression tests in `test_auto_scenario.py` asserting the days_ago > cap contract directly (so future regressions trip without needing the specific fuzz seed). Re-locked all 4 affected hashes (spec_example + sasquatch_pr YAML seed_hash; same two for 'l1_plus_broad' broad-mode sidecar; 'broad' mode unchanged since no L1 plants). Updated `test_cli_seed_l2.py`'s hardcoded-old-hash assertion to a regex match (robust to future rotations).

**Sequencing rationale.** M.0 is a vertical-slice spike — same approach as Phase L's L.0 (smallest possible scope, validate the shape, cherry-pick what works into the proper library). M.1 lifts the spike's working glue into typed library code. M.2 (AR CMS) ports first because its checks are mostly L1-invariant-with-light-scoping — easier landing pad for the L2 plumbing. M.3 (PR) is the real SPEC stress test (TransferTemplates, Variable closure, XOR Chains, AggregatingRails — almost every L2 primitive in flight). M.4 cleans up the legacy apps + completes the harness coverage. **M.9 ships v6.0.0** with the L2 foundation as the headline; persona infra + CLI polish + docs/training render pipelines (originally M.5–M.8) defer to Phase N as post-v6 enhancements.

- [ ] **Phase N — Post-v6 enhancements.** Everything kicked from M.4–M.8 during the v6 ship push. Each entry below was originally scoped under M; they're collected here so v6 can ship without waiting on the persona / CLI / docs / training polish. Re-shape as needed when Phase N planning starts.

  - [ ] **N.1 — Investigation + Executives reshape decision** (was M.4.5). Not a delete by default; the question is "what shape, if any, do these need post-M.3?" Three substeps:
    - **Audit doc.** Read each app's surface fresh: what does Investigation actually answer that L1+L2FT can't? What does Executives summarize that the L1 KPI plus the L2FT exceptions don't? Capture in `docs/audits/n_1_inv_exec_audit.md`.
    - **Decision: keep / reshape / delete.** Pick one of three candidate paths: **keep** as-is (Investigation's question-shaped analysis stays untouched); **reshape onto L2** (Investigation's primitives become a third L2-fed app, e.g., `apps/l2_network_analysis/`); **delete** (no stakeholder will miss them, sweep them like M.4.3/M.4.4).
    - **Materialize chosen path.** "Keep" is no-op + docs freshness; "Reshape" is M.3-style port; "Delete" is the M.4.3/M.4.4 parallel.

Persona substitution wired so a fresh `quicksight-gen generate config demo > sasquatch.yaml` produces a runnable bundle. Handbook prose templated against L2 persona vocabulary. mkdocs render step that takes `(L2 instance, neutral templates) → rendered handbook`. Replaces today's `mapping.yaml` substitution. The deferred L.5 "always-emitted persona leaks" cleanup happens here naturally. **Per F12:** any sub-step that invokes ScreenshotHarness MUST run a DB warm-up `SELECT 1` against `cfg.demo_database_url` right before fetching the embed URL — Aurora Serverless cold-start otherwise surfaces as QS's generic "We can't open that dashboard" error.
    - **Major Idea**: add a sheet at the end of each dashboard and load the documentation into the dashboard itself.
    - **L2 topology diagram render** (deferred from M.3.10d). The L2 instance is a graph; render as SVG via Graphviz `dot` (hierarchical) or `neato`/`sfdp` (force-directed) and embed in the handbook. Three plausible cuts: account-rail-account topology, chain DAG, layered combination. **Out of scope** (deferred per SPEC.md "Deliberately not in v1"):

The control card is found and clicked, but the MUI listbox popover never resolves under the expected selector.

Likely a QuickSight UI change pushed the listbox out of the `data-automation-context`-scoped popover, breaking the first half of the selector union — the `[role="listbox"] [role="option"]` fallback may be matching a stale popover from a different control.
  - Same dropdown helper works for AR (Today's Exceptions multi-selects) — comparing the two pages' DOM should isolate what's PR-specific.
  - Acceptance: all 5 pass three runs in a row at `--parallel 4`. Try fixing as part of L.4 (PR port); if the structural pattern doesn't naturally refactor away, leave here.

## Tech Debt
- Are there more invariants that are better encoded into the type system? K.2 did this for drill-param shape compatibility (`common/drill.py`: `ColumnShape` + `DrillParam` + `DrillSourceField` + `cross_sheet_drill()` refuse mismatched wirings at construction time) and codified the rule in `CLAUDE.md`. Phase L's tree primitives close another big chunk by encoding parent-child structure and cross-reference shape; what remains after L is the candidate list for the next round.

### QuickSight URL-parameter control sync — known platform limitation (do not re-attempt without new evidence)

**The defect.** When a QuickSight dashboard URL sets a parameter via the fragment (`#p.<param>=<value>`), QS applies the value to the parameter store (visuals filter, "Reset" eventually shows blue after a hard refresh) but **does not push the value into the on-screen parameter / filter controls** bound to that parameter. The control widgets keep showing "All" even though data is filtered. Same defect affects QS's own intra-product Navigation Action with parameters — confirmed in [re:Post Q&A](https://repost.aws/questions/QUPWsGyb8wRNS8lojxfhkJmA/quicksight-navigation-action-with-parameters-doesn-t-update-the-controls-in-the-new-tab) and the [QuickSight community thread](https://community.amazonquicksight.com/t/values-of-filter-list-added-to-sheet-are-not-getting-updates-dynamically-based-on-parameter-passed-in-url/15355). AWS's own [parameters-in-a-URL doc](https://docs.aws.amazon.com/quick/latest/userguide/parameters-in-a-url.html) doesn't address it.

**Why we care.** A drill where filtered data and visible controls disagree is a non-user-obvious error that reduces analyst trust — worse than no drill. K.4.7 dropped its three Investigation → AR cross-app drills for this reason.

**Re-entry conditions** — re-attempt cross-app URL drills only if one of these flips:
1. AWS ships a fix (check the re:Post / community threads above; QS release notes for "URL parameter" or "navigation action" entries).
2. We re-architect to a custom embedded app and use the embedding SDK's `setParameters()` API, which DOES sync controls. Big scope; only justified if cross-app drilling becomes a load-bearing UX pattern across multiple personas.
3. Someone discovers a URL form / fragment syntax that triggers control sync. Low probability — the docs are silent and the existing form is well-trodden.

**Reuse for new URL features.** The dropped K.4.7 code (`CustomActionURLOperation` model, `cross_app_drill()` helper, `URLSourceColumn` + `url_column()`, `_build_url_template()`) is in git history at the commit prior to the K.4.7 revert — recoverable for any future static-link or non-parameterized URL action. **Don't** rebuild for a parameterized cross-app drill without one of the re-entry conditions above.

### Cross-app dataset prune drops sibling app's non-default-L2 datasets

**The defect.** When two L2-fed apps (currently `l1-dashboard` + `l2-flow-tracing`) deploy against the same non-default L2 instance (e.g., `sasquatch_pr`), running `quicksight-gen generate` for one app causes its `_prune_stale_files` step to delete the other app's already-generated dataset JSONs. Surfaced during M.3.10's first deploy attempt: generating l1-dashboard against sasquatch_pr left 14 sasquatch_pr L1 dataset files; then generating l2-flow-tracing against sasquatch_pr pruned all 14 L1 files (kept only its own 36) — and vice versa.

**Root cause.** `cli.py::_all_dataset_filenames(cfg, keep_current=...)` builds the keep-list by calling each sibling app's `build_all_*_datasets(cfg, default_l2_instance())` to enumerate filenames. Sibling apps always use the **default** L2 instance (`spec_example`), not whatever instance the *current* generate is targeting. So when the current generate is against `sasquatch_pr`, the keep-list contains:
- Current app's sasquatch_pr-prefixed datasets (correct)
- Sibling apps' spec_example-prefixed datasets (wrong — should be sasquatch_pr-prefixed)

Anything not in the keep-list gets pruned. The previous-generate's sasquatch_pr-prefixed dataset files don't appear in any sibling's enumeration → deleted.

**Workaround used at M.3.10.** Skip the CLI; write JSON directly via Python (build both apps in one process, write all datasets, no prune). One-off — not a sustained workflow.

**Fix candidates.**
1. Thread the L2 instance through `_all_dataset_filenames(cfg, l2_instance, *, keep_current=...)` so sibling apps enumerate against the same instance the current generate is using. Cleanest, but assumes all L2-fed apps in a given deploy share one L2 instance.
2. Make `_all_dataset_filenames` enumerate against EVERY known L2 instance (walk `tests/l2/*.yaml`?). Robust but costly (rebuilds every dataset list × N instances per generate).
3. Replace the union-keep prune with a per-app-prefix prune: each app only prunes files matching its own URL stem (`l1-*`, `l2ft-*`). Keeps cross-app concerns separated.

Recommended: option 3 — each app's prune only touches files it could plausibly have written. Cross-app contamination becomes structurally impossible.

---

# PLAN — Y.2.gate: Test layer chain audit + runner [shipped v8.8.0a6 / a17 / a19 / a20]

**Why.** Y.2.b shipped a SQL bug the e2e suite let through — the dataset-SQL smoke verifier was a CLI script, not pytest-collected, so a deployed `UndefinedColumn` exception got past API + browser e2e. We patched that one gap (`tests/e2e/test_dataset_sql_smoke.py`), but the broader concern stood: nothing chained the test layers cheap→expensive, so each layer needed manual invocation and we'd forget. Y.2.gate built that chain runner.

**What shipped — the runner** (`src/quicksight_gen/_dev/runner.py`, surfaced via `./run_tests.sh`):

- **Layered chain**: `unit → db → app2 → deploy → api → browser` (pyright folds into `unit` via the conftest sessionstart gate). `./run_tests.sh up_to=<layer>` runs the chain through that layer, stop-on-first-failure; per-layer artifacts (`cmd.json` / `stdout.log` / `stderr.log` / `timings.json`) land under `runs/<utc-ts>-<short-sha>/<variant>/<layer>/`.
- **Variant matrix** (m.0–m.5, v8.8.0a6): 3-axis `scenario × dialect × target` cells. Scenarios `sp` (spec_example) / `sq` (sasquatch_pr) / `fuzz[:N]` (random synthesized L2 yaml, deterministic per seed) / `us:<path>`. Dialects `pg` / `or` / `sl`. Targets `lo` (local container or sqlite tempfile) / `aw` (operator's external Aurora / Oracle). No flags = full 13-cell matrix; `--scenarios` / `--dialects` / `--targets` sub-flags compose multiplicatively; `--variants=<code>` pins a single cell for triage; `sl × aw` auto-skips. `common/variant.py` carries `VariantSpec` + `compose_matrix`. Hard-cut the legacy `local-pg` / `local-oracle` / `local-sqlite` / `default` names.
- **Unit-as-prelude** (n, v8.8.0a19): the `unit` layer is variant-independent → it runs ONCE per invocation as a prelude (`runs/<id>/_prelude/unit/`), not once per matrix cell. `up_to=unit` runs just the prelude; `>= db` runs the prelude first then fans the matrix out at `db`; a prelude failure aborts before any cell dispatches.
- **CI parity** (k, v8.8.0a14–a20): `ci.yml` / `e2e.yml` test jobs are thin `./run_tests.sh up_to=<layer>` wrappers (`QS_GEN_RUNNER_CI=1` skips Docker spin-up when the GHA service container / Aurora is the DB); per-event cost tiers (PR = PG-only `up_to=db`; push:main = PG+Oracle `up_to=db`; nightly cron = AW-touching matrix sweep); pre-push git hook (`git config core.hooksPath .githooks` → `up_to=db --dialects=pg --targets=lo` ~30s); failure-surface parity (same artifact set + exit codes locally and in CI). `k.1.coverage` (v8.8.0a20): `--coverage` flag → per-(variant, layer) `.coverage.<variant>.<layer>` data files; `ci.yml::integration-pg` emits + uploads `coverage-data-pg-runner`; the existing `coverage` aggregator picks them up (W.8b unchanged).
- **Cfg-driven auth** (h+i): `run/config.<dialect>.yaml`'s optional `auth:` block — `aws_profile` injected into every layer subprocess; `QS_E2E_USER_ARN` auto-derived via STS+ListUsers; no `export`-then-run dance, no `aws sso login` in the loop (recommended local dev = a long-lived `quicksight-gen-local` IAM user). Cfg precedence + env-override + loud-fail-on-missing (h.2–h.5). Pre-dispatch probes (l.3) — creds / Docker / `QS_E2E_USER_ARN` / RDS-status checked before container spin-up, refuse with `EXIT_NEEDS_OPERATOR=2` + actionable message.
- **Perf + iteration knobs** (j): Oracle container name-cached + reused across runs; within-layer pytest-xdist `-n auto` by default (`--parallel=N` override); `--only=<expr>` narrows every layer's `pytest -k`; `--skip-cheap` skips the cheap layers if green for the current SHA earlier in the session; per-run `timings.json` + `hashes.json` drift detection (±50% → ⚠), top-queries dump per cell.
- **Ephemeral AWS infra** (l): CI start/stop on every AWS-touching job; runner `up local|aws|all` / `down [local|aws]` / `status [--cost]` on cfg-declared `aws_pg_cluster_id` / `aws_oracle_instance_id`; `l.7` (v8.8.0a19) — `.github/actions/ensure-rds-available` composite action fixes the cold-RDS-start race (only `start-db-*` when truly `stopped`; waits out all transitional states); `l.8` (v8.8.0a20) — `release.yml::e2e-against-testpypi` moved to its own concurrency group `e2e-pg-release` (was the shared `e2e-pg` → the release-e2e gate kept getting *evicted* as the older pending run when a push:main `e2e-pg-api` entered the group, which left v8.8.0a18 + a19 on TestPyPI but not PyPI) + a synthesized per-release L2 instance (disjoint `rel_<tag>_*` tables) + a "last one stops the cluster" guard so the now-possible concurrent runs don't collide.
- **Docs + invariants**: CLAUDE.md's `Test sequencing + git hooks` section ("never invoke `pytest tests/e2e/` directly for layered work" — the Y.2.b SQL bug is the cost example); memory `feedback_test_layer_chain.md`; the dispatch-table cross-check unit tests against `docs/audits/y_2_gate_test_layer_chain_audit.md`; a synthetic-regression audit (`docs/audits/y_2_gate_e_synthetic_regression.md`) verifying each planted bug class halts at the right layer; `b.15` typed `EnvVar` registry + a custom AST-lint suite (`_dev` linters: EnvVar-bypass, bare-str IDs, explicit `Any`, module-level `random.X()` in seed modules, `boto3.client` outside wrappers, hardcoded `qs-gen-` prefix, `datetime.now()` in determinism-sensitive modules, `time.sleep` in `tests/e2e/`, `@dataclass` shape in `common/tree/`, `json.dumps` without `indent=2`, `boto3 create_*` without `Tags=`).

**Sub-items** (a–o, all `[x]`): a (audit doc) · b (runner substrate + CI artifact wiring) · c (L2FT Rails dataset-SQL pushdown) · d (CLAUDE.md + memory test-sequencing rule) · e (synthetic regression) · f (scripts/ + harness fold-or-delete audit) · h+i (cfg-driven auth) · j (perf + iteration knobs) · k (CI parity, incl. k.1.coverage) · l (ephemeral AWS, incl. l.7 cold-RDS + l.8 release-concurrency) · m (variant matrix) · n (unit-as-prelude) · o (terminal "Y.2.c+ unblocked" gate). The literal `k.1` "push:main + PR cells run `up_to=browser variants=full`" was superseded by `k.3`'s cost-tiering + the thin-wrapper migration. The m.4 follow-up "App2 Oracle column-casing bug" was confirmed already fixed by `Y.3.f.alt`.

**Pointers for the gory detail**: `docs/audits/y_2_gate_*.md` (audit doc, runner-CI-mode spike, AWS-provisioning runbook, synthetic-regression); `RELEASE_NOTES.md` v8.8.0a6 / a17 / a19 / a20; PLAN.md @ `a7cf58f` (the verbatim a–o checklist before this sweep); the runner `--help` epilog.

---

# PLAN — Phase Y: SQL-level parameter pushdown (QuickSight + App2 convergence) [shipped v8.8.0a2…a27 → v9.0.0 → v9.0.1]

**Why.** Two implementations of one filter intent. QuickSight ran every visual as a parameter-blind Direct Query — pulled the whole dataset-SQL result set, narrowed in QS's process via analysis-level `FilterGroup`s + calc fields; DB indexes never applied to the analyst's slider, and a growing matview shipped in full per visual. App2 (built database-native) used `:param` binds that pruned at SQL-execute time. They drifted; QS paid a perf tax that only grew.

**The shift.** The dataset SQL becomes the single source of truth for filter intent: `<<$paramName>>` substitution (literal at query time via `MappedDataSetParameters` for QS) / `:param_<name>` binds (one-line preprocessor in App2's `_sql_executor`); `{date_filter}` slot for the universal date range (`build_dataset(sql_template, CONTRACT, ..., app2_date_column="t.col")` does both substitutions). Analysis-level `FilterGroup`s deprecated for filter intent (kept only for the universal date `TimeRangeFilter` and the rare highlight-without-narrowing case). Calc fields that existed only to be filtered (Recipient Fanout `distinct_senders`, Account Network counterparty/inbound/outbound, Volume Anomalies z-score) pushed down to real dataset columns; the calc-field declarations dropped — the Investigation analysis tree now emits zero CalcFields.

**What shipped:**

- **Y.1 — spike** (Volume Anomalies σ slider, PG): proved the QS substitution + App2 bind round-trip. Surfaced the `SELECTED_VISUALS`-scope wrinkle → the **companion-dataset pattern**: visuals that must stay unfiltered point at a second dataset wrapping the same matview *without* the parameter (the σ distribution chart; later reused for Money Trail's chain-root dropdown, Account Network's anchor dropdown, L1's `account_id`/`transfer_id` data-value dropdowns, Executives' Active Accounts split). Live PG receipts: ~10× latency drop, ~48× fewer rows on the wire for the Table visual, ~6213× for the KPI COUNT(*). Y.1.k/p/q: the **cross-app-drill-into-a-dataset-bridged-param cascade does NOT work** — `MappedDataSetParameters` bridges fire only on manual widget interaction, not on URL-driven initial load (three reference shapes tried, all reverted; quirks-log entry 2.1 rewritten). K.4.7's dropped cross-app drills that target dataset-bridged params stay dropped; the L2FT metadata cascade stays on its OR-cascade WHERE (works under manual interaction; URL load = unfiltered universe — accepted UX cost). Y.1.m: type-system enforcement (`ParameterTextField.__post_init__` rejects `multi_valued=True`) — caught the 3 L2FT offenders that the X.1.b dropdown→text-field swap left mis-flagged.
- **Y.2 — sweep simple-filter datasets**: dataset-SQL pushdown across every sheet with pushdownable filters — Money Trail / Account Network / L2FT Rails+Chains+Transfer-Templates (multi-valued `IN (<<$p>>)`), the L1 universal date range (Y.2.f, dual-SQL `{date_filter}` pattern across 8 datasets), the ~22 L1 per-sheet categorical dropdowns (Y.2.g — fixed the X.1.g cold-fetch footgun *and* the pushdown together; enum columns via `StaticValues`, data-value columns via 3 new companion datasets `<prefix>_l1_accounts`/`_l1_tx_ids`/`_l1_tx_facets`), Executives Active Accounts dataset split (Y.2.h). App2 parity: `apply_dataset_param_defaults` (a fresh App2 page matches QS's initial-load render) + `expand_multivalued_dataset_params` (2+ URL values → `:param_pX_n` IN-bind expansion, never string-spliced); L2FT became the 4th app on the generic tree-fetcher path with auto-rendered MULTI_SELECT filter forms; `tests/e2e/test_dataset_sql_smoke.py` (the Y.2.b deployed-SQL-exception verifier, now pytest-collected).
- **Y.2.gate — test layer chain runner** (`./run_tests.sh` / `src/quicksight_gen/_dev/runner.py`): the hard prereq — `unit → db → app2 → deploy → api → browser`, variant matrix `scenario × dialect × target`, unit-as-prelude, cfg-driven auth, ephemeral AWS lifecycle, pre-dispatch probes, per-run timings/hashes drift, CI thin-wrapper parity, pre-push git hook, `b.15` typed `EnvVar` registry + AST-lint suite. **Full detail: the `# PLAN — Y.2.gate` section above** + `docs/audits/y_2_gate_*.md` + RELEASE_NOTES v8.8.0a6/a17/a19/a20.
- **Y.3 — calc fields → real dataset columns**: Recipient Fanout `distinct_senders` window column (`COUNT(DISTINCT ...) OVER (PARTITION BY recipient)` in a CTE; threshold pushed via `<<$pInvFanoutThreshold>>`); Account Network `is_inbound_edge`/`is_outbound_edge`/`counterparty_display` CASE columns over `<<$pInvANetworkAnchor>>`; Volume Anomalies — no-op (no CalcFields). Y.3.f (drop `_oracle_lowercase_alias_wrapper`, emit dialect-natural identifier case from the generator) **parked** — Oracle's analysis-side validation is case-sensitive against `Dataset.Columns`, so dropping the wrapper means case-folding ~30+ analysis-side column refs, out of scope; the actual App2 Oracle column-casing bug (m.5.d) was fixed narrowly by **Y.3.f.alt** (`wrap_for_visual` quotes column refs → quoted-lowercase aliases match on Oracle/PG, SQLite is case-insensitive anyway). Residual carried to PLAN.md tech-debt. Y.3.g spike (SQLAlchemy Core / sqlglot): **decision = stay on strings + helpers** (sqlglot's Oracle JSON path emits the nonexistent `JSON_EXTRACT`; SA Core costs ~50 lines/dataset vs ~20; neither moves the needle on case bridging — `spike/y3g/findings.md`).
- **Y.4 — test sweep** (re-locks happened with each Y.2/Y.3 touch; App2 preprocessor unit-covered) · **Y.5 — App2 cleanup** (`app2_sql=` → typed `app2_date_column=`; `app2_param_eq/gte/lte` + `app2_anchor_filter` dropped; `common/sql/app2_filters.py` shrunk to `app2_date_filter` only) · **Y.6 — perf verification** (methodology: run every dataset's registered SQL directly against seeded Aurora PG, wide-open ≡ pre-Y vs narrow-7d; **−15.3% rows on the wire / −8.5% query time** overall across 36 datasets in 4 apps; `l1-transactions-ds` −92% rows / −74% time; 9 datasets ≥80% row reduction; `runs/y6/summary.md`) · **Y.7 — e2e clean on PG + SQLite + Oracle** (the merge gate; Y.7-followup: Oracle browser layer — `drop_matview_if_exists` hardened against half-dropped matviews + orphan container tables, `xdist_group` on the audit-agreement re-seed fixture so Oracle's auto-committing DDL doesn't race ORA-00955, 60s browser-layer `QS_E2E_PAGE_TIMEOUT` + `pytest-rerunfailures --reruns 2` so a QS-embed-render flake auto-retries inside the same pytest invocation) · **Y.8 — Phase X rebase** obviated (Phase Y landed on `main` piecemeal; the `phase-x-2-g-investigation-app2` branch's content re-done convergently on main; branch deleted) · **Y.9 — docs sweep** (CLAUDE.md `## Filter authoring — SQL-level parameter pushdown is the canonical pattern`; README "Add a filter" rewrite; `docs/handbook/customization.md` "How filters work" + migration note) · **Y.10 — v9.0.0** (major: customer-facing artifacts — CLI / config.yaml / L2 YAML — unchanged, but the internal filter architecture is a clean break).

**v9.0.1 fast-follow** — v9.0.0's release pipeline died at the Tests job: `tests/audit/test_dashboard_extract.py`'s module-level `os.environ.setdefault("QS_GEN_DATASOURCE_ARN", ...)` leaked into `load_config`'s env-override path in a full-suite run, flipping the new `Config.datasource_arn_was_derived` gate (the "explicit `datasource_arn` wins — don't regenerate the QS datasource even when `demo_database_url` is also set" change, V.1.a) to `False`, so the auto-emit-`out/datasource.json` test failed. Fixed by `delenv`-ing the fallback up front in that test (sibling-test pattern); v9.0.0 stays a phantom (never reached PyPI), v9.0.1 = v9.0.0 content + the one-line test fix.

**Pointers for the gory detail**: RELEASE_NOTES.md v8.8.0a2 … v8.8.0a27 / v9.0.0 / v9.0.1 (per-release narrative); the `# PLAN — Y.2.gate` section above (the runner); `docs/reference/quicksight-quirks.md` entry 2.1 (the URL-param-doesn't-wake-the-bridge limitation); `spike/y3g/findings.md` (SQL-builder spike); `runs/y6/summary.md` (perf table); PLAN.md @ `e67f18e` (the verbatim Y.1–Y.10 checklist before this sweep). The CLI-shape revisit (`Q.6` — cfg ⇄ L2 dual-yaml factoring, surfaced during Y.2.gate.h.6) was moved out to Phase Q and stays open in PLAN.md.

---

# PLAN — Phase X.2: App 2 — self-hosted dashboard renderer (QuickSight as one dialect, not THE frontend)

*Shipped v9.0.0 → v9.3.0 (2026-05). Swept from `PLAN.md` at phase close; the as-built detail (sub-task notes, decisions, the X.2.q/r/s/t/u sub-phases) is below as it stood at v9.3.0. Per-release narratives: `RELEASE_NOTES.md` v9.0.x → v9.3.0.*

### X.2 — App 2: self-hosted dashboard renderer (QuickSight as one dialect, not THE frontend)

**Reframe.** Same way `Dialect.POSTGRES`/`ORACLE` are SQL dialects projected from one schema model, the dashboard tree (`common/tree/`) becomes a **dashboard model** with three renderers: QuickSight JSON (today), audit PDF (today, proves the pattern works), and a self-hosted HTML renderer (this phase). The tree's job description sharpens — it IS the dashboard, not a description of QS dashboards.

**Stack** (all proven via spike): Python backend (Starlette) + HTMX + Tailwind v4 (via `pytailwindcss` standalone CLI) + d3 from CDN. No bundler, no TS, no npm. Read-only surface, no auth in X.2 (auth deferred to backlog).

**Browser support.** Modern evergreens only — Chrome / Edge / Firefox / Safari, current minus 2 versions. No IE, no legacy mobile webview support. The HTMX + d3 + Tailwind v4 stack we're building on doesn't push beyond standard ES6 / modern SVG / CSS variables, so this is essentially "browsers people actually use today" — no exotic features being demanded.

**Why it's worth building (not just an annoyed diversion):**
- **RESTful filtering as the killer USP.** Every (sheet, filter-set) is a bookmarkable URL — "click this URL to see what I saw on May 5 at 3pm." QS embed URLs are signed, single-use, don't carry filter state. Pairs with the audit PDF — both become reproducible-view artifacts.
- **Server-side cache keys are trivial.** `(sheet, filter-set)` → SQL result. URL == cache key. SPICE-equivalent for the Python backend, with edge / browser caching free via Cache-Control.
- **Bypasses the QS quirks log entirely.** URL parameter sync, dropdown click-target weirdness, spinner-forever footgun, render flakes — none of these surface for the HTMX dialect.
- **No QS per-user license fees.** Real cost story for customers.
- **Same e2e harness gates both dialects.** Layer 1 (matview check) is renderer-agnostic; Layer 2 swaps the driver. Bug-parity falls out of the harness shape already in place.

**Hard parts (still real, but smaller post-spike):**
- **Sheet count + visual richness.** L1 dashboard alone is 11 sheets × 5–15 visuals each. Each app's surface needs the full visual catalog wired (KPI / Table / BarChart / LineChart / Sankey + filters).
- **Embedding context.** QS dashboards embed via signed URLs; HTMX dialect needs its own iframe story when phase.2 lands. Out of scope here.
- **Maintenance.** Two render implementations of the same surface — Layer 2 e2e parity (the dialect-comparison gate) is what keeps them honest.

**Spike sequence — proven on `phase-x-2-htmx-renderer` branch (Apr-May 2026):**

- [x] **X.2.spike.1** — `emit_html(app, sheet)` projects tree → HTML. Pure projection, takes in-memory tree node, never touches disk. spike.1.fix promoted `App._resolve_auto_ids` to public + threaded App through `emit_html` so `data-visual-id` attributes resolve before render.
- [x] **X.2.spike.2** — Starlette server + HTMX swap + d3 hydration on swapped fragments. Pluggable `DataFetcher` callable so spike tests stay DB-free. `python -m quicksight_gen.common.html` is the smoke runner.
- [x] **X.2.spike.3** — Layer 2 (Playwright + WebKit) against the local Starlette server. Positive case asserts SVG rect/path counts match Layer 1 fetcher's promise; negative case (route-intercepted empty body) catches the regression class. Same shape as the QS harness's Layer 2, different selectors. Dialect-comparison thesis proven.
- [x] **X.2 capability experiments** — clickable Sankey via d3 + `htmx.ajax` (anchor click pattern), dev-log + HTMX event forwarder, Tailwind v4 CSS via pytailwindcss CLI (styles HTML + d3 SVG), ForceGraph visual via d3-force (proves new visual kinds add as one `case` arm + one render function).

Architecture decisions captured in `docs/x_2_design_thoughts.md` (App 1 vs App 2 split, all-GET REST surface, plural nouns + nested resource paths, query-param state, cascade-rename via `HX-Trigger`, force-directed as shared primitive across three surfaces).

**Test matrix expansion (X.2 + X.3 woven together).** As renderers + DB backends multiply, the regression surface multiplies. The matrix that needs to stay green to call this "parity":

|                 | Postgres | Oracle | SQLite (X.3) |
|-----------------|----------|--------|--------------|
| **Layer 1** (matview check, renderer-agnostic — `_layer1_query.py`) | ✓ today | ✓ today | ✓ X.3.g.1 |
| **L2 QS JSON dialect** | ✓ today (`e2e-pg-api/browser`) | ✓ today (`e2e-oracle-api`) | N/A — QS doesn't read SQLite |
| **L2 Audit PDF dialect** | ✓ today (`tests/audit/`) | ✓ today | ✓ X.3.g.2 |
| **L2 HTMX dialect (this phase)** | X.2.h | X.2.h | X.3.g |
| **Cross-tool agreement** (U.8.b becomes 4-way: `expected == PDF == QS == HTMX`) | X.2.j | X.2.j | X.3.g |

Eight cells worth gating on (3 renderers × 3 DBs minus QS-on-SQLite). Five exist today; X.2.h adds two (HTMX × {PG, Oracle}); X.3.g adds three (Layer 1 + Audit PDF + HTMX, all on SQLite); X.2.j wraps it with the 4-way agreement contract that catches "all the renderers passed but they disagreed." Cost shape (which cells need AWS, which run on Docker / locally) lives in X.7.

**Parity-as-much-as-possible principle.** Some cells are physically unsupportable — QS×SQLite is the obvious one (QuickSight can't read SQLite; no native datasource type for it). Future combos may surface similar gaps (e.g. a renderer that doesn't support a particular visual kind, a DB feature missing on one dialect). When that happens: mark the cell N/A in the matrix with a one-line reason, run every other combination in the row + column. The principle is parity wherever the combination is technically possible — not parity everywhere, regardless of physics.

**Theme parity — its own 4-way test.** Distinct concern from data parity. The L2 YAML's `theme:` block (`common/l2/theme.py::ThemePreset`) is the single source of truth for accent / primary_fg / link_tint / etc. Today QS dashboards, audit PDF, and the docs site all consume it (Phase U.1 cover, v8.6.10 docs CSS injection). App 2 (X.2) currently uses hardcoded Tailwind classes — needs to consume the same theme. Once it does, the four visual surfaces below should render the same accent for the same theme spec:

| Surface | Status |
|---------|--------|
| QS dashboard | ✓ today (`build_theme(cfg, theme)` → QS Theme JSON) |
| Audit PDF | ✓ today (Phase U.1 cover) |
| Docs site | ✓ today (v8.6.10 CSS injection) |
| App 2 HTMX | X.2.l |

Test: change one accent value in the L2 YAML, all four surfaces shift in lockstep. Becomes a release-gate visual smoke (one screenshot per surface; pixel-diff or eyeball — eyeball acceptable since the gate is "do they all match the spec," not "are they pixel-identical").

**Scope to feature parity + e2e tests passing:**

- [ ] **X.2.a — Architecture cleanup post-spike.** Promote the experimental code into the phase shape:
  - Lift `tests/spike/test_html_layer2.py` → `tests/e2e/_harness_html2.py` (Layer 2 against HTMX dialect, fixture pattern matches the QS harness).
  - Replace the smoke runner's stub fetcher with a real DB-backed `DataFetcher` factory; keep the stub callable for unit tests.
  - Move the `python -m quicksight_gen.common.html` entry point under a Click subcommand (`quicksight-gen serve` group: `app2 apply`, mirroring the existing `schema | data | json | docs | audit` shape).
  - Branch consolidation pass — squash / rebase the spike experiments before further work, get the diff reviewable.
  - **JS tooling — same standalone-binary pattern as pytailwindcss:** add `biome` (Rust binary, single executable — replaces eslint + prettier + a minifier) via `biome-py` on PyPI or a 30-line downloader if no current wrapper. Adds to `[dev]` extras. CI step: `biome lint` + `biome check --write` (format) + `biome --apply --write --max-diagnostics=0` to gate merges. Minify in the build pipeline alongside the tailwindcss build. **JS unit tests:** extend the existing Playwright pattern — small HTML fixtures under `tests/js/` load the function under test in a real browser context, exercise it, write results to `window.__test_result` for Playwright to assert on. No jest / vitest / Node dependency. Trade-off: each test costs ~50ms Playwright launch overhead; we accept that because the JS is DOM/HTMX-coupled enough that real-browser tests catch the right class of bugs.

- [ ] **X.2.b — All-GET REST surface per design doc.** Drop `POST /visual/{id}/data`. New routes (plural nouns, nested resources):
  - `GET /` — landing page, lists `/dashboards`.
  - `GET /dashboards` — fixed list of the four apps for the served L2 instance (L1 Dashboard + L2 Flow Tracing + Investigation + Executives). One App 2 process serves one L2 instance — multi-tenancy is the auth use case (deferred to phase.2).
  - `GET /dashboards/:id` — redirect to first sheet OR render dashboard chrome + first sheet inline.
  - `GET /dashboards/:id/sheets/:id` — full sheet content.
  - `GET /dashboards/:id/sheets/:id/visuals/:id` — single visual (with chart data inline). Filter values via query string.
  - Bookmarkability: `hx-push-url="true"` on every swap so URL stays in sync with filter / sort / page state. Browser back/forward replays.
  - Cache-Control headers on data routes (Money Trail data scoped to a date range becomes cacheable per-tuple).
  - `POST /log` (dev-only) is the only POST that survives — for the dev-log forwarder.

- [ ] **X.2.c — d3 renderers for the remaining visual primitives.** Currently Sankey + ForceGraph proven. Add one `case` arm + one `renderXxx` JS function each:
  - **KPI** — a single number + delta arrow. ~10 lines of d3 (mostly text styling).
  - **Table** — `<table>` with sortable headers (each `<th>` is a link to `?sort_column=col:desc`). Pagination via `?page_offset=N&page_size=50`. Tailwind classes for striped rows + sticky header.
    - Comment: for the pagination, a big win over quicksight would be to give a total row count with the pagination (prefer 0-50 of x over page 1 of xx). this will make the e2e testing way easier
  - **BarChart** — d3 bars with axis labels (the plain-English ones added in v8.5.5 carry over via the tree).
  - **LineChart** — d3 line + axes + legend.
  - Per-renderer Layer 2 unit test: stub fetcher, assert SVG / DOM shape matches Layer 1 promise (rect counts, path counts, etc.).

- [x] **X.2.d — Filter primitives wired.** Currently date range form. Add:
  - **ParameterDropdown** — `<select>` driven by L2 / dataset values; change fires a swap with the new value in `?param_<name>=...`.
  - **CategoryFilter** — multi-select check group; change fires `?filter_<col>=v1,v2,v3`.
  - **NumericRange** — two inputs or slider; fires `?min_<col>=N&max_<col>=M`.
  - All values flow into URL query params per X.2.b. No form state.
  - **Status:** `ParameterDropdownSpec` / `CategoryFilterSpec` / `NumericRangeSpec` frozen dataclasses in `common/html/render.py`, exported from `common/html/__init__.py`. `emit_html(..., filter_specs=[...])` threads them into the form. Server-side: existing `visual_data` route already passes all query params through to the data fetcher, so no server changes needed (X.2.f's real fetcher consumes the prefix-keyed dict). CategoryFilter's checkboxes are unnamed — a hidden `filter_<col>` input is what HTMX serializes; `wireCategoryFilters` (bootstrap.js) keeps it in sync as a comma-joined string. 23 tests: 16 in `tests/unit/test_html_filter_primitives.py` (render + TestClient round-trip) + 7 in `tests/js/test_filter_primitives.py` (CategoryFilter checkbox sync).

- [x] **X.2.e — Sheet structure + cross-sheet + cross-app navigation.** Sheet tabs across the top of `/dashboards/:id`. Click switches sheet via `hx-get` + `hx-push-url`. Cross-sheet drills (currently QS `CustomActionURLOperation`) become plain `<a href>`s in the rendered HTML — `/dashboards/:id/sheets/:other-sheet?param_account_id=...`. URL-as-state means the QS URL-param-doesn't-sync-controls quirk doesn't surface.
  - **Cross-app drills (QS-blocked, App 2 unblocks).** L1 → Investigation drills are dropped under QS (`project_qs_url_parameter_no_control_sync` memory: K.4.7 — URL fragment sets parameter but doesn't push values into bound controls). App 2's URL-as-state model makes this trivial — `<a href="/dashboards/investigation/sheets/money-trail?param_anchor=...">` works. Wire the previously-deferred K.4.7 cross-app drills back in for the App 2 dialect; QS dialect stays as-is. Drill destinations need to know the OTHER app's URL pattern — resolve at render time via a small `app_for(visual)` helper that maps tree references to dashboard ids.
  - **X.2.g.1.c — Visual-level aggregation wrapping.** ✓ — App2's tree fetcher now wraps the dataset SQL with the visual's declared aggregation before executing. Without this, KPI(values=[count(...)]) rendered one card PER DATASET ROW (the screenshot bug). New `common/html/_visual_sql.py::wrap_for_visual(base_sql, visual)` produces: KPI → `SELECT <agg(col)> FROM (base_sql) sub`; BarChart → `SELECT <cat>, <agg(val)> FROM (base_sql) sub GROUP BY <cat>`; LineChart → same + `ORDER BY <cat>`; Table / Sankey / ForceGraph → unwrapped pass-through. Maps Measure.kind ("sum"/"max"/"min"/"average"/"count"/"distinct_count") to the SQL aggregation function. Dialect-portable (SQL-92 aggregations every dialect supports). Tree fetcher unit tests updated to use row-grain dataset SQL.
  - **X.2.g.1.b — Cross-dialect filter wiring via SQL templating.** ✓ — `build_dataset(..., app2_sql=...)` accepts an optional App2 SQL variant; QS SQL stays as-is for `CustomSql.SqlQuery`. Each app's dataset author writes ONE SQL template with a `{date_filter}` slot — QS gets `""` (its filter comes from the analysis-level FilterGroup), App2 gets the bind-clause snippet from `common/sql/app2_filters.app2_date_filter("col_name")`. The snippet uses `NULLIF(:date_from, '') IS NULL OR ...` to handle PG's `''` vs Oracle's `''`-as-NULL vs SQLite's `''`-as-text. Executives' two datasets (`exec_transaction_summary`, `exec_account_summary`) ported to the templating pattern — no SQL duplication. The same pattern lifts to L1 / L2FT / Investigation when their X.2.g.{2,3,4} wiring lands. **Architecture note:** this is the latest example of the broader "one logical model, projected per target runtime" pattern: SQL placeholders (PG `%s` / Oracle `:1` / SQLite `?` / App2 `:name` / QS `<<$name>>`), theme tokens (CSS vars vs QS Theme JSON), filter primitives (URL params vs ParameterControl), all converging.
  - **Status:** Sheet tabs + sheet route shipped. `_render_sheet_tabs(dashboard_id, sheets, active_sheet_id)` renders plain `<a href="/dashboards/:d/sheets/:s">` per analysis sheet (active tab carries `bg-accent`); single-sheet analyses get an empty tab strip (suppressed). New `/dashboards/:d/sheets/:s` route in `server.py::sheet_view` resolves any analysis sheet by id (404 themed). `visual_data` route widened to accept any analysis-sheet id, not just the served (default landing) sheet's. Tabs use full-page reload (no HTMX swap) — Tailwind/HTMX/d3 are cached so only chrome reloads, and URL stays trivially bookmarkable. Decision was plain-anchor over hx-get to avoid the fragment-vs-full-page distinction. 13 tests in `tests/unit/test_html_sheet_nav.py`. **Deferred to X.2.e.2:** cross-sheet drill rendering (per-row anchors derived from the tree's `Drill` primitive — needs renderer-per-visual-kind work in bootstrap.js or per-row server fragments) and cross-app drill rendering (the K.4.7 re-enable — needs an `app_for(visual)` resolver that lands when X.2.g wires the 4 apps). The plumbing this phase shipped is what those follow-ons sit on top of.

- [x] **X.2.f — Real data fetcher.** Replace the stub `DataFetcher` callable with an implementation that:
  - Takes the visual's dataset SQL (already in `apps/<app>/datasets.py`).
  - Substitutes filter values into the SQL (parameterized — never string-format user input).
  - Executes against the configured DB (Postgres / Oracle, dispatched via `Dialect`).
  - Returns rows shaped per visual kind (Table → list of dicts, Sankey → nodes/links, KPI → number, etc.).
  - Per-visual `data_shape()` helper on each tree primitive that documents the JSON shape its d3 renderer expects.
  - **Status:** Infrastructure shipped. `common/html/_sql_executor.py` provides `execute_visual_sql(connection_factory, sql, url_params, dialect)` — accepts `:name`-style placeholders in dataset SQL, rewrites to `%(name)s` for Postgres (Oracle/SQLite stay native), collects bind params from the URL-keyed filter dict, executes against any DB-API 2.0 connection, returns `(rows, columns)`. Unreferenced URL params are silently dropped (forms serialize every input on every Refresh; per-visual SQL only references the filters it cares about). `common/html/_data_shape.py` provides `shape_kpi` / `shape_table` / `shape_bar_chart` / `shape_line_chart` / `shape_sankey` adapters matching the bootstrap.js `renderXxx` JSON contracts exactly, plus `shape_for_kind(kind, rows, columns, **opts)` dispatcher keyed off `type(visual).__name__`. ForceGraph stays projector-driven (no SQL). Wiring into `make_db_fetcher` per app lands when X.2.g builds out the 4 apps — X.2.f is the renderer-agnostic infrastructure those per-app fetchers consume. 31 tests in `tests/unit/test_html_data_shape.py` (17) + `tests/unit/test_html_sql_executor.py` (14); end-to-end SQLite round-trip in the executor tests.

- [ ] **X.2.g — Build out the 4 apps.** Order by dependency / risk, lightest first to surface architecture gaps early:
  - **X.2.g.0 — Generic per-tree DataFetcher factory** ✓ — `make_tree_db_fetcher(tree_app, cfg)` walks visuals, looks up dataset SQL via the new `get_sql(visual_identifier)` registry (populated by `build_dataset` → `register_sql`), executes via X.2.f's `_sql_executor`, shapes via X.2.f's `_data_shape`. 10 tests in `tests/unit/test_html_tree_fetcher.py` (build-time visual indexing + dispatch + filter substitution + multi-sheet + loud-fail on missing SQL).
  - **X.2.g.1 — Executives** (5 sheets: Getting Started + Account Coverage + Transaction Volume + Money Moved + Info; KPI + Table + BarChart visuals). ✓ — `quicksight-gen serve app2 apply --app executives` builds the real Executives tree, calls `build_all_datasets(cfg)` to populate the SQL registry, constructs the fetcher via `make_tree_db_fetcher`, and serves through the existing App2 server. 4 wiring tests in `tests/unit/test_html_executives_wiring.py` pin sheet count + assert the build-time SQL lookup succeeds for every visual. Operator verifies end-to-end against live PG before X.2.g.2 lands. Fastest end-to-end signal that the renderer carries a real app.
  - **X.2.g.2 — Investigation** (5 sheets: Money Trail Sankey already proven via spike, Account Network already a force-directed shape).
  - **X.2.g.3 — L2 Flow Tracing** (4 sheets: Rails, Chains, Templates, Hygiene — heavy on ParameterDropdown + cascading filters from X.1.g).
  - **X.2.g.4 — L1 Dashboard** (11 sheets — biggest surface, do last when the renderer is settled).
  - [x] **X.2.g.5 — `serve app2 apply` serves all 4 real apps from one process by default** *(done).* The X.2.g.{1–4} wiring landed `--app <one>` (one tree per invocation); `server.py::make_app(dashboards: Mapping[str, ServedDashboard])` was already built for many but the CLI never made "all" the default. Now `serve app2 apply` with no `--app` builds the four real apps' trees + registers their (per-app-prefixed → non-colliding) datasets + constructs the `{dashboard_id: ServedDashboard}` mapping with one shared DB pool, so `/dashboards` lists all four and you switch in-process — same "no-arg = all" shape as `json apply` (`feedback_common_path_default`). `--app <one>` stays for single-app iteration; `--app smoke` stays the DB-free fixture (and the only one `--stub` applies to). `_build_real_app(name, cfg, instance)` helper extracted. `test_serve_smoke.py` asserts `[default: all]` + the `--app`/`--stub` options. Live-verified: `serve app2 apply --l2 tests/l2/sasquatch_pr.yaml` on a SQLite-seeded sasquatch_pr DB → `/dashboards` lists L1 Dashboard / L2 Flow Tracing / Investigation / Executives, each renders + their KPI data fragments return real values (L1 Drift `{"value":271}`, Inv Fanout `{"value":20}`), SNB theme + `/static/vendor/...` assets throughout, no errors.
  - [x] **X.2.g.5.followon — server-side pagination for Table visuals** *(done).* The L1 Transactions sheet froze the browser: its Table dataset has ~68k rows and `_tree_fetcher` returned ALL of them in one ~20 MB `<script class="chart-data">` JSON fragment → `renderTable` choked building 68k `<tr>`s before its (already-built) client-side pager could run. Fix: the fetcher now wraps Table-visual SQL as `SELECT qs_page.*, COUNT(*) OVER () FROM (<base>) qs_page ORDER BY 1 <LIMIT/OFFSET | OFFSET ROWS FETCH NEXT — dialect-correct>`, honoring the `page_offset` / `page_size` URL params the renderer already sends, returning the in-page slice + the full `total_rows`; the `COUNT(*)` column is stripped positionally; `page_size` is clamped to ≤10 000 so a crafted value can't OOM. Default page 50. (`_paginate_table_sql` + `_page_int` helpers in `_tree_fetcher.py`; `test_html_tree_fetcher.py::test_make_tree_db_fetcher_paginates_table` covers page boundaries + total + the no-leak + the clamp; the L1 Transactions fragment is now ~16 KB / 50 rows of 68 874.) **Server-side sort** landed alongside (X.2.h.5): `_parse_sort` reads the renderer's `sort_column=<name>:<asc|desc>`, `_paginate_table_sql` emits `ORDER BY <column_name(name, dialect)> [DESC], 1` (the trailing `, 1` is a deterministic tiebreak), bare-identifier guard rejects anything else → falls back to `ORDER BY 1`, the *resolved* sort is echoed back so the renderer's badge / next-direction logic stays consistent (`test_make_tree_db_fetcher_sorts_table` covers asc/desc + the injection-rejection). Browser round-trip in `X.2.h.5` below.
  - Per-app smoke: render every sheet, walk every drill, exercise every filter.
  - **Discipline (pre-X.6 docs work):** every new sheet's `description` and every visual's `subtitle` is the single source of truth for the corresponding docs page. CLAUDE.md already mandates "every visual has a subtitle" — extend the rule to "the subtitle IS the docs source of truth." X.6 will read these strings to auto-generate walkthroughs; if they live in tree primitives now, X.6 has nothing to refactor.
  - **App Info sheet parity.** Every QS app has the `Info` canary as its last sheet (CLAUDE.md mandate; renders App version + per-matview latest_date + deploy stamp). App 2 serves the same Info sheet — same diagnostic value when a sheet renders empty: glance at Info first to tell "App 2 is healthy, the data/SQL is the bug" from "App 2 itself broke." Renderer treats the Info text-box visual the same as a KPI card.

Findings: (1) **Count vs row-identity** → row-identity (set of `(account_id, business_day_start)` key tuples) for the flat-shape invariants (drift / overdraft / limit_breach); count + `App2_rows == QS_rows == direct_matview_rows` (natural key) for the divergent-shape ones (stuck_pending / stuck_unbundled / supersession — the PDF roll-up shape diverges by design). (2) **Add the 5th anchor** — a direct `SELECT` against the L1-invariant matview *is* the ground truth: the spike showed `expected.drift_count = 1` but the matview holds **2 rows** (`cust-001 +75` is an incidental drift cell, not a plant), so `expected` is a lower bound (`⊆`). Chain: `scenario_plants ⊆ direct_SQL == PDF* == QS == App2`. (3) **App2 leg mechanics** → `App2Driver.serving(tree_app=<L1 tree>, sheet=first, data_fetcher=make_live_db_fetchers_for_app(tree_app, cfg)[0], options_fetcher=…)` works against any connection string (Aurora = just a different `demo_database_url`); confirmed live (the 2 drift matview rows surfaced in "Leaf Account Drift", matching direct-SQL exactly). **Gotcha:** App2's Table renderer is server-side paginated (`_TABLE_PAGE_SIZE = 50`) — `App2Driver.table_row_count` reads one DOM page, under-counts > 50-row tables; the true total is in `.table-pager-range` text (`"X–Y of M"`). Fix in X.2.j.B: make `table_row_count` pagination-aware. Use the **plural** `make_live_db_fetchers_for_app` (the L1 tree has dataset-sourced dropdowns → needs the options half). (4) **Dialect coverage** → CI gate (`e2e-against-testpypi` / `e2e-pg-browser`) = PG only (4-way); runner `lo` cells = {pg 4-way, oracle 4-way, sqlite 3-way (no QS leg — `QsEmbedDriver` can't reach a sqlite tempfile)}; runner `aw` cells = {pg 4-way, oracle 4-way}. No new dialect machinery — additive on the 3-way's existing parametrization + per-cell skips. (5) **Reuses the seed?** → yes — one module-scoped `per_dialect_app2_driver` fixture rides the existing `seeded_audit` fixture; the fetcher only reads. (6) **dateparity** → **no divergence** for `spec_example` / `sasquatch_pr` (both midnight-aligned `business_day_start`; neither sets `role_business_day_offsets`); BUT `app2_date_filter`'s `<= date_to` is genuinely wrong for non-midnight TIMESTAMP columns (fuzz cells with role offsets; the `posting`-keyed Transactions / Executives / Investigation date filters) — X.2.j.dateparity stays a real fix.

    - [x] **X.2.j.dateparity — `app2_date_filter` upper-bound is exclusive of the last day; widen it.** *Done — commit `651af7e`. Upper clause is now `column < date_to + 1 day` (PG `+ INTERVAL '1 day'` / Oracle `+ 1` / SQLite `date(:date_to, '+1 day')`); upper sentinel lowered `9999-12-31`→`9999-12-30` so `+1` stays in range on Oracle (ORA-01841) + SQLite; applies to every `app2_date_filter` call site (L1 Drift / Overdraft / Limit Breach / Transactions, Executives, Investigation). Unit tests updated + a `TestDayInclusiveUpperBound` regression guard against re-introducing the `<=` form. (The X.2.j.0 verdict — no divergence for the midnight-aligned `spec_example` / `sasquatch_pr` — means the *e2e* regression guard "a planted non-midnight upper-edge row visible in App2 == QS" would need a fuzz/role-offset instance to actually bite; the unit-level guard covers it for now. Also-revisit-someday: the QS-DateTime-param-substitution shape if we ever pivot to Y.2.f Option A.)*
  - [x] **X.2.j.C — Wire the 4-way test into the release gate + the runner.** *Done — `test_audit_dashboard_agreement.py` already runs in the runner's `browser` layer (browser-marked; the runner dispatches it; the new App2-leg changes ride along since the marker is unchanged). Added a separate step running it (`-m browser -v -k postgres`) in both `e2e.yml::e2e-pg-browser` and `release.yml::e2e-against-testpypi` — separate invocation because `seeded_audit` re-applies the prefixed schema (DROP + CREATE + re-plant), so it can't share a worker pool with the render tests above; runs last. File lists in the two workflows kept in sync (`feedback_ci_release_workflow_parity`). Both workflow YAMLs `yaml.safe_load`-parse clean. In `e2e-pg-browser` the deployed `spec_example` L1 dashboard supplies the QS leg → full 4-way on PG; in the release gate the synthesized `rel_<tag>` dashboard may or may not be deployed under the agreement test's derived ID (it uses `run/config.postgres.yaml`, ignoring `QS_GEN_CONFIG`) — if not, the QS leg self-skips and it's the 3-way `scenario ⊆ direct == App2` + PDF against the just-published wheel, still a real prod-publish gate. **First-CI-run caveat:** the agreement test's `_DIALECT_CONFIG_PATHS` is hardcoded to `run/config.{postgres,oracle}.yaml`; if the CI checkout's `run/config.postgres.yaml` doesn't cleanly connect to the CI Aurora, the step errors loudly — fix forward (a `dialect_cfg` skip-on-connection-failure is the obvious patch if it bites).*

A tree-primitive change for App 2 that breaks QS emit is a regression to fix, not a tradeoff. (The X.2.j.dateparity change touches only the App2 SQL — QS gets `{date_filter}` → `""` — so it's backward-compat-safe by construction; the dataset SQL isn't stored in the DB, so no re-lock either.)*

- [ ] **X.2.q — Dialect-aware e2e driver layer (one test body, two renderers).** Today there are two parallel browser-e2e suites with disjoint helper vocabularies: the QS suite (`tests/e2e/test_l1_*.py` / `test_inv_*.py` / `test_exec_*.py`) drives the embedded QS iframe via `data-automation-id` selectors with all the QS quirks baked into the test bodies (cell virtualization, racy tab switches, the page-size-bump-for-true-row-count trick, the `ParameterDropDownControl` grey-bar click); the App 2 suite (`tests/e2e/test_html2_*.py`) drives the local App 2 page via its own `#filter-form` / `data-widget` / `data-visual-id` selectors. Same *intent* ("set a date filter", "find the rows in the Drift table", "pick a status"), two implementations, drifting apart — and nothing forces the two renderers to agree on a result.

  **Fix:** a `DashboardDriver` protocol (`common/browser/` or `tests/e2e/_drivers/`) — the verbs are the test vocabulary (`open(dashboard, sheet)` / `goto_sheet(name)` / `set_date_range(from_, to)` / `pick_filter(label, values)` / `set_slider(label, lo, hi)` / `clear_filters()` / `table_rows(visual_title) -> list[dict[str, str]]` / `kpi_value(visual_title) -> str | None` / `visual_titles() -> list[str]` / `wait_loaded(visual_title)` / `cross_link(label)` / **`screenshot(path | -> bytes)`** — on-demand capture of the current state, useful both as a test-failure artifact and for the `ScreenshotHarness`-style doc/eyeball captures, with the QS-embed vs App2-page mechanics sealed in each driver …) — and **the driver wraps the results into plain Python (dicts / lists / strs / bytes), never returning a Playwright `Locator` or `Page`**, so the e2e test bodies become almost pure functions: `assert driver.table_rows("Drift") == expected`, no DOM poking, no `wait_for_selector`, no virtualization arithmetic in the test. Two impls: `QsEmbedDriver(embed_url)` (the QS quirks live entirely in here) and `App2Driver(base_url)` (reads `<table>` rows directly; drives Tom Select / Flatpickr / noUiSlider via the `data-widget` markup). e2e tests get `@pytest.mark.parametrize`'d over `[qs, app2]` via a `driver` fixture; QS-only or App2-only checks just `pytest.skip` the irrelevant param. This is the foundation `X.2.j`'s 4-way agreement gate is built on (the same `table_rows()` from the `qs` and `app2` drivers, plus the audit PDF's numbers, must match), and `X.2.l.4.d` rides on it (the widget round-trips ARE `set_date_range` / `pick_filter` / `set_slider` — any parametrized test exercises them; plus a couple of App2-driver-only "the filter narrows `table_rows()`" asserts). **Spike-before-locking** (per `feedback_spike_before_locking_implementation` — this is a codebase-shape change for the whole e2e layer).
  - [x] **X.2.q.0 — SPIKE: prove the protocol on one existing test.** *Done — both legs green; spike doc at `docs/audits/x_2_q_e2e_driver_spike.md`.* Landed: `tests/e2e/_drivers/base.py` (`DashboardDriver` Protocol — `dialect`, `open`, `goto_sheet`, `visual_titles`, `wait_loaded`, `table_rows -> list[dict[str,str]]`, `kpi_value -> str|None`, `pick_filter`, `set_date_range`, `set_slider`, `clear_filters`, `cross_link`, `screenshot -> bytes`, `close` — all reads plain Python, no `Locator`/`Page`); `tests/e2e/_drivers/app2.py` (`App2Driver` — `.smoke()` factory owns `html2_server` + `webkit_page`; impl `open`/`visual_titles`/`wait_loaded`/`table_rows`/`kpi_value`/`screenshot`, rest `NotImplementedError("X.2.q.2")`); `tests/e2e/_drivers/qs.py` (`QsEmbedDriver` — `.embed()` factory owns `webkit_page`; `open(dashboard_id, sheet=)` mints a fresh region-matched embed URL; impl `open`/`goto_sheet`/`visual_titles`/`wait_loaded`/`kpi_value`/`screenshot`; `table_rows` + write verbs `NotImplementedError("X.2.q.2")` — `table_rows` because the `sn-table-cell-*` automation-ids are body-only, no verified header-cell id); `tests/e2e/test_dashboard_driver.py` (3 pure-assertion smoke-Showcase tests via `App2Driver.smoke()` + 2 live-deployed-L1 tests via `QsEmbedDriver.embed()` — all 5 green against the deployed `qs-gen-postgres-sasquatch_pr-l1-dashboard`). Decisions locked (rationale in the doc): drivers live in `tests/e2e/_drivers/` (test infra; promotable to `common/browser/` later); `table_rows` keys by header text; `wait_loaded(visual_title, *, timeout_ms=15_000)`; "this verb isn't meaningful here" → `NotImplementedError` from the driver (not skip) — tests skip the *param*, not the verb; `screenshot` returns PNG bytes + optionally writes a path; factories are `@contextmanager` classmethods that own the browser/server lifecycle.

It now (1) gives the re-fetch ~1.2s to start clearing, (2) polls the tables' first-few cell texts until steady across two ~0.7s reads; `pick_filter`/`set_date_range` call it so the read after a write sees the post-filter state. `wait_loaded` for a *table* visual now waits for `sn-table-cell-0-0` (vs. just the title label) — best-effort, swallowed for legitimately-empty tables. - [~] **X.2.r — Drop the QS sleep/poll waits for native Playwright event-based waits.** The `QsEmbedDriver._settle_after_param_change()` heuristic (1.2s upfront sleep + 700ms-spaced cell-text-stability poll, capped 18s — landed in X.2.q.3) plus the scattered `wait_for_timeout` calls in `common/browser/helpers.py` are correctness-driven smells. Each was added because we couldn't tell when QS finished a state change. With Y.2's SQL pushdown making the actual queries fast, the polling overhead is now larger than the useful wait.
  - [x] **Spike** *(done — `docs/audits/x_2_r_event_wait_spike.md`; capture tool `scripts/spike_x2r_qs_event_capture.py`).* Found: QS routes every dataset query as a JSON text frame over a single long-lived WebSocket — `{"type":"START_VIS","cid":"<uuid>","request":{…}}` to start a visual's query, `{"type":"STOP_VIS","cids":[…]}` once the client's processed the response + torn down the rendering pipeline. So `sent_START − sent_STOP` is the in-flight re-query count; watching it drain to zero (after ≥1 fresh START fired + a 300ms quiet window — the pick triggers two bursts: immediate + debounced-follow-up ~2s later) is the "data layer is done" signal. (Playwright's WebKit channel surfaced only `framesent`, never `framereceived` — doesn't matter, client-sent `STOP_VIS` is sufficient.) **No HTTP signal exists** for the data layer — only structural fetches (`?Operation=GetSheetForDashboard` etc.) and telemetry POSTs go over HTTP. The DOM-spinner fallback wasn't needed.
  - [x] **Implementation** *(done).* `_QsWsActivityTracker` in `tests/e2e/_drivers/qs.py` hooks `page.on("websocket")` + `ws.on("framesent")` at driver construction, parses each text frame, tracks `pending: set[str]` / `total_starts: int` / `last_start_at`. `_settle_after_param_change()` rewritten: snapshot `baseline = total_starts`, then spin (80ms in-process polls — tracker state lives in Python, no IPC) until `total_starts > baseline AND pending_count == 0 AND ms_since_last_start >= 300`; capped 18s; swallowed on timeout (same best-effort contract). Dropped the 1.2s upfront sleep + the cell-text-stability poll loop. Call sites (`pick_filter` / `set_date_range` / `drill_from_first_row`) unchanged.
  - [x] **Verify against the L2FT dropdown walk** *(done).* `test_l1_filters` + `test_inv_filters` + `test_l2ft_{rails,chains,templates}_dropdowns` against the deployed `sasquatch_pr`: 8 passed + 2 skipped + 1 xpassed, ~3:44 — roughly comparable to the X.2.q.3 baseline (~3:03), within Aurora-variance noise; the win is correctness (event-driven signal, not a content-stability heuristic), AND no flakiness on the L2FT walk (the test that surfaced the original race). `up_to=unit` green.
  - [x] **Quirks-log update** *(done — §3.6 rewritten: the workaround is now the WS-frame tracker, not the sleep-and-poll heuristic; the underlying stale-rows quirk stays documented).*
  - [x] **Sweep the helpers** (`common/browser/helpers.py`) *(done — the wasteful unconditional waits; the rest are either acceptable poll-loop backoffs or genuinely need a settle).* `right_click_first_row_of_visual`'s 800ms post-click → `wait_for_selector('[role="menu"]', state="visible")` — confirms the contextmenu actually popped (returns the moment it mounts; *and* fails here with "waiting for [role=menu]" if no DATA_POINT_MENU drill is wired, instead of `click_context_menu_item` timing out 30s later on the absent menu *item* — clearer + earlier failure for the deployed-drill-stale case). `count_table_total_rows` post-focus-click 1500ms + `expand_all_tables_on_sheet` post-focus-click 800ms → deleted; the immediately-following `wait_for_selector` for `simplePagedDisplayNav_dropdown_pageSize` bumped by the deleted amount (3s→4.5s, 1.5s→2.5s) so the effective deadline is preserved but it returns the moment the control mounts. **Left as-is (and why):** the poll-loop backoffs (`wait_for_table_total_rows_to_change` 500ms, `wait_for_chart_categories_to_change` 250ms, `wait_for_kpi_*` 250ms, `wait_for_dropdown_options_present` `time.sleep(0.25)`) — these re-check an event-y condition on a bounded loop; the X.2.r plan explicitly carved these out as the acceptable pattern, and `helpers.py` isn't in the `no-sleep` lint scope. `click_chart_bar`'s per-keypress settles (300/100/120/500ms) — QS renders charts to `<canvas>`; there's no event for "QS processed my Tab/Arrow keypress" on a canvas. `scroll_visual_into_view`'s 800ms post-scroll (`wait_for_cells=False` path) — deliberately kept: it's a *reliability* hedge (gives QS time to lazy-mount the now-visible visual), not a flakiness source, and the only `wait_for_cells=False` callers (`wait_loaded` / `table_rows`) do their own post-checks anyway. `count_table_total_rows`'s 2000ms fallback-scroll branch — a rare edge path (standard scroll already failed). The App2 leg reads a **live DB**, slotting into the **output** position of the established pipeline — `scenario → DB (sqlite/oracle/postgres) → output (QuickSight / App2 / audit-PDF)` — exactly the shape `test_audit_dashboard_agreement.py` already uses (seed a scenario into the dialect-specific DB, then verify via QS *and* audit off the same data); App2 becomes the third output reading that same DB (`make_live_db_fetcher_for_app(tree_app, cfg)`, dialect via `cfg.dialect`'s `_sql_executor` placeholder rewriting — App2 already supports all three dialects per X.3.e).         - [x] **u.4.e.3.a — Vendor `ctxmenu`** *(done).* Added `assets/vendor/js/ctxmenu.min.js` — the `ctxmenu@2.1.0/standalone/ctxmenu.min.js` build (an IIFE that sets `window.ctxmenu`; the package's other dist is CommonJS — `exports.ctxmenu` — no good for a plain `<script>`; 8251 bytes, sha256 `00dd49473c5e8cf821841805ea0b46b851105ea13c96b14d8c7c6ed83ee9b5a4`). ctxmenu ships no CSS file — it injects its own `<style id="ctxmenu">` into `<head>` at runtime — so instead of a vendored stylesheet, `widgets-theme.css` got a `.ctxmenu` re-skin block (`!important` on every colour rule, since the injected sheet loads *after* our override sheet) mapping the popover onto the L2 `--color-*` vars, same pattern as the Tom Select / Flatpickr / noUiSlider blocks. `vendor.lock` carries the `ctxmenu` entry; `scripts/vendor_js_deps.py` is data-driven off `vendor.lock` (`--update` re-downloads it) — no script change; `tests/unit/test_vendor_assets.py` picks it up (parametrized over `deps`; `_CTXMENU_JS` added to the `render.py` local-constants assertion).
