- Drift dataset's WHERE uses `_account_display_clause` which expands to `('__l1_all__' = <<$p>> OR (account_name || ' (' || account_id || ')') = <<$p>>)` — looks correct on paper.
- Direct DB query with `apply_dataset_param_defaults` returns the anchor row when fed `"Demo Customer 1 (tmpl-cust-001)"` → so the SQL pipeline is **not** the bug.
- `db_counts.txt` confirms: `qsgen_sp_pg_aw_drift: 10` rows. Data is there.

What's unverified (the next-session pickup):

- **What value does QS actually send in the post-pick START_VIS WS frame?** If QS's MUI Autocomplete coerces the picker value (split on the `(...)`, drop the trailing paren content, only send the leading display text, etc.), the WHERE clause's parenthesized concat wouldn't match. The X.2.r spike confirmed `START_VIS` carries `request.cfg` — `_QsWsActivityTracker` already parses these frames; one targeted run with a `console.debug(JSON.stringify(msg.request))` hook inside the tracker would surface what QS is actually substituting.
- **What does the Account dropdown actually advertise?** Pre-pick DOM has a text-box panel listing `ClearingSuspense (clearing-suspense)` / `CustomerSubledger (cust-001)` — but this is the sheet's "Internal Accounts in Scope" descriptive text, NOT the Account dropdown's option list. Need to expand the dropdown post-load + read `filter_options("Account")` to confirm the dropdown's actual option strings match the test's `f"{account_name} ({account_id})"` format.
- **Is this AA.E.2 leftover?** AA.E.2 wired `account_display` for search-by-name-AND-id; possibly the Drift dataset's projection still has the raw `account_id` column where the test's anchor reads from, but the dropdown's source dataset projects a different concat. Cross-reference: the dropdown's `LinkedValues` source dataset vs `build_drift_dataset`'s projection.
- **App2-Transactions** (separate from QS-* but same kind of shape): 2 failures (additive + inverse) in `[app2-Transactions]`. Spec-specific — Transactions is the only L1 sheet whose dataset doesn't share the standard L1-invariant matview pattern. May be the same dropdown-format-mismatch class, just on App2 instead of QS.

- [x] **AA.A.qs-triage.1 — Instrumented WS-frame capture.** Done — generalized into `ws_frames.txt` artifact (commit `20091e3`), captured 12+ frames in run `20260518T060135Z-20091e3/sp_pg_aw/browser/`. Findings split into two distinct shapes (not one):
  - **Shape A (Drift / Limit Breach / Today's Exceptions)** — pickers fire correctly; QS's `TimeRangeFilter` with default `include_minimum=None` compiles to `business_day_start >= addDateTime(1, 'DD', truncDate('DD', date_from)) AND < truncDate('DD', date_to)`. With `date_from == date_to` (the anchor's date), the lower bound shifts to `date_from + 1`, producing an empty inverted range. App2 ducks this via `column < date_to + 1 day` inclusive (X.2.j.dateparity). Supplanted by **AA.A.daterange** below (refactor to single filter-bound `DATE_RANGE` control).
  - **Shape B (Overdraft / Transactions)** — picker doesn't fire dataset params; every `dsp-l1-*` parameter stays at sentinel `"__l1_all__"` post-pick, dates are at default 7-day window. SQL should match everything, yet visual shows 0 rows. Separate root cause — needs further triage (AA.A.qs-triage.4 / new sub-task).
- [x] **AA.A.qs-triage.2 — Dropdown option-list capture.** Folded into Shape A finding: the picker values that DID propagate (e.g. `"Demo Customer 1 (tmpl-cust-001)"`) match the test's expected `account_display` format exactly. Dropdown format is fine — the bug was the date filter, not the value substitution. App2 narrows correctly on the same value (post-cache-fix), confirming the substitution path works.
- [x] **AA.A.qs-triage.3 — Decide race.3 fate.** Stays in tree. Root cause was filter-expression semantics, not a WebSocket-timing race; race.3 didn't help these failures but doesn't hurt and remains defense-in-depth for the cache-equivalent failure class it was designed to catch (which hasn't surfaced yet on the QS side but is structurally analogous to App2's cache bug).

Both renderers fail identically, strongly suggesting parameter-bridge missing on this sheet. Tracked separately as AA.A.qs-triage.5.
- [x] **AA.A.qs-triage.5 — Today's Exceptions filter shape (4/4 PASS, closed 2026-05-19).** Resolved by the combination of three landings: (a) `SheetAnchorSpec(anchor_where_template="account_id IN (SELECT account_id FROM {prefix}_current_daily_balances)")` in `tests/e2e/test_l1_additive_pickers.py` constrains the anchor to the Account-dropdown universe (the Today's Exceptions matview pulls stuck_pending/stuck_unbundled rows on control accounts that aren't in `current_daily_balances`); (b) the dropdown-popover selector widening in `helpers.py` (`_OPTION_SELECTOR` accepts both `[role="listbox"]` and `sheet_control_value-menu` shapes); (c) the qs-triage.5.followon matview-refresh fixture ensured the deployed Aurora state was fully populated (2287 accounts) rather than the partially-refreshed 2-account state from a prior `exceptions_only` run. The `MuiAutocomplete-noOptions` symptom observed in the 17:47 May 18 failure was a side effect of `current_daily_balances=2` at that moment, not a code bug in the dropdown layer. Verified 4/4 PASS post-redeploy (`f4b9cda`): `keep_anchor_row[qs|app2-Today's Exceptions]` + `inverse_excludes_anchor[qs|app2-Today's Exceptions]`, 108.66s total. Closed via the per-call SQL-trace artifact (`AA.A.qs-triage.5.sql-trace`) + `record_sql_trace` follow-on so future "dropdown empty after typing" triages can split DB-from-QS without re-running queries by hand.
  - [x] **AA.A.qs-triage.5.sql-trace** — `record_sql_trace(label, sql, summary)` in `common/browser/helpers.py`; `fetch_anchor_row` writes the wrapped anchor SQL + the resulting row (or "no rows") to `<capture_dir>/sql_trace.txt` per call. Surfaces "what did the test ask the DB for, and what came back" alongside `db_counts.txt` for every browser failure. Sidecar-safe (swallows its own exceptions); exempt from `no-playwright-leak` lint (sidecar, no Playwright coupling) and `no-datetime-now` (debug provenance, not in hash-locked output). Commit `b00cfa9`.

Refreshes the deployed-DB matviews once per session so picker tests + agreement tests always see live data after ad-hoc `data apply --execute` flows that skipped `data refresh`. The chain runner's `seed_variant` already runs `data refresh` after seed (runner.py:2565), so this is a safety net for direct-pytest invocations + post-CLI-iteration flows. Idempotent. Best-effort on failure.

### AA.A.daterange — single DATE_RANGE control instead of two-param Date From/To (umbrella, 2026-05-18)

Replaces the `(ParameterDateTimePickerControl Date From + ParameterDateTimePickerControl Date To + TimeRangeFilter)` triplet with a single `FilterDateTimePickerControl(Type="DATE_RANGE")` bound directly to the column. Closes the date-collapse bug class structurally (you can't put a range control into an inverted state), and removes the App2/QS date-semantics drift that X.2.j.dateparity patched only on the App2 side.

Captured root cause (`20260518T060135Z-20091e3/sp_pg_aw/browser/.../qs-Drift/ws_frames.txt`): `_scope_one` in `apps/l1_dashboard/app.py:1581` creates `TimeRangeFilter` without setting `include_minimum`/`include_maximum`; QS defaults both to exclusive, then compiles the lower bound to `addDateTime(1, 'DD', truncDate('DD', date_from))` — "after the start of date_from's day". Correct semantics for "exclusive-min day-granularity range", wrong UX for "show me this date range". App2 has the same shift on the upper bound (correct: `< date_to + 1 day` → inclusive-upper day semantics).

QS supports the right widget natively: `FilterDateTimePickerControl(Type="DATE_RANGE")` exists at `common/models.py:1086`. One widget, two bound dates, can't be put in invalid state. We just don't use it.

**Parked branch context (CRITICAL — must not lose sight of)**: `aa-a-9b-l2ft-picker-extension` (commit `4ff8dc4`) extends `AA.A.6/7` picker tests to L2FT Rails/Chains/Templates using the existing per-sheet date picker spec. **Merge that branch FIRST** before the daterange refactor — otherwise the branch gets rebase conflicts on the picker spec shape change. After merging, the daterange refactor naturally covers L2FT's new picker specs in the same sweep.

**Shape A is closed by the 1-line fix** (commits `8dac205` L1 + `0504756` L2FT/Exec, v11.0.1). The structural refactor below stays as **backlogged structural debt**, not bug-fix work — its motivation shifts from "fix failing tests" to "QS / App2 dialect parity + multi-widget UX footgun." User-rationale (2026-05-18): "I'm always a fan of closer parity between dashboards and QS."

- [x] **AA.A.daterange.1 — Spike done.** Investigation already uses the pattern in production (`apps/investigation/app.py:376` — `sheet.add_filter_datetime_picker(... type="DATE_RANGE")`). Tree primitive (`common/tree/controls.py:469`, `common/tree/filters.py:130`) and App2 renderer (Flatpickr `mode:"range"`) both proven. Multi-dataset-per-sheet (L1 Drift's leaf + ledger drift, etc.) is the real wall — needs dataset consolidation OR a different sharing mechanism for the widget-bound filter.
- [x] **AA.A.daterange.2 — Parked branch merged.** `aa-a-9b-l2ft-picker-extension` (commit `4ff8dc4`) landed into `aa-a-daterange` as the first merge. L2FT picker tests live on this branch.
- [x] **AA.A.daterange.fix — 1-line fix (Shape A only).** Applied to 7 L1 + L2FT + Executives `TimeRangeFilter` call sites: `include_minimum=True, include_maximum=True`. Closes the bug without the structural refactor. L1 verify against Aurora (`runs/20260518T062835Z-8dac205/sp_pg_aw/browser/`) confirmed: 3 Shape A L1 failures (Drift / Limit Breach / Today's Exceptions × additive+inverse = 6 closed). L2FT verify in progress.
- [x] **AA.A.9.a — L1 refactor to dataset-builder-driven.** Done. `SheetAnchorSpec` now carries `dataset_builder: Callable[[Config, L2Instance], DataSet]` instead of `anchor_table` + `anchor_columns`. `fetch_anchor_row(cfg, l2, spec)` calls the builder, extracts CustomSql from `DataSet.PhysicalTableMap`, walks `DataSetParameters` and substitutes `<<$pX>>` with each param's declared default via the production `apply_dataset_param_defaults` substitutor (the same one App2's `_sql_executor` uses), wraps in `SELECT * FROM (<that>) sub ORDER BY {anchor_order} LIMIT 1` (Postgres) / `FETCH FIRST 1 ROWS ONLY` (Oracle), executes, returns dict from `cursor.description`. New `l2` session fixture added to `tests/e2e/conftest.py`. All 7 L1 SheetAnchorSpec entries migrated to `dataset_builder=build_*_dataset`. Both `test_l1_additive_pickers_keep_anchor_row` and `test_l1_dropdown_pickers_inverse_excludes_anchor` take the `l2` fixture and call `fetch_anchor_row(cfg, l2, spec)`. 28 tests collect (14 sheets × 2 tests). Net effect: SQL renames / JOINs / sentinel changes flow through automatically — the test runs the same emitter the deploy runs. Chain verification rolls on next `up_to=browser --variants=sp_pg_aw`.
- [x] **AA.A.9.b — Extend AA.A.6/7 to L2FT (Rails / Chains / Templates).** Was deferred under the matview-coupled v1 because the L2FT dropdown columns are CTE-derived or CASE-projected and have no underlying matview to query directly. Now unblocked by AA.A.9.a — wire `SheetAnchorSpec(dataset_builder=build_rails_dataset, ...)` (and chains / templates equivalents) into the L2FT picker list. Investigation Money Trail / Account Network stay deferred — different shape (pick-first-then-narrow), needs a v2 wrapper. Recipient Fanout / Volume Anomalies / Executives stay out (axis count, not approach).
- [ ] **AA.A.11 — Cross-corpus duplication lint (test ↔ src), paired approaches 1+3.** User-flagged 2026-05-17 as "huge structural win": every duplicated SQL string between `tests/` and `src/` is a second codebase that can pass while production breaks, or vice versa. Land both halves together — they catch different failure modes and reinforce each other.
  - **Approach 1 — content-based AST lint** in the `b.15.lint.*` family. Walk `tests/`, extract string literals over a length threshold AND any string containing a SQL fingerprint (`SELECT`/`FROM`/`<<$p`/`WHERE `). For each, check if a normalized substring appears in `src/`. Flag with the matched src file + line. Allowlist via `# duplicate-ok: <why>` sibling marker (same pattern as `# WHY:` for `Any` escapes). Home: `tests/unit/test_lint_no_test_src_duplication.py`. Catches inline SQL copies, repeated fixture strings, hand-mirrored constants.
  - **Approach 3 — structural "did the test import what it asserts on?"** lint. Same AST walker; for any test assertion that touches a SQL string OR a known production constant (sentinel value, parameter name, column name from the `Column` registry), require the value to be obtained via an `import` from `src/recon_gen/...`. Inline string literals in those assertions are the smell. Catches the same content the content-based lint catches PLUS test files that *re-define* a constant rather than import the canonical one.
  - **Why both, not either alone.** Approach 1 catches "the SQL is the same but the test doesn't know it should match production"; approach 3 catches "the test defines its own copy of a value that production also defines, and they currently happen to agree." Approach 1 is *content-equality* (catches today's drift); approach 3 is *provenance* (catches future drift before it can happen).
  - **Approach 2 (token-stream tool — jscpd/PMD CPD) — deliberately not pursued.** Both are non-Rust (Node + Java), against the standalone-binary preference. The content + provenance pair (1+3) covers the same regression class with codebase-native tooling that fits the existing `b.15.lint.*` AST infrastructure. If 1+3 turn out to miss a regression class in practice, re-evaluate.
  - **Open questions to resolve at impl time** (not blocking the entry): length threshold tuning (50? 100? 200? — measure false-positive rate against current corpus); allowlist syntax (sibling comment vs central registry vs per-file `__duplicate_ok__` set); does it run in the unit prelude (cheap, every chain) or as an opt-in `./run_tests.sh lint` mode (heavier — depends on corpus walk cost); cross-corpus scope (`tests/` ↔ `src/` definitely; also `tests/e2e/` ↔ `tests/e2e/_drivers/` to catch driver-internals leakage into tests?).
  - **Spike before locking implementation choices** — write a throwaway script that runs approach 1 against the current `tests/` corpus, measure the FP count at each threshold, decide allowlist shape from observed cases. Same shape for approach 3 (walk for non-import-sourced constants). Spike doc lands under `docs/audits/aa_a_11_spike.md` (or similar) per the spike-before-implement rule.
- [x] **AA.A.8 — Generic "table failed to render" probe across all sheets.** Shipped — `QsEmbedDriver.wait_loaded` HARD-FAILS on any QS error overlay (`visual_error_text` DOM probe in `common/browser/helpers.py`; raises `RuntimeError` with the overlay text). The specific Pending Aging "duplicate columns" bug fixed in 4 sheets (Stuck Pending Detail / Stuck Unbundled Detail / Transactions Audit / Posting Ledger — duplicate `rail_name` column wells) AND closed as a class via `Table.__post_init__` typed invariant (`common/tree/visuals.py` — raises at construction with the AWS error text quote when the same `(dataset, column)` appears twice across columns / group_by / values). Future duplicates fail at the `add_table` call site, not at render time. *(Spike resolution locked 2026-05-17: path (3) — make `wait_loaded` HARD-FAIL on QS error overlay. Spike grep over `tests/e2e/` + `common/browser/` confirmed zero tests depend on the silent-timeout behavior: the only `qs_errors` codepath is `_capture_failure_qs_errors` (post-failure artifact capture, not a wait predicate), and no test asserts an error overlay IS present. Path (3) is safe to land. Plus AA.A.8.bug — fix specific Pending Aging duplicate-columns bug, separate sub-task.)* User-surfaced 2026-05-16 from a specific incident: Pending Aging → Stuck Pending Detail table shows QS error "your tabular report contains duplicate columns. To proceed, remove all duplicates." The specific bug is one fix; the generic ask is the coverage gap — there's no test that walks every visual in every sheet of every dashboard and asserts "the visual rendered something (data OR a 'No data' overlay) and NOT a QuickSight error banner." Today the Info canary catches "QS itself is dead", X.2.j's cross-tool agreement catches "QS disagrees with the source SQL", but a per-visual error banner (`"duplicate columns"`, `"column not found"`, `"too many rows"`, `"query timeout"`) only surfaces in the canary if it happens to hit the Info sheet's matview counts — every other broken visual slips. Shape (sketch — spike-before-implement): walk the tree per app per sheet; for each visual call `wait_loaded(visual_title)` then probe for the QS error-banner DOM (per the quirks log's standing error-overlay selector family) AND for App2's equivalent rendered error state; fail with the banner's text so the operator gets the actual QS error in the failure message, not "spinner didn't disappear." Inverts the AA.H.11 positive-signal pattern: there we waited for cells-or-empty-overlay; here we'd assert NEITHER an error overlay NOR a still-spinning state. Resolution paths (decide at impl time): (1) a dedicated `tests/e2e/test_no_broken_visuals.py` parametrized over `[qs, app2] × every dashboard × every sheet × every visual` — most-explicit, runtime cost = visuals × sheets × dashboards × 2; (2) fold a non-fatal "did this visual surface an error?" probe into `DashboardDriver.wait_loaded` and write it to a per-test artifact alongside the existing dom/screenshot capture — adds zero new test cells but operator must remember to check the artifact; (3) make `wait_loaded` HARD-FAIL on QS error overlay (currently it just times out the visible/cell predicate), so every existing browser e2e gets this coverage for free — most-leveraged but risks breaking tests that legitimately expect an error to be visible. Path (3) is probably the right answer; check the existing helpers for "expects-error" patterns first. Also fix the specific Pending Aging duplicate-columns bug (separate sub-task — likely a dataset/visual-emit collision where the same column is added twice via different paths).

### AA.B — Daily Statement fixes

Two operator-asked changes on the same sheet. Pair them.

- [x] **AA.B.1 — Add account_role dropdown filter to Daily Statement.** Cascade interpretation (user-ratified 2026-05-16): Role narrows the Account dropdown's options, summary + transactions datasets stay single-account. New `DS_L1_DS_ROLES` companion (DISTINCT account_role over `current_daily_balances`) feeds the Role dropdown; new `pL1DsRole` dataset param on `DS_L1_ACCOUNTS` pushes the role into `SELECT DISTINCT account_id, account_role WHERE ('__l1_all__' = <<$pL1DsRole>>) OR (account_role = <<$pL1DsRole>>)`. Show-all sentinel default means every L1 sheet's Account dropdown (the companion's other consumers) sees every account on first load — Daily Statement is the only sheet that bridges the role param. New analysis param `pL1DsRole` + sheet control sit *above* the Account picker so the cascade direction is visually explicit. Updated `test_y2g_companion_datasets_registered_and_unparameterized` to carve out the now-parameterized accounts dataset + added new `test_aa_b_1_l1_accounts_dataset_is_role_cascaded` covering the AA.B.1 contract. 2198 unit + json tests green. Browser verify in AA.B.4.
- [x] **AA.B.2 — Filter accounts we don't track balances for off Daily Statement.** *(already satisfied — empirical verify 2026-05-16.)* The DropDown's source is `SELECT DISTINCT account_id FROM <prefix>_current_daily_balances` (DS_L1_ACCOUNTS) — that IS the "has daily_balances rows" filter the PLAN prescribed. Confirmed against `qsgen_sp_pg_aw`: 27 distinct accounts in `transactions`, 25 in `current_daily_balances`; the 2-account gap (`Clearing Suspense`/`Customer Ledger`, both ClearingSuspense/CustomerLedger role) are L2-account stubs that have transactions but no own-balance row — already correctly excluded from the picker. 1 ExternalCounterparty account stays visible because it DOES have daily_balances rows (the "tracked external" exception the PLAN explicitly preserved). Daily Statement transactions dataset reads from `<prefix>_current_transactions` already account-scoped via `WHERE account_id = <<$pL1DsAccount>>` — counterparty legs aren't pulled. No code change needed. Original concern from the PLAN didn't reproduce against the sp_pg_aw seed.
- [x] **AA.B.3 — Sheet description tweak.** Sheet description gains a one-line note appended to `_DAILY_STATEMENT_DESCRIPTION` (`apps/l1_dashboard/app.py:357`): "Account picker lists accounts with stored daily balances only (L2 control-account stubs that lack their own balance row are filtered out); pick a Role first to narrow the Account list." Wording diverged from the PLAN's "Internal accounts only. Filter by role to narrow further." because AA.B.2's empirical sweep showed it's not strictly internal-only — 1 ExternalCounterparty stays visible (the "tracked external" with its own balance row), so "stored daily balances only" is the accurate framing. Cross-references AA.B.1's Role cascade. 2198 unit + json tests green (Sheet `__post_init__` would raise on a blank description, the non-empty edit is safe).
- [x] **AA.B.4 — Browser e2e + commit.** Done. New `tests/e2e/test_l1_account_filters.py::test_daily_statement_role_dropdown_narrows_account_options` parametrized over `[qs, app2]` — opens Daily Statement, snapshots the full Account universe, iterates the Role dropdown's actual advertised values until it finds one that produces a narrowable cascade, then asserts `narrowed_set ⊊ full_set` AND `len(full) > len(narrowed)`. Data-agnostic by design (no hardcoded role names — the L2 may declare any roles; only the *cascade behavior* is universal). The `(a)` assertion ("no external rows") drops in spirit because the AA.B.2 audit empirically confirmed `DS_L1_ACCOUNTS` already excludes accounts without daily-balance rows (the External-counterparty *with* its own balance row is the explicit kept-case), so the test focuses on the new contract (role cascade) rather than re-asserting AA.B.2's already-verified shape. AA.B.2 commit summary noted `current_daily_balances` is the source — that's the structural filter, no e2e add needed. Live verify rolls with AA.A.5's full chain pass.
- [x] **AA.B.5 — App2Driver.pick_filter routes through TomSelect.setValue.** Done. Chain `c1ed613` had 2 lingering [app2] Daily Statement failures even after the AA.B.4.followon `hx-sync="this:replace"` render.py fix made all 6 visuals re-fetch — picks of `Customer 11 (cust-011)` produced post-pick URLs with `param_pL1DsAccount=` empty. Root cause: TomSelect's internal `Sync` runs in response to mutations on the underlying `<select>` and overwrites a manual `option.selected = true` with its own (empty) items store. Direct DOM evidence in the captured `dom.html`: zero `<option selected>` attributes after pick. Fix in `tests/e2e/_drivers/app2.py::pick_filter` — branch on `select.tomselect` and call `setValue(...)` (resolved text→value via the option map). Plain-mutation path retained as fallback for the offline-CDN degraded case (`typeof TomSelect === "undefined"`). New regression test `test_app2_pick_filter_persists_in_underlying_select` in `tests/e2e/test_dashboard_driver.py` pins the contract against the underlying form element — runs in app2 layer (no AWS). Why this didn't surface in the smoke parity tests already: `test_app2_pick_filter_changes_kpi` measures KPI delta after a `View → "detail"` pick on the showcase sheet, and the smoke fetcher's KPI formula `47 + sum(ord(view_value)) % 50` happens to differ for `view=""` (47) vs `view="detail"` (74), so the bug DID slip past it pre-fix — kept the test, added the explicit `select.value` pin on top so a future regression of the same shape lands as a clear "select.value should be 'detail'; got ''" rather than a noisy KPI delta. **Confirmed via post-fix chain `33ad8a4`:** the URL log now shows 9 requests with `param_pL1DsAccount=Customer%2011%20(cust-011)` post-pick — the pick reaches the URL correctly. The TomSelect fix is doing its job.
- [x] **AA.B.5.followon.2 — Data-driven Daily Statement filter picker (DB-queries-for-known-good-(account, day)).** Shipped in commit `6387344` (helper `tests/e2e/_daily_statement_pick.py::find_account_day_with_data`, `DashboardDriver.set_date` verb, both Daily Statement tests rewritten). Chain `952ab9b` confirmed [qs] turned green; calendar dependency removed. Triage of chain `bqaak83tb` (4 failures: 2 [app2] + 2 [qs]) surfaced that `[qs]` regressed from 0→2 between chain `33ad8a4` (passing) and `edbfe99` (failing) on the *same code* — pure calendar luck. Mechanism: both Daily Statement tests picked `options[0]` (alphabetical first account = `Customer 11`) and left the Business Day picker at its `RollingDate=yesterday` default. Prev chain ran at 23:48 UTC May 16 → "yesterday" = May 15 → cust-011 had 11 tx → passed. This chain at 00:48 UTC May 17 → "yesterday" = May 16 → cust-011 had 0 tx (only 4 accounts had any) → QS faithfully rendered "No data found" → test failed. Fix in `tests/e2e/_daily_statement_pick.py::find_account_day_with_data(cfg) -> (account_display, account_role, business_day_iso)`: SQL queries `<prefix>_transactions` for the most-recent (account, day) pair with most rows that day; both Daily Statement browser tests now drive all three filter pickers (Role / Account / Business Day) to those values. New `DashboardDriver.set_date(label, iso)` verb — drives single-value DateTimePicker (currently only L1 Daily Statement "Business Day"). QS impl reuses `set_parameter_datetime_value`; App2 impl is a no-op (App2 skips `add_parameter_datetime_picker` during filter-spec derivation today, so date narrowing is QS-only). Doesn't fix the [app2] partial-refetch bug (still tracked at AA.B.5.followon); does decouple [qs] from calendar position so the next chain stays green on clock-skew.
- [x] **AA.B.5.followon — App2 partial-refetch (3-of-6 visuals miss refresh) — fixed via queue-last + per-visual trigger + skeleton.** Shipped in commits `11c02b0` (hx-sync queue-last) + `a2d0ab9` (per-visual trigger + skeleton + skeleton-absence wait). Root cause was three concurrent bugs: (1) HTMX `hx-sync="this:replace"` failed to issue the new request after aborting the in-flight under parallel-load + mid-load pick — switched to `this:queue last`; (2) `htmx.trigger(body, 'refresh')` broadcast silently dropped on 2-3 visuals depending on which were mid-load — replaced with explicit per-visual `htmx.trigger(div, 'refresh')` iteration; (3) `App2Driver._wait_for_refetch`'s first-response + networkidle pattern returned before queued refreshes fired — replaced with skeleton-absence polling (`.visual-data:not(:has(.visual-loading))`). Skeleton element itself doubles as a UX improvement (300ms-delayed shimmer for slow loads) AND the per-visual "is loading?" detection signal — gives App2 a comparable readiness spec to QuickSight's `analysis_visual`. Chain `a2d0ab9` confirmed 0 failures across all 51 browser tests after the fix. Continued from AA.B.5 fix verification. Established with high confidence: server + bind path + SQL pipeline are ALL correct. Evidence: (1) Direct DB query for `cust-011` returns 349 transactions; (2) `make_tree_db_fetcher` called with `{'param_pL1DsAccount': ['Customer 11 (cust-011)']}` returns 50 rows + total_rows=349; (3) Direct Playwright repro pointing at the same live Aurora with the same cfg (`/tmp/repro_v3.py` — committed evidence captured in this PLAN entry, script not retained): all 6 visuals fire fresh requests with the picked value on `setValue`, no race. **But the chain `33ad8a4` shows only 3 of 6 visuals receive the with-value request** (per-visual breakdown from stdout.log: `9fbe0cb9/ac3a085b/44e0dc11` = 9 empty + 3 with-val each; `a7b73e03/08f76a41/98deed9f` = 9 empty + 0 with-val each — Posted Money Records is in the all-empty group). So three visuals' refresh broadcast is being dropped somehow under the test-runner's exact conditions. Likely culprits: pytest-xdist parallelism + the App2 server's shared connection pool + `hx-sync="this:replace"` race where the initial-load request is still in-flight when pick fires and the replace strategy doesn't actually replace the way HTMX documents. **Can't reliably triage further without seeing the in-chain network sequence per visual** — the existing failure-capture's `network.txt` filtered to non-2xx, so 200-with-empty-rows looked identical to "no request fired" → invisible. Fixed the diagnostic in `c7e4161` (every `/visuals/*/data` response now captured regardless of status). Next chain run that hits this failure will surface the per-visual request order + timing in the artifact, making the actual root cause diagnosable from artifacts alone. Until then: 2 [app2] Daily Statement tests stay red (DO NOT skip / xfail — the test is checking a real contract; the failure flagging the bug is useful signal). User-flagged adjacent: live deployed QS dashboard at `quicksight->L1 (qsgen-sp_pg_aw)->pending aging->stuck pending detail` shows the QS "duplicate columns" error — separate bug tracked at AA.A.8.

### AA.C — Exception literacy (sticky on-sheet panel + trainer pane) *(independent sub-phase — can land on its own branch/commits + timeline; doesn't gate on AA.A/B/D/E/H)*

The L1_Invariants.md parser + sheet-bottom panels + Studio trainer pane are orthogonal to the dropdown flips (AA.A), Daily Statement fixes (AA.B), label renames (AA.D), and account search (AA.E). Can branch off `main` (or off `phase-aa` after AA.A.5 closes) and ship independently — AA.F end-of-phase tag will bundle whatever's landed by then, and missing AA.C work would just slip into the next tag.

Operators don't crack open the manual. The exception-type vocabulary + remediation guidance has to live where they're already looking. Source of truth is `src/quicksight_gen/docs/L1_Invariants.md` (already structured per-invariant under `### N. <name>` headings) — the panel content reads from there at generate time, not net-new prose.

### AA.E — Search by name AND id

- [x] **AA.E.1 — Decide pattern (concat calc field vs two-column table vs smart input).** Decision: **hybrid — concat `name (id)` in dropdowns, two-column adjacent in tables.** Survey confirmed (a) every L1 table that shows an account already renders `account_id, account_name` as two adjacent columns (no operator complaint about it, sortability + per-column conditional formatting are real benefits), and (b) all 7 L1 account-pickers (Drift / Drift Timelines / Overdraft / Limit Breach / Daily Statement / Transactions / Pending Aging) read only `account_id` — the operator can type the raw id but not the name. Investigation Account-Network anchor already does dropdown-concat (`source_account_name || ' (' || source_account_id || ')' AS source_display` in `apps/investigation/datasets.py`) — this just extends the same pattern to L1. Option (c) "single search input" rejected because QS has no native table-cell search widget; building one in both renderers is out of phase scope. Audit doc at `docs/audits/aa_e_1_account_search_pattern.md`; lists the 7 dropdowns to flip in AA.E.2.
- [x] **AA.E.2 — Wire across affected sheets.** Done. QS's `LinkedValues` carries ONE column (label == value), so the dropdown bind value IS the displayed display string (not a separate bare id). Implementation:<br>**(a)** Extended `DS_L1_ACCOUNTS` SQL to project `account_name` + `account_display = account_name || ' (' || account_id || ')'`; added both to `L1_ACCOUNTS_CONTRACT` (`account_display` carries `ColumnShape.ACCOUNT_DISPLAY`).<br>**(b)** New helper `_account_display_clause(param_name)` in `apps/l1_dashboard/datasets.py` — inline-concat WHERE shape `('__l1_all__' = <<$p>> OR (account_name || ' (' || account_id || ')') = <<$p>>)`. Same sentinel-guard as `_data_value_clause`, so show-all on initial load is unchanged. Avoids having to extend every consuming dataset's SELECT — every L1 matview already exposes `account_name` + `account_id` so the inline concat works portably (PG / Oracle / SQLite all share `||`).<br>**(c)** Flipped 8 WHERE clauses: 7 went `_data_value_clause('account_id', P_L1_*_ACCOUNT)` → `_account_display_clause(P_L1_*_ACCOUNT)` (drift x2 / overdraft / limit_breach / todays_exc / tx / pending / unbundled); the 2 Daily Statement bare `account_id = <<$pL1DsAccount>>` sites inlined the same `(account_name || ' (' || account_id || ')')` concat (the special `_L1_DS_ACCOUNT_SENTINEL` start-empty default still matches no real display string, preserving the "pick an account first" behaviour).<br>**(d)** Flipped 7 dropdown callsites in `apps/l1_dashboard/app.py`: `options_column="account_id"` → `options_column="account_display"`.<br>**(e)** Unit tests in `tests/unit/test_aa_a_single_value_clauses.py`: 3 new `test_aa_e_2_account_display_clause_*` tests pin the shape / sentinel / name-then-id concat ordering. 87 unit + json tests green in the touched suites; full json suite 450 green.<br>Live verify rolls into AA.E.3 (browser e2e). The 7-callsite flip lands atomically because every dropdown reads the same `DS_L1_ACCOUNTS` — the dropdown options + the consuming WHERE clauses must match the display shape together, so a partial flip would break the dropdowns that still read `account_id`.
- [x] **AA.E.3 — Browser e2e + commit (caught + fixed AA.E.2 silent-empty miss).** Done. New `tests/e2e/test_l1_account_filters.py` parametrized over `[qs, app2]` carries two tests: **(a)** `test_account_dropdown_shows_display_form` walks all 6 L1 sheets carrying an Account picker (Drift / Overdraft / Limit Breach / Today's Exceptions / Daily Statement / Transactions) and asserts every Account dropdown advertises ≥1 option matching the `"<name> (<id>)"` shape ('name (id)' substring) — catches a future regression that flips the dropdown back to bare-id. Pending Aging + Unbundled Aging are structurally identical, excluded for runtime parsimony (same `options_column="account_display"` flip applies, JSON-pinned by AA.E.2's unit tests). **(b)** `test_daily_statement_picked_account_narrows_table` picks the first Account option from the display dropdown, then asserts the Daily Statement summary table renders ≥1 row post-pick — the end-to-end "picked account → data shows up" contract. **Caught the AA.E.2 miss:** the Daily Statement's direct `add_parameter_dropdown` (line 2069 in `apps/l1_dashboard/app.py`) still bound `account_id` while the WHERE clause expected the display-format concat — every pick left the page silently empty. **Fixed in this commit:** flipped to `datasets[DS_L1_ACCOUNTS]["account_display"]`. New JSON pin `tests/json/test_l1_dashboard.py::test_aa_e_2_daily_statement_account_dropdown_binds_display_column` walks the Daily Statement Account `ParameterDropdownControl`'s `LinkedValues.column_name` and asserts `"account_display"` (regression guard for the dropdown's wiring shape — would catch the original miss at unit-test speed instead of waiting for the browser layer). 88 unit + json tests green in the touched suites. Live AW verify rolls into AA.F.1's chain pass.

### AA.G — Dependabot fixes *(COMPLETE — pre-phase-AA)*

- [x] **AA.G — Dependabot urllib3 alerts closed.** Two high-severity alerts on default branch (GHSA-mf9v-mfxr-j63j decompression-bomb; GHSA-qccp-gfcp-xxvc cross-origin header forwarding), both urllib3, both fixed by the bump to ≥ 2.7.0 in commit `c0c2d2f` ("deps: urllib3 2.6.3 → 2.7.0 (2 high CVEs)") before Phase AA branched. uv.lock at 2.7.0; suite stayed green on subsequent main merges; both alerts now `state:fixed` per `gh api dependabot/alerts`.
- [x] **AA.G.1 — Bump urllib3 to ≥ 2.7.0.** Shipped in `c0c2d2f`; uv.lock at 2.7.0.
- [x] **AA.G.2 — Verify suite stays green.** Implicit — `c0c2d2f` is on main and subsequent merges have flown through CI.
- [x] **AA.G.3 — Confirm Dependabot closes the alerts.** Both alerts now `state:fixed`.

### AA.H — Browser-capture infra fix *(landed mid-phase; AA.A.5 triage exposed the gap)*

The `webkit_page` failure-capture path was silently broken for parametrized e2e tests — the May 16 Money Trail anchor failure dropped zero artifacts (no screenshot, no console, no qs_errors, no network), and the most recent legacy artifacts in `tests/e2e/screenshots/_failures/` were 12 days old (pre-parametrize refactor). Triage required reading SQL + tree code to guess; if the capture had worked we'd have had DOM + screenshot in seconds.

- [x] **AA.H.1 — Sanitize test_id chars.** Added `_sanitize_test_id` in `common/browser/helpers.py` — collapses any non-`[A-Za-z0-9_\-\[\].]` char (or run thereof) to a single `_`. Brackets stay (parametrize ID disambiguation); spaces / em-dashes / parens / colons collapse. Filename is now portable across macOS APFS / ext4 / NTFS / GHA artifact zip / shell-glob.
- [x] **AA.H.2 — Snapshot test_id at `webkit_page` entry.** `PYTEST_CURRENT_TEST` is reliably set inside the test body but can be cleared by the time fixture teardown runs the `except` handler — silently demoting captures to `unknown/`. Resolve once at entry, pass down to every `_capture_failure_*` function.
- [x] **AA.H.3 — Add `dom.html` capture.** New 6th artifact: `page.content()` → `<capture_dir>/dom.html`. Pairs with the screenshot — pixels show what's visually there, DOM shows what the test's selectors were actually looking at. The single most-useful diagnostic for "click target not found" / "control didn't mount" failures (which is exactly the Money Trail shape).
- [x] **AA.H.4 — Loud-fail capture exceptions.** New `_warn_capture_failure(artifact, exc)` helper emits a `[CAPTURE FAILURE] <artifact>: <type>: <msg>` line to stderr. Replaces the 5× `except Exception: pass` silent-fail blocks. Test failure still surfaces as the primary error (sidecar contract); but a capture-path regression now lands in the layer's `stderr.log` instead of being invisible until the next forensic session.
- [x] **AA.H.5 — Regression guard test.** New `test_failure_path_handles_parametrized_test_id_with_specials` (in `tests/unit/test_browser_trace_smoke.py`) reproduces the exact `PYTEST_CURRENT_TEST` shape that bit us — `[qs-Money Trail-Chain root transfer-Money Trail — Hop-by-Hop]` with spaces, em-dash, parens, brackets — and asserts all 6 artifacts land under a sanitized capture dir. Plus 6 new `TestSanitizeTestId` unit tests covering edge cases (alphanumeric kept, run collapsing, paren/colon stripping). 27 browser-helper tests green; 1755 full unit suite green.
- [x] **AA.H.6 — Wire fixture-path capture (the real bug).** AA.H.1-5 were necessary but not sufficient: the chain after AA.H still dropped zero artifacts for the Money Trail failure. Real root cause = pytest's yield-fixture semantics. When a test fails, pytest does NOT re-throw the exception into the fixture's generator — the `with webkit_page(...)` block exits cleanly, and `webkit_page`'s `except BaseException:` never fires. The AA.H.5 regression test passed because it raises *inside* the `with` block in the same stack frame, which is a different code path. Fix: (a) `webkit_page` now attaches `_qs_gen_console_sink` / `_qs_gen_network_sink` / `_qs_gen_test_id` to the page object so callers can read them from outside the `with` block. (b) New public `trigger_failure_capture(page, *, test_id=None)` writes all 6 artifacts on demand; sets `_qs_gen_capture_triggered` so the trace.zip lands too. (c) `_parametrized_dashboard_driver` post-yield check: `_maybe_capture_on_failure(request, driver)` consults `request.node.rep_call.failed` (set by the existing `pytest_runtest_makereport` hook) and invokes `trigger_failure_capture` with the sanitized nodeid as the test_id. Works for both `QsEmbedDriver._page` and `App2Driver.page` (duck-typed). New regression test `test_explicit_trigger_writes_all_artifacts_for_pytest_fixture_path` simulates the fixture path — exits the `with` block cleanly but invokes the trigger mid-block, asserts all 6 artifacts cluster under the override test_id (including trace.zip, which would have otherwise orphaned to the entry-time test_id). 1756 unit + 28 browser tests green.
- [x] **AA.H.7 — Search-variant DOM dispatch (initial guess).** Money Trail anchor failure persisted across 4 chains because `_open_control_dropdown` only knew the simple variant (`sheet_control_value` trigger). AA.H.6's capture surfaced that 8080-option QS dropdowns swap to a Material-UI Select with `sheet_control_search_results_dropdown` trigger; `sheet_control_value` isn't in the DOM at all. Added dispatch on selector presence: try simple-variant trigger first, fall back to search-variant. Wait-for-popover step now accepts either container automation-id. Quirks log entry 3.7 captures the divergence. Wrong popover-id assumption in this entry — corrected in AA.H.8.
- [x] **AA.H.8 — MUI Autocomplete lazy-render (the actual fix).** Chain `bf40ntdxd` showed AA.H.7's dispatch worked (the helper found the search-variant trigger and clicked it) but the option-wait still timed out at 2s. DOM dump revealed: (a) the search-variant popover container is `sheet_control_search_results_dropdown-menu` (suffix `-menu`), NOT `sheet_control_menu_dropdown` — my AA.H.7 guess was a wrong path name from selector inference; (b) the popover holds a `MuiAutocomplete-root` widget whose `[role="option"]` items are virtualized and don't render on open — the autocomplete input must take typed input (or ArrowDown) before the listbox mounts. Fix: (1) `_open_control_dropdown` now waits for the popover container (correct ID), then if a search input is present, focuses it + presses ArrowDown to force the listbox to render before the option-wait fires. (2) `set_dropdown_value` now types the requested `value` into the search input before clicking — handles both variants transparently, so `pick_filter` Just Works regardless of cardinality. Driver-level encapsulation per user direction: "the mui autocomplete handling should be something exercised by the driver so its not test specific" — no special-purpose verb on the QS driver; tests stay renderer-agnostic. Quirks log entry 3.7 rewritten to call out the MUI Autocomplete lazy-render + the correct popover ID. New browser e2e `test_money_trail_anchor_pick_narrows_hop_by_hop_table` exercises the type+select path through `pick_filter` (discover an option via `filter_options`, pick it, assert the Hop-by-Hop table re-fetches non-empty rows for that root) — fails on both renderers if the search-variant path regresses. 2198 unit + json tests green; pyright strict on `common/browser/helpers.py` clean.
- [x] **AA.H.10 — Wire capture hook into all 3 QS-driver fixtures.** AA.H.6 wired the post-yield `_maybe_capture_on_failure` hook into `_parametrized_dashboard_driver` only — `qs_driver` (`conftest.py:130`) and `per_dialect_qs_driver` (`test_audit_dashboard_agreement.py:343`) both silently dropped artifacts on failure. Today's `20260516T203824Z-914fc4c` chain lost all 4 audit-agreement failures' DOM + screenshot + trace.zip for exactly that reason — triage cost +1 round-trip. Fix: lifted the helper to `tests/e2e/_capture.py::maybe_capture_on_failure`; conftest.py + `test_audit_dashboard_agreement.py` both import + invoke it post-yield. New static regression guard `tests/unit/test_failure_capture_fixture_wiring.py` AST-walks the three fixture functions and asserts each contains the capture call — a future new QS-driver fixture without the wiring will fail this test loudly instead of going to production with silent drops. 1810 unit + json tests green; no-playwright-leak lint stays clean (the new `_capture.py` carries the existing `# typing-smell: ignore[no-playwright-leak]: <reason>` marker that the conftest helper used).
- [x] **AA.H.11 — Replace `count_table_total_rows`'s time-based wait with WS settle.** AA.H.10's wiring gave us our first real failure-capture haul: 4 audit-agreement `qs_count=0` failures with screenshots showing populated tables (2 rows visibly mounted, `sn-table-cell-0-*`/`sn-table-cell-1-*` in the DOM dump). NOT the QS silent-fail footgun — `count_table_total_rows` was returning 0 against tables that visibly had data. Root cause: the bundled helper unconditionally clicked the page-size-bump menu (`simplePagedDisplayNav_*`), then `wait_for_timeout(500)` for the re-fetch, then scroll-accumulated. On cold sheets the 500ms wait raced QS's re-fetch (sometimes lands at 200ms, sometimes at 1500ms); on small tables (≤10 rows) the page-size control isn't even in the DOM, so the timed wait was burning 500ms for no reason. User direction: *"skip page-size bump on small tables but also on big ones, wait for the settle. I consider time based waits (as opposed to timeouts) to be a major smell/failure source"*. Fix: split the helper into 3 primitives — `table_is_paginated(page, visual_title) -> bool` (cheap DOM probe for `simplePagedDisplayNav_*` presence), `bump_table_page_size_to_10000(page, visual_title, timeout_ms) -> bool` (just clicks, no timed wait), `count_table_total_rows` simplified to scroll-only. `QsEmbedDriver.table_row_count` orchestrates: scroll_into_view → cheap probe → return DOM count if no pagination → else bump + `_settle_after_param_change()` (the WS-frame-keyed settle from X.2.r — drains `sent_START - sent_STOP` to zero + 300ms quiet window) → scroll-accumulate. The WS settle replaces the timed wait — event-driven, can't race. Quirks log §3.3 updated with the bundled-helper race + the fix. Commit `603c354`. 2 browser e2e affected (audit-agreement + `test_total_rows_post_bump`) now stable across cold-sheet repros.
- [x] **AA.H.12 — Lift QS embed lifecycle into shared primitive.** User flagged on review of AA.H.10: *"why do we have 3 different quicksight drivers? sounds like duplication that will blow up in our faces"* — exactly right. The 3 QS-driver fixtures (`qs_driver`, `_parametrized_dashboard_driver`'s qs branch, `per_dialect_qs_driver`) each open-coded the same {`get_user_arn()` gate + `QsEmbedDriver.embed(...)` context manager + `maybe_capture_on_failure(request, driver)` post-yield} lifecycle. AA.H.10 just bit us on exactly this duplication — capture hook missing from 2 of 3 because the AA.H.6 author only wired one. Fix: new `tests/e2e/_drivers/_lifecycle.py::qs_driver_or_none` context manager owns the whole lifecycle once. The 3 fixtures collapse to thin policy-shaped wrappers that express only their distinguishers — `qs_driver` (skip on missing ARN, scalar yield, default viewport); `_parametrized_dashboard_driver`'s qs branch (skip on missing ARN OR missing dashboard, scalar yield, default viewport); `per_dialect_qs_driver` (yield-None on missing ARN so 3-way fallback still runs, tall `(1600, 4000)` viewport for stacked-layout audit sheets). Why a context manager not a fixture: fixture-level abstraction can't easily express the policy knobs (skip vs yield-None, yield shape, viewport) without an explosion of fixture variants. Static guard `tests/unit/test_failure_capture_fixture_wiring.py` updated to accept either wiring shape (`_maybe_capture_on_failure` direct call OR `qs_driver_or_none` lifecycle call); new `test_lifecycle_primitive_lives_at_shared_path` pins the helper module's existence + asserts it calls `maybe_capture_on_failure` internally (so deleting the lifecycle without inlining doesn't silently break capture across the suite); `test_parametrized_dashboard_driver_wires_capture_hook` now asserts BOTH branches (qs via lifecycle, app2 via inlined hook) so a one-sided regression fails loudly. Commit `3cc704c`.
- [x] **AA.H.11.followon — `scroll_visual_into_view` watches QS's empty-overlay marker, not the timeout.** AA.H.11's chain (`bgruxlztr`) settled with 3 NEW QS failures the prior chain didn't have — `test_inv_anchor_control_present_and_populated[qs-{Money Trail, Account Network}-*]` and `test_money_trail_anchor_pick_narrows_hop_by_hop_table[qs]` — all hitting `Page.wait_for_function: Timeout 15000ms exceeded` inside `scroll_visual_into_view` during `table_row_count`. Captured DOM (thanks to AA.H.10) showed: visual mounted fine, `grid-container count: 0`, `qs_errors.txt` empty, `visual-overlay-title` with `data-automation-context="No data"` present. Root cause: empty tables (matview returned zero rows) don't mount `.grid-container`, so `scroll_visual_into_view`'s wait-for-`sn-table-cell-0-0` predicate timed out at the full visual_timeout instead of cleanly reporting 0. Pre-AA.H.11 the bundled `count_table_total_rows` wrapped the scroll in try/except with a plain-JS fallback; the AA.H.11 helper-split dropped it. **Two-commit fix.** First commit `12e9f8a` restored the try/except pattern with a tight 5 s window (symptomatic fix). User asked the right follow-up: *"is there something we could do to avoid those timeouts? something to watch on?"* — yes. QS already emits a positive signal we weren't watching for: any visual whose backing dataset returned zero rows mounts `[data-automation-id="visual-overlay-title"][data-automation-context="No data"]` inside its container at render time (~200 ms after sheet load), same shape for table / Sankey / chart / KPI. Second commit `18634fe` implements the proper fix: (a) new `common/browser/helpers.py::visual_is_empty` (cheap DOM probe, no waits); (b) `scroll_visual_into_view`'s predicate races `sn-table-cell-0-0` OR the empty overlay — either mounting means "settled" — so empty visuals settle in their natural render time (~200 ms vs the prior 15 s timeout, ~75× faster); (c) `QsEmbedDriver.table_row_count` replaces the try/except sentinel with explicit `visual_is_empty` short-circuit. The race is safe — a visual is either populated or shows the overlay, never both. **Lesson generalizes**: positive signal beats negative timeout. Anywhere we're catching a timeout to infer state, there's usually a DOM marker we can watch for instead. Quirks log §3.3 updated with the AA.H.11.followon entry.
- [x] **AA.H.13 — `expand_all_tables_on_sheet` deleted; was dead code.** Originally filed as a same-class fix for the AA.H.11 race shape (page-size bump → `wait_for_timeout(500)`). Caller audit revealed it has **zero live references** — defined in `common/browser/helpers.py` and used nowhere across `src/`, `tests/`, `scripts/`. Historical context: written in `09e8f16` for the X.1.c "Sasquatch L1 flake" fix (the harness `_active_sheet_text` walk read truncated table text; this helper bumped page-size to 10000 first so all rows mounted). The harness assertion path it served was later replaced by targeted per-visual reads (`table_rows` / `table_row_count`), but the dead helper survived. Per CLAUDE.md "if you are certain that something is unused, you can delete it completely" — deleted. No design choice needed (the spike A-vs-B framing in the original entry was moot).
- [x] **AA.H.13.followon — full dead-helpers sweep of `common/browser/helpers.py`.** AA.H.13's "is anything else dead?" audit found **15 more functions with zero external + zero internal references** — 333 lines of stale helpers from old test patterns that survived their callers' migration. Includes the 4 `wait_for_*_to_change` poll-rate limiters I had previously classified as "acceptable" — but they're never *called*, so the polling pattern is moot (same lesson as expand_all_tables: AA.H.13.x). Round 1 (commit `673be71`, 89 lines, 3 functions): spot-checked `click_chart_bar` (canvas-keyboard bar-click, 48 lines — the one I'd flagged as "intrinsic to canvas, can't fix" in the AA.H.13 audit), `set_slider_range` (43-line range-slider variant, sibling of `set_parameter_slider_value` which IS used), `parse_kpi_number` (KPI text→number parser; consumers parse inline instead). Round 2 (commit `cea2c84`, 214 lines, 12 functions): `wait_for_visuals_rendered`, `selected_sheet_name`, `wait_for_sheet_tab`, `wait_for_table_cells_present`, `first_table_cell_text`, `wait_for_sheet_controls_present`, `wait_for_table_total_rows_to_change`, `wait_for_chart_categories_to_change`, `read_visual_column_values`, `wait_for_kpi_text_nonempty`, `wait_for_kpi_value_to_change`, `wait_for_table_nonzero`. Method: AST-driven delete script (not naive line-range — initial naive attempt scooped up `_OPTION_SELECTOR` module-level constant between sibling defs; AST traversal correctly preserves module-level statements between functions). Verified: 12 unit tests (browser-trace-smoke + failure-capture-fixture wiring + typing-smells) pass; pyright strict clean. **303 lines total** removed across rounds 1+2.

### AA backlog — items intentionally deferred

Items below were uncovered during AA work but explicitly deferred — either backlog tag or a spike-before-locking gate. Carried here so the AA active surface stays focused; rehome when a real driver picks one up.

- [ ] **AA.A.l2ft-rails-inverse.4 — Type-encode the invariant.** Backlog: `table_rows()` for narrowing-assertion sites is a smell — the picker-row-survival contract is about SQL row count, not DOM visibility. Consider deprecating `len(table_rows())` for assertion use, or naming it `dom_visible_rows()` so the cap is obvious at call sites.
- [ ] **AA.A.daterange.3 (BACKLOGGED) — Structural refactor: single DATE_RANGE control.** Replace each sheet's `(ParameterDateTimePickerControl Date From + ParameterDateTimePickerControl Date To + TimeRangeFilter)` triplet with one `FilterDateTimePickerControl(Type="DATE_RANGE")`. Closes the "from > to" UX footgun structurally and aligns L1 / L2FT / Exec with Investigation. **Wall:** L1's multi-dataset-per-sheet model (Drift sheet has `_scope_one(DS_DRIFT, ...) + _scope_one(DS_LEDGER_DRIFT, ...)`) needs a sharing mechanism — the filter-bound widget pattern Investigation uses binds to ONE filter on ONE dataset. Options: (a) consolidate L1 datasets per sheet (schema work), (b) accept one widget per dataset per sheet (UX noise), (c) find a QS mechanism for one widget driving multiple parameter-bound filters via parameter intermediates. Spike before locking direction.
- [ ] **AA.A.daterange.4 (BACKLOGGED) — App2 renderer for widget-bound DATE_RANGE.** Already proven for Investigation; would extend to the new L1/L2FT/Exec range controls.
- [ ] **AA.A.daterange.5 (BACKLOGGED) — Test infra.** `apply_anchor_to_pickers` for date pickers becomes "set the range to span anchor's date ±1 day" instead of separate from/to. Single picker spec, not two.
- [ ] **AA.A.10 (stretch) — Tree-walk picker→column derivation.** Even after AA.A.9, `PickerSpec.column` is still hand-mapped (1 line per picker referencing the dataset projection column). The tree carries the wiring formally: `ParameterControl.parameter` → `Parameter.mapped_dataset_params` → `(dataset, dataset_param_name)` → dataset SQL's `<<$p>>` substitution site → the column it compares. Either parse the dataset SQL to find the column the param narrows on, OR annotate `DataSetParameter` with a `narrows_column` field at construction time (production-code surface change). Result: spec carries only sheet/visual/builder/order — every PickerSpec disappears, the helper derives the full picker→column map from the tree. Same "generic over the problem" principle as the DashboardDriver protocol — 80-90% of sheets covered by the generic walk, bespoke escape hatch for the odd cases (e.g. account_display concat format). Plan + spike before locking the annotation-vs-parse path.

## 2026-05-19

- [x] AB.1 Enhancement 4: LimitSchedule per-direction caps (Outbound + Inbound)
  - [x] AB.1.0 Locks (3 decisions before .1 fires, 2026-05-19).
  - **Enum**: new `LimitDirection(OUTBOUND, INBOUND)` at the primitives layer (NOT reusing `Amount.Direction.Debit/Credit`). Reason: `Amount.Direction` is the accounting / entry-side perspective; `LimitDirection` is the cap-policy / flow-perspective. Conflating them invites the Z.B-class footgun where `LimitSchedule.transfer_type` got matched against the wrong column shape. YAML uses `Inbound` / `Outbound` literals.
  - **Matview shape**: `UNION ALL` two SELECTs in `<prefix>_limit_breach` — one per direction, each filtered to `amount_direction = 'Debit'/'Credit'` AND its own direction-filtered cap CASE. Each output row carries an explicit `direction` column (no inference downstream). `_render_limit_breach_cases` gains a `direction` parameter; the matview emits twice.
  - **Default**: `direction=OUTBOUND` (gap doc §4(A) locked; backward-compat for every existing L2 instance not yet specifying).
  - [x] AB.1.1 SPEC + theorem. Done. SPEC.md: added `InboundFlow` theorem (line 131, mirror of OutboundFlow filtering on `Credit`); rewrote the "Limit breach" SHOULD-constraint to reference both theorems per LimitSchedule direction; updated the `LimitSchedule` entity definition (line 567-area) to declare the `Direction` field with the `Outbound` default + the load-time note that `(ParentRole, Rail, Direction)` uniqueness allows `(parent, rail)` to appear twice with different directions; updated the M.2d.2 uniqueness rule (line 667) to match. Schema_v6.md: noted the per-direction emit in the matview-tree diagram + extended the LimitSchedule-CASE-branch prose to describe the UNION ALL shape. L1_Invariants.md: rewrote section 5 ("Outbound flow cap" → "Per-direction flow cap"), updated the SHOULD-constraint blockquote to reference both theorems, expanded the body + columns to mention the new `direction` column, expanded the `**What to do:**` line to call out the AML-flag interpretation for Inbound breaches. Parser tests (`tests/unit/test_handbook_invariants.py`) stay green at 22/22 (the parser keys on heading shape + `**Columns:**` + `**What to do:**` markers — all preserved). The dashboard panel's body content + the trainer-pane card both regenerate from the doc automatically (AA.C.2 + AA.C.5). Sub-tasks of AB.1.2-.4 will follow with the code-side changes (primitives + loader + matview).
  - [x] AB.1.2 `primitives.py`: new `LimitDirection` enum + `direction: LimitDirection = "Outbound"` on LimitSchedule. Done. Style-aligned with existing `Scope` / `LegDirection` / `SupersedeReason` Literal aliases (codebase pattern, not a separate `enum.Enum`) — `LimitDirection: TypeAlias = Literal["Outbound", "Inbound"]`. New `direction` field placed between `cap` and `description`, default `"Outbound"` keeps every existing keyword/positional construction byte-equivalent. Smoke-verified construction + positional path; full L2 unit suite green (130 passed).
  - [x] AB.1.3 Loader + serializer + validator. Done. Loader: new `_load_limit_direction(raw, *, path)` mirrors `_load_scope` / `_load_leg_direction` — rejects anything outside `{"Outbound", "Inbound"}` with the actionable message. `_load_limit_schedule` reads `raw_d.get("direction", "Outbound")` so unset YAMLs default cleanly. Serializer: `_dump_limit_schedule` emits `direction:` ONLY when non-default (`!= "Outbound"`) — every pre-AB.1 YAML is byte-equivalent through load+dump. Validator U5: broadened from `(parent_role, rail)` to `(parent_role, rail, direction)` triple — same `(parent, rail)` may now appear twice as long as direction differs. Header docstring + body updated with the AB.1 reason. Smoke-verified all 7 round-trip behaviors (default omit / explicit emit / load explicit / load default / reject bogus / U5 reject same-direction dup / U5 allow Outbound+Inbound on same parent+rail). Full L2 unit suite green (130 passed).
  - [x] AB.1.4 `schema.py`: `<prefix>_limit_breach` matview UNION ALL two direction-branches. Done. `_render_limit_breach_cases(instance, *, p, dialect, direction="Outbound")` filters inlined CASE branches to LimitSchedules matching `direction`; an empty filter result returns typed-NULL so the branch contributes zero breach rows after the outer `cap IS NOT NULL` filter (an L2 with zero Inbound caps stays cleanly empty without conditional template surgery). Matview's body is now `SELECT * FROM (Outbound-SELECT UNION ALL Inbound-SELECT) flow_with_cap WHERE cap IS NOT NULL AND outbound_total > cap`. Each branch carries a literal `'Outbound'` / `'Inbound'` direction column in the projection + filters on `amount_direction='Debit'`/`'Credit'` accordingly. New `idx_<p>_lb_direction` index. `LIMIT_BREACH_CONTRACT` extended with `ColumnSpec("direction", "STRING")` so `SELECT * FROM matview` projection matches the 9-column dataset shape on both PG and Oracle (the Oracle wrapper aliases by contract). Visual rendering of the column lands in AB.1.8. Verified the new matview SQL emits cleanly on PG / Oracle / SQLite; unit + schema + data + json + cli + audit suites green (2878 passed).
  - [x] AB.1.5 `auto_scenario.py`: new `InboundCapBreachPlant`. Done. New `InboundCapBreachPlant` dataclass in `common/l2/seed.py` (mirror of `LimitBreachPlant`); new `_emit_inbound_cap_breach_rows` emits Credit customer leg + Debit external counter (`Origin=ExternalForcePosted`, flips Outbound's `InternalInitiated`). `ScenarioPlant` gains `inbound_cap_breach_plants` field; `emit_seed` dispatches the new plants. `auto_scenario._pick_inbound_breach_inputs` mirrors `_pick_breach_inputs` but filters LimitSchedules by `direction=="Inbound"` and resolves an inbound 2-leg rail + external source counter. Existing `_pick_breach_inputs` narrowed to `direction=="Outbound"`. Plant assembly mirror at `days_ago=3` (distinct from Outbound's `days_ago=4`). All 3 `ScenarioPlant` pass-through call sites (`boost_inv_fanout_plants`, broken-rail wrapper, only_template selector) carry the new field. `replicate_inbound_breach` densifier mirror lands. Seed-header stats line splits Outbound/Inbound counts. `test_auto_scenario` permits `InboundCapBreachPlant` omission for spec_example (no Inbound LS yet — covered in AB.1.5.spec). Re-locked all 3 spec_example seeds (pg/oracle/sqlite). Full unit + schema + data + json + cli + audit suite green (2878 passed).
  - [x] AB.1.5.fuzz `tests/l2/fuzz.py`: emit `direction` on synthesized LimitSchedules. Today's chain `child:` field accepts Rail only. Two-template chains (e.g. `InternalTransferCycle → InternalTransferBatch`) force an awkward "pick one of the child template's leg_rails" workaround.

**Preferred shape** (gap doc §3): allow `child: TransferTemplate` symmetric to `parent: TransferTemplate`. Semantics: first leg_rail firing of the child template sets the shared Transfer's `Parent` via the firing's `parent_transfer_id` metadata; subsequent firings join via lookup-or-create without rewriting Parent.


- [ ] AB.2 Enhancement 3: Template-as-chain-child (symmetric with template-as-chain-parent)
  - [x] AB.2.0 Locks (3 decisions before .1 fires, 2026-05-19).
  - **Matview shape**: new dedicated `<prefix>_chain_parent_disagreement` matview, NOT folded into an existing matview. Reason: no existing matview is "Conservation-shape" by name — the PLAN suggestion to fold lacked a target. Naming follows the `_<violation_class>` pattern of the existing 6 L1 matviews (`_drift` / `_overdraft` / `_limit_breach` / `_stuck_pending` / `_stuck_unbundled` / `_supersession_audit`). Column shape mirrors `_limit_breach`: `transfer_id`, `child_template_name`, `parent_template_name`, `distinct_parent_count`, `business_day`, `parent_transfer_ids` (concat list for the table display).
  - **Validator rule (AB.2.2)**: auto-derive `parent_transfer_id` metadata-key from the chain relationship — when chain.children contains a TransferTemplate, every leg_rail of that template implicitly accepts `parent_transfer_id` as a posted metadata key, without requiring the operator to declare it in yaml. Reason: the chain relationship is the unique source of truth; requiring duplicate yaml declaration is friction with no information gain (and the validator's job is to enforce L2 grammar invariants, not to require operators to restate what's already inferable from related primitives). The validator surfaces a clear error message if a posted firing lacks `parent_transfer_id` at runtime — that's the AB.2.3 disagreement matview's concern, not load-time validation.
  - **Seed integration (AB.2.5)**: first-firing-wins — the first leg_rail firing of the child template emits a NEW Transfer (assigns `transfer_id`), subsequent leg_rail firings reuse that Transfer's id via lookup-on-`(template_name, parent_transfer_id, business_day)`. Reason: matches the gap-doc §3 narrative; the disagreement case (AB.2.3) is the L1 violation that surfaces when the lookup-key collides with a *different* parent_transfer_id (= ETL writing leg rows that disagree on which parent firing they belong to).
  - [x] AB.2.1 `loader.py`: chain `child:` accepts TransferTemplate identifier. Verified — no loader code change required. Loader does NOT reject; validator R5 already accepts both Rail and Template as `chain.children` entries (`validate.py:470-482` — "every Chain.parent and every Chain.children entry resolves to a Rail or Template"). What was unverified pre-AB.2: what happens downstream. **Confirmed silent-skip in seed**: `_emit_baseline_chains` at `seed.py:2442-2446` carries an explicit guard ("Chain references a TransferTemplate or unknown name — skip for R.2.d's first land.") — when child resolves to a template name, the chain firing emits zero rows. Topology also filters chain.children to `rail_names_set` at `topology.py:733` so template children don't enter the anchored_rails set. So today's behavior for a two-template chain: L2 loads cleanly, validates, serializes, BUT zero chain-firing rows land in `<prefix>_transactions` and the chain doesn't show on the topology diagram. AB.2.4/.5 replaces the silent-skip with a working seed path; AB.2.8 adds template-as-child to the topology renderer.

Filters: `transfer_parent_id IS NOT NULL`, `template_name IS NOT NULL` (rail-as-child chains don't have template identity so they don't false-positive), `status <> 'Failed'`. Today's C1 ("at most one Variable-direction leg per template") blocks the natural model for per-mode operating variants (e.g. `MerchantCardSaleAutoSettle` / `StandardSettle` / `SlowSettle` as Variable closing legs, exactly one firing per cycle based on merchant config).

**Preferred shape** (gap doc §1): restate C1 as "per *firing* across XOR-grouped legs"; add `leg_rail_xor_groups: [[v1, v2, v3]]` field on TransferTemplate, mirroring the chain XOR pattern. Validator rule: members must all appear in the template's leg_rails.


- [ ] AB.3 Enhancement 1: TransferTemplate multi-Variable + leg_rails XOR
  - [x] AB.3.0 Locks (3 decisions before .1 fires, 2026-05-19). Done — all 3 locks user-ratified (matview shape = dedicated `_xor_group_violation`; validator split = load-time structural + matview-runtime cardinality; seed integration = 2 plants both .5 missed + new .5b overlap). Mirrors AB.2.0 pattern; same close-the-door discipline before the sub-tasks touch code.
  - **Matview shape**: new dedicated `<prefix>_xor_group_violation` matview, NOT folded into PostedRequirements / Conservation. Naming follows the `_<violation_class>` pattern of the existing 7 L1 matviews (`_drift` / `_overdraft` / `_limit_breach` / `_stuck_pending` / `_stuck_unbundled` / `_supersession_audit` / `_chain_parent_disagreement`). Per-row: `transfer_id`, `template_name`, `xor_group_index` (0-based index into the template's `leg_rail_xor_groups`), `firing_count`, `fired_rails` (concat list of variant rail names that fired in this Transfer's window — supports both overlap and missed cases for analyst drill), `business_day` (MIN of posting day across the group's fired legs; for `firing_count=0` rows: the Transfer's Completion-deadline day, since the violation surfaces post-Completion). `GROUP BY (transfer_id, template_name, xor_group_index)` over `<prefix>_current_transactions`, joined against each template's `leg_rail_xor_groups` declaration, `HAVING firing_count <> 1`. Reason: C1 is a *firing cardinality* invariant (zero or ≥2 firings of XOR-grouped Variables in one Transfer), structurally distinct from Conservation (legs sum to expected_net) and from PostedRequirements (every leg has its declared metadata keys). Folding would conflate post-time / stuck-pending / cardinality classes that catch different ETL bugs and analyst-route to different remediation queues. UNION ALL branch into `<prefix>_todays_exceptions` follows the AB.1 / AB.2 pattern (`check_type='xor_group_violation'`, `template_name AS rail_name`, `firing_count AS magnitude`).
  - **Validator C1 rewrite (load-time vs runtime split)**: load-time validator enforces *structural* rules only; runtime "exactly one fires per Transfer" lives in the AB.3.3 matview. New load-time rules:
    - **C1** (rewritten): "at most one *non-grouped* Variable-direction leg per template" — preserves the pre-AB.3 semantic for templates with zero XOR groups; the grouped Variables are excluded from this count.
    - **C1a** (new): members of `leg_rail_xor_groups[i]` ⊆ `leg_rails`.
    - **C1b** (new): members of `leg_rail_xor_groups[i]` MUST resolve to Variable-direction SingleLegRails.
    - **C1c** (new): no rail appears in two XOR groups within the same template.
    - **C1d** (new): each XOR group has ≥2 members. A 1-member group is degenerate (the rail always fires; not an XOR) — same defense-in-depth shape as Z.A's C5 empty-children check.
    Reason: keep the load-time validator's job tight (catch *structural* mistakes the operator can fix by editing yaml); push *firing-time* invariants (zero firings, overlap firings) to the matview where the deadline + cardinality semantic naturally lives. Mirrors AB.2.0's split (validator catches structural, matview catches runtime ETL bugs).
  - **Seed integration (XOR pick mechanism + 2 plants, not 1)**: per-firing deterministic pick via the existing seeded `rng` already wired through `seed.py`'s baseline + plant paths. Picker shape: keyed off `(template_name, xor_group_index, firing_counter)` so reproducibility holds across seeds AND across scope changes (re-running with a different `scope:` doesn't shift which variant fires per cycle). Emit ONE leg row per XOR group per firing — the picked variant; suppress the other members. **TWO plants, not one** (the cross-cutting contract requires ≥1 demo row per violation kind, and the AB.3.3 matview catches two cases):
    - **`XorVariantMissedFiringPlant`** (the plan's existing AB.3.5 plant) — suppress the pick for a single firing; matview row carries `firing_count=0`, `fired_rails=''`.
    - **`XorVariantOverlapPlant`** (new — added as AB.3.5b below) — emit TWO variant legs for a single firing; matview row carries `firing_count=2`, `fired_rails='<v1>,<v2>'`. Cheap addition (same plant primitive shape, different row count); the demo visual stays non-empty for both branches of the matview's `HAVING` filter.
  - [x] AB.3.1 `primitives.py`: `leg_rail_xor_groups: tuple[tuple[Identifier, ...], ...] = ()` on TransferTemplate. Done. New field placed between `leg_rails` and `description`, default `()` keeps every pre-AB.3 construction (positional + keyword) byte-equivalent. Docstring extended to declare the XOR semantics + the runtime-vs-validator split per AB.3.0 lock. Smoke-verified default + explicit-keyword construction; full L2 primitives + validate + derived + topology unit suite green (116 passed).
  - [x] AB.3.2 Loader + serializer + validator.   - [x] AB.3.4 `seed.py`: per-firing variant resolution (per AB.3.0 lock). Done. New helper `_xor_suppressed_members(template, *, firing_id)` computes the per-firing pick: for each `leg_rail_xor_groups[gi]`, picks one member via `zlib.crc32(f"{template_name}|{gi}|{firing_id}".encode())` and returns the set of non-picked members for caller-side suppression. **Firing key chosen = `parent_transfer_id`, not `counter.next()`**: parent_transfer_id is stable per chain invocation regardless of seed / scope (the chain parent's id is content-derived from the parent firing), so re-running with `scope: only_template` (or any subset) doesn't shift which variant fires for any given firing — satisfies the AB.3.0 "reproducibility holds across seeds + scope changes" lock more strictly than a global counter would. Picker takes no `rng` arg → independent of seeded RNG state. Integration: `_emit_chain_child_template_legs` consults the suppressed set before each `child_template.leg_rails` iteration and skips suppressed members; templates with empty `leg_rail_xor_groups` see no behavioral change (suppressed set empty). Scope confined to baseline chain-child template firings — other `template_name`-bearing paths (TransferTemplatePlant, AB.2 plants) stay untouched per the PLAN lock; cascade-emitted rows are XOR-invisible because they don't write `template_name`. New `tests/unit/test_l2_seed_xor.py` pins 8 picker-shape contracts (empty default, single + multi groups, determinism, distribution, RNG-independence, 2-member symmetry, template_name in key).
